# Introduction

An Extraction, Transformation and Load (ETL) software tool has been
developed to generate LION files, Geosupport System files and district
boundary polygon files from data extracted and transformed from the
Citywide Street Centerline (CSCL) geodatabase. This document contains
descriptions of methodologies utilized by the ETL tool to produce these
output files. This document has been delivered to the City of New York
Department of Information Technology and Telecommunications as part of
Phase II of the CSCL project.

An interactive routine has been developed to serve as a user interface
for launching the ETL tool. When successfully launched, the tool will
then execute as a batch process. The user interface is discussed in
detail in Section 1.1.

The ETL tool can run on any Windows machine on which ArcGIS and the CSCL
Editor application are installed, both servers and desktop computers.
Beyond those requirements, any desired limitations can be imposed by
manual coordination. Experience over time within the live CSCL working
environment with respect to performance of the ETL tool itself and its
impacts on other activities can help inform policy on which machine(s)
would best be utilized.

The versions of the CSCL database that are eligible to serve as the
input data to the ETL process are the DCP Working version and all of its
child versions, and only those versions. The user interface populates a
pull-down menu "on the fly" with a list of the eligible versions that
exist at that time, from which the user must select one.

During execution of the ETL tool, it is necessary for the input version
to be locked against updating. Careful consideration has been given
during the detailed programming design of the ETL tool to maximizing its
execution performance. That will help to minimize the period during
which the version being processed has to be locked.

It is anticipated that the Centerline Maintenance Group staff will run
the ETL tool periodically on a regular schedule (to be determined). From
time to time, the CMG staff may also run the tool on an ad hoc basis. It
will be possible for multiple users to run the tool simultaneously, as
long as they are generating non-overlapping sets of output files. That
would have to be ensured through manual coordination. Such simultaneous
executions could facilitate the expeditious production of output files
for a new update cycle.

The ETL tool only produces output files; it does not modify the CSCL
database in any way. It is designed to perform only a limited set of
validations of the CSCL data. In general, it does not redundantly
perform validations that the Maintenance System is designed to perform
"on the fly" or that separate batch validation programs will
perform[^1]. For the validations that the ETL tool does perform, it
writes messages into an output report for any errors encountered. Each
message states the type of problem and identifies the invalid data in
terms appropriate to the type of error, such as a SEGMENTID, a NODEID,
house number values etc. ESRI OBJECTIDs are included in the messages,
facilitating navigation in the CSCL Maintenance System to the feature or
table entry that has engendered the given problem.

Upon completing the creation of each output file (including sorting it
if necessary), the ETL tool reports that completion in the output report
by writing out a summary message for that file. The message identifies
the file (and borough, if it is borough-specific) and indicates the
file's record count as well as error counts itemized by type of error.
The ETL tool may run for a considerable duration, especially if a full
set of output files is being generated. If execution is interrupted at
any point, whether intentionally by the user or as the result of a
problem, the file completion messages will enable the user to re-launch
the tool without having to regenerate files that have already been
successfully created. Users will be able to monitor progress during
execution of the batch process by viewing the output report file via any
standard text processor such as Word at any time.

The output path (directory) that serves as the repository for all output
files, as well as the (possibly different) path for the output report,
are set in the configuration file, and can be modified therein if
desired.

Some of the output files are required to be sorted. The specific sort
requirements for those files are specified in the respective chapters of
this document. Requirements for the names of the ETL output files are
contained in Appendix E.

## User Interface

An interactive user interface is used to launch the ETL tool. It enables
the user to select the database version to be processed and the output
files desired for that run. It is possible to request the production of
various combinations of output files, ranging from a single file to the
full set. For files that are produced by borough, it is possible to
request a specific borough or boroughs. Thus, the user is able to
regenerate specific output files that have been found to contain errors
or omissions without having to regenerate the full set of files.

The user interface utilizes the CSCL Maintenance System's Login form.
When the user clicks the Login button on the screen, that form appears,
and the user is then prompted to log in and select a work order or
create a new one. A button has also been provided that links the user to
an interface for extracting LION Differences Files (LDFs). LDF
extraction is performed by a separate tool and is not discussed in this
document.

A pull-down menu for the user to select the database version to be
processed has been included at the top of the screen.

Below the database version pull-down menu there is a pair of "extract
option" check boxes. They are used to control what geodatabase is to be
processed as the input data. The two possible input geodatabases are the
SDE geodatabase used by the CSCL Maintenance System (defined in the
system's configuration file), and a local file geodatabase that must be
named **ETL Working GDB.gdb**. If the latter does not exist, but the
user wishes the ETL execution to access local data, the user can direct
the ETL tool to create a local file GDB by copying the SDE database. If
a local file GDB having the aforementioned name already exists, the user
can choose to use it or to delete it and create a new one by copying the
SDE database.

The appearance of the initial User Interface screen depends on whether a
local file GDB exists. If it does not, the initial screen appears as
shown in Figure 1.

![](media/image5.png){width="6.117361111111111in"
height="5.261111111111111in"}

[]{#_Ref248636866 .anchor}

Figure 1 -- Initial UI Screen if Local GDB Does Not Exist

Note the following:

- The message "No Local GDB Exists, Creating & Using a New One" is
  displayed.

- The "Use Existing Local GDB" check box is disabled

- The "Create & Use New Local GDB" check box contains a check mark.

If the user leaves the Create & Use New Local GDB check box checked, the
ETL tool will automatically create a new local file GDB with the
required name by copying the SDE database, and will use that as the
input data during this ETL run.

If the user unchecks the Create & Use New Local GDB check box, the User
Interface screen will appear as shown in Figure 2. Note that the message
has disappeared. In this case, the ETL tool will process the SDE GDB as
the input data. It will not create a local file GDB.

![[]{#_Ref254267936 .anchor}Figure 2 -- UI Screen After Unchecking
Box](media/image6.png){width="6.117361111111111in"
height="5.261111111111111in"}

If a local file geodatabase exists, the initial User Interface screen
appears as shown in Figure 3.

![](media/image7.png){width="6.179861111111111in"
height="5.261111111111111in"}

[]{#_Ref248638561 .anchor}

Figure 3 -- Initial UI Screen if Local GDB Exists

Note the following:

- A message indicating the date and time when the existing local file
  GDB was created is displayed.

- Both check boxes are enabled.

- The "Use Existing Local GDB" check box contains a check mark.

If the user leaves the "Use Existing Local GDB" check box checked, the
ETL tool will process the existing local file geodatabase as the input
data.

If the user checks the "Create & Use New Local GDB", the ETL tool will
uncheck the "Use Existing Local GDB" check box, it will replace the
message with the message "Creating & Using a New Local GDB", it will
delete the existing local file GDB and it will create a new one by
copying the SDE database.

The names of some of the output files include the update cycle
identifier as part of the name. (See Appendix E.) If any of those output
files are to be created, it is mandatory for the user to insert a value
into the text box near the upper left of the screen labeled "Enter Cycle
Name". That text box is enabled only when the user has selected at least
one of those files.

The user designates the output files to be extracted and launches the
batch ETL process as follows:

- The user can choose to generate any combination of the output files.
  When the user begins, the scrollable text box at the left side of the
  screen is initialized to contain a list of all of the possible ETL
  output files. Files that are extracted by borough are listed
  generically, followed by the names of the five boroughs.

- The text box at the right side of the screen contains a list of the
  output files that the user has designated for extraction so far. When
  the user begins, the right text box is initialized to empty.

There are three alternative means for the user to designate files for
extraction:

- The user can double-click a file (or a specific borough of a file that
  is extracted by borough) in the left-hand box, whereupon it will be
  moved from the left-hand box to the right-hand box (that is, it will
  be added to the right-hand box and removed from the left-hand box). If
  the user double-clicks the generic name of a file that is extracted by
  borough, all boroughs for that file that are not currently designated
  will be designated (moved to the right-hand box).

- The user can select a file (or a borough of a file) in the left-hand
  box with a single click, and then use the Add button to move the
  selected file to the right-hand box. Multiple files can be selected by
  holding down the CTRL key and single-clicking each desired file. Using
  the Add button will then cause all selected files to be moved to the
  right-hand box. Selecting and adding the generic name of a file that
  is extracted by borough will cause all not currently designated
  boroughs for that file to be moved to the right-hand box.

- The user can utilize the Add All button to designate all files for
  extraction, that is, to move all files from the left-hand box to the
  right-hand box.

There are three alternative means for the user to de-designate currently
designated files (files currently listed in the right-hand box):

- The user can double-click on a file in the right-hand box, whereupon
  it will be moved to the left-hand box. If the user double-clicks a
  generic name, all currently designated boroughs of that file will be
  moved to the left-hand box.

- The user can select a file (or borough) in the right-hand box with a
  single click, or select multiple files by holding down the CTL key
  while single-clicking the desired files, then use the Remove button to
  move the selected files to the left-hand box. If the user selects and
  removes a generic name, all currently designated boroughs of that file
  will be moved to the left-hand box.

- The user can utilize the Remove All button to de-designate (move from
  the right-hand box to the left-hand box) all currently designated
  files.

An efficient way to designate all but a few files for extraction is to
first use the Add All button to designate all files simultaneously, and
then individually de-designate the few specific files that are not
desired.

The user interface will enable the "Run ETL" button at the bottom of the
screen whenever the user has selected a database version and has
designated at least one output file. If the user utilizes the "Run ETL"
button, the user interface will submit a batch process to execute the
ETL tool and will terminate. The ETL tool, running as a batch process,
will produce the output files designated by the user in the order in
which they were listed in the "Files to Be Extracted" list box.

The "Close" button at the bottom of the screen can be used at any time
to exit the user interface without launching the batch ETL process.

Figure 4 depicts a sample screen after the user has designated some
output files. The "Run ETL" button is enabled. The user may now launch
the batch ETL process. Note that in this example, the user has chosen to
process an existing local file GDB.

![[]{#_Ref250991486 .anchor}Figure 4 -- UI Screen After Designation of
Output Files](media/image8.png){width="6.179861111111111in"
height="5.206944444444445in"}

## Summary of Output Files

The ETL tool is able to generate the following Geosupport-related files:

- LION, discussed in Chapter 2. The following formats will be produced:

  - A Geosupport version of LION (a separate file for each borough)

  - A BYTES of the BIG APPLE™ LION in ESRI file geodatabase format (a
    single file geodatabase for the entire city)

  - ~~A BYTES of the BIG APPLE™ LION in MapInfo MIF format (a single set
    of files for the entire city)~~

- Street Name Dictionary, discussed in Chapter 3

- Geosupport normalizing tables, discussed in Chapter 4:

  - Exception Table

  - Universal Word Table and Last Word Table

  - Enders Table

- Face Code File (a separate file for each borough), discussed in
  Chapter 5

- District equivalency files, discussed in Chapter 6:

  - ThinLION (a separate file for each borough)

  - ThinFire (a separate file for each borough)

- Special Address File (SAF), discussed in Chapter 7

- Election District-related files, discussed in Chapter 8:

  - Split ED Address table (SEDAT)

  - Special SEDAT

- Roadbed Pointer List (RPL), discussed in Chapter 9

- District boundary polygons for various types of operational,
  administrative and political districts in ESRI file geodatabase
  format, discussed in Chapter 10

Note that the ETL tool is not designed to generate LDF files. They can
be generated by a separate process that has been developed as part of
CSCL Phase III. The ETL tool's user interface contains a link to that
process.

## Field Identification Codes (FICs)

To ensure that references to fields in output files are unambiguous and
consistent within this document, a Field Identifier Code (FIC) has been
assigned to each field in each of the output files other than those for
the BYTES of the BIG APPLE™. The FICs appear in the first column of the
record layout tables provided for each output file.

The first portion of the FIC is an alphabetic string that identifies the
output file, or in the case of the SAF file, which has multiple record
types with differing layouts, it identifies the record type. No layouts
are provided in this document for files in which the entire record
consists of a single field. Therefore, those files have not been
assigned FIC's. Those files are the Exception table and the Enders
table.

The alphabetic file identifiers are listed in Table 1.

[]{#_Ref212975021 .anchor}Table 1 -- File Identifier Portion of Field
Identifier Code (FIC)

  ---------------------------------------------------------------
    **File   **File**                     **Record Type(s)**
     ID**                                 
  ---------- ---------------------------- -----------------------
      FC     Face Code File               

      L      Geosupport LION              

     RPL     RPL                          

     SAFA    SAF                          A, B, C, E, G, N, P and
                                          X

     SAFD    SAF                          D

     SAFI    SAF                          I

     SAFV    SAF                          O and V

     SAFS    SAF                          S

    SEDAT    SEDAT and Special SEDAT      

     SNDN    SND                          Non-S

      TF     ThinFire                     

      TL     ThinLION                     

      WT     Universal and Last Word      
             Tables                       
  ---------------------------------------------------------------

The digits that follow the alphabetic portion of the FIC identify the
specific field within the given file. For example, the FIC value 'L23'
identifies the 23rd field in file L (the LION File), which is the Left
Department of Sanitation Subsection (see Table 2). Filler fields are not
in general assigned FIC values.

## Field Formatting

All output fields labeled as "filler" in the layouts in this document
will be populated with blanks. All output fields populated from a CSCL
field whose value is null will be populated with blanks unless otherwise
noted.

The following abbreviations are used below to refer to field formats:

LJ = "left-justified"

RJ = "right-justified"

SF = "space-filled"

ZF = "zero-filled"

House number fields and census tract fields have special formatting
requirements, as follows:

- House number fields:

  - Unhyphenated house numbers will be stored in output house number
    fields RJSF.

  - Hyphenated house numbers will be stored RJSF. There will be three
    bytes after the hyphen, with the value after the hyphen stored RJZF
    within those three bytes. (Note the **ASSUMPTION**: hyphenated house
    numbers will never have more than three digits to the left of the
    hyphen. It would be impossible to store such a house number in a
    seven-byte house number field so that it is formatted with three
    bytes after the hyphen.)

  - If there is no house number, the value stored in the output house
    number field will consist of a single zero RJSF. That is, the value
    will consist of six spaces followed by a zero.

- "Standalone" census tract fields except tract label fields:

  - Tract fields (other than label fields) are a total of six bytes in
    length. They consist of two subfields: a "basic tract number"
    subfield of four bytes followed by a "tract suffix" subfield of two
    bytes. Symbolically, this format can be expressed as BBBBSS, where
    BBBB is the four-byte basic tract number field and SS is the
    two-byte tract suffix subfield.

  - The basic tract number value is stored in its subfield RJSF.

  - The suffix value is stored in its subfield RJZF, except that if
    there is no suffix, the suffix subfield will contain blanks.

  - Examples ('\*' represents a blank):

    - **107201** (basic number is 1072, suffix is 01)

    - **\*\*5604** (basic number is 56, suffix is 04)

    - **\*\*87\*\*** (basic number is 87, no suffix)

- In fields that contain a Borough Code and Census Tract concatenated
  (for example, field TT5, BoroCT2000, in the ThinTract ETL file), the
  value of the basic tract number will be stored RJSF in the four-byte
  basic tract subfield. If there is no suffix, the suffix subfield will
  be filled with blanks. For example, if the Borough Code = 4, the basic
  tract = 32, and there is no suffix, the field will be populated with
  the value **4\*\*32\*\*,** where '\*' represents a blank.

- Tract number label fields (for example, field TT1, Census Tract Label,
  in the ThinTract ETL file) are a total of seven bytes in length. They
  consist of up to three subfields: a basic tract number subfield of
  four bytes, followed by a one-byte subfield possibly containing a
  decimal point, followed by a tract suffix subfield of two bytes.
  Symbolically, the format can be expressed as BBBBDSS where BBBB is the
  four-byte basic field, D is the decimal point (if any) and SS is the
  two-byte suffix subfield.

  - The entire tract value will be stored LJSF within the seven-byte
    field.

  - If there is a suffix, a decimal point will be stored in the decimal
    point subfield, and the suffix will be stored RJZF within the suffix
    subfield.

  - If there is no suffix, blanks will be stored in the decimal point
    and suffix subfields.

  - Examples: ('\*' represents a blank):

    - **1072.01** (basic number is 1072, suffix is 01)

    - **56.04\*\*** (basic number is 56, suffix is 04)

    - **87\*\*\*\*\*** (basic number is 87, no suffix)

# LION

The ETL tool is designed to extract a Geosupport version of LION as well
as BYTES of the BIG APPLE™ versions of LION. The Geosupport LION is
extracted as a sequential file, as discussed in detail in Sections 2.1
through 2.6.7. The BYTES of the BIG APPLE™ LION is extracted in the
formats, ESRI file geodatabase format ~~and MapInfo (MIF) format~~, as
discussed in Sections 2.7 and 2.8, respectively.

The ETL tool produces a separate Geosupport LION output file for each of
the five boroughs. These files will be produced by generating the
following output records:

- One record for each segment in CSCL's linear feature classes
  (Centerline, Shoreline, Rail, Subway and NonStreetFeature), EXCEPT:

  - Centerline segments for private streets (RWJURISDICTION = '3') that
    do not exist physically (STATUS not = '2')

  - Subterranean rail and subway segments that do not serve as district
    boundaries (ROW_TYPE = 1 [or 8]{.mark}). (However, records for such
    segments will be written into the BYTES of the BIG APPLE™ versions
    of LION.)

  - [Centerline segments for Driveway (RW=8). (However, records for such
    segments will be written into the BYTES of the BIG APPLE™ versions
    of LION)]{.mark}

- One record for each "proto-segment" (coincident segment entry in the
  CSCL AltSegmentData table), discussed in detail in Section 2.6.

## Geosupport LION Output Record Layout

Table 2 contains a record layout of the Geosupport LION output file. The
penultimate column indicates formatting information for the given field.
A 'RJZF' in this column signifies right-justified with leading zeros.
The last column indicates for which types of features the given field is
populated. For output records generated from segments in feature classes
not specified in the last column, the ETL tool will populate the given
field with blanks.

**[(Note for Census Tract fields:]{.mark}**

**[CT Basic, RJSF]{.mark}**

**[CT Suf , 2 bytes RJZF if it has value; Blank if it is none
)]{.mark}**

Many of the Geosupport LION output fields are populated by directly
copying the contents of a corresponding source attribute field in a CSCL
linear feature class, with no re-formatting or other processing
required, other than to replace null values with blanks. Other output
fields are populated via translation or reformatting of the values in
corresponding source CSCL fields or require more elaborate processing.

Sections 2.2, 2.3, 2.4 and 2.5 describe the methodology for populating
fields in Geosupport LION output records generated from segments in the
feature class Centerline, Shoreline, Rail and Subway, and
NonStreetFeature, respectively. Section 2.6 describes the generation of
output records for proto-segments. For simplicity, the term LION is used
in these sections to refer to the Geosupport LION output file.

## Generating Records from Centerline Segments

Table 3 and the sections following it indicate how each field is
populated in LION output records generated from Centerline segments.

### Street Code and Face Code Items

**FIELDS**: L2 (Face Code), L5 (5-Digit Street Code (5SC)), L6 through
L9 (LGC1, LGC2, LGC3, LGC4), L10 (Board of Elections Preferred LGC), L74
through L78 (LGC5, LGC6, LGC7, LGC8, LGC9)

**ASSUMPTIONS**: The ETL tool assumes the following conditions to be
true with respect to the CSCL database, and does not perform validations
for them:

- Every feature in the Centerline feature class has at least one street
  name and corresponding street code in the StreetName table. Every
  feature in the Rail, Subway, Shoreline and NonStreetFeature feature
  classes has at least one feature name and corresponding street code in
  the FeatureName table.

- Every segment (of any linear feature class) has at least one
  Segment_LGC table entry and has at most nine.

- All of the Segment_LGC entries for a given SEGMENTID contain the same
  B5SC value.

- Precisely one of the Segment_LGC entries for a given SEGMENTID
  contains a 'Y' in the PREFERRED_LGC_FLAG. (The LGC in that entry is
  the "preferred LGC" for that segment, and the B7SC formed by
  concatenating the B5SC and the preferred LGC is the "preferred B7SC".)

- The FACECODE field is non-empty in the StreetName and FeatureName
  table entries for preferred B7SCs.

- Exactly one of the Segment_LGC entries for a given SEGMENTID contains
  a 'Y' in the BOE_PREFERRED_LGC_FLAG.

**METHODOLOGY**:

- The tool will examine all entries in the Segment_LGC table for the
  given SEGMENTID.

- The tool will populate the output 5SC field from the last five bytes
  of the B5SC field in any of the Segment_LGC entries for the given
  SEGMENTID.

- The tool will populate the output LGC fields as follows:

  - The tool will populate LGC1 with the preferred LGC.

  - If there are additional Segment_LGC entries for the given SEGMENTID,
    the tool will populate the output LGC2 through LGC9 fields in
    sequence from the LGCs in those additional Segment_LGC entries,
    until all Segment_LGC entries for the given SEGMENTID have been
    used.

  - The tool will populate any unused output LGC fields with blanks.

  - If Segment_LGC ever contains more than nine entries for a SEGMENTID,
    the ETL tool will populate the output record with the first nine LGC
    values encountered, and will insert a message into the output report
    stating that the Segment_LGC table contains more than nine entries
    for that SEGMENTID. (If and when that event should ever occur, it
    would be necessary for DCP to consider adding additional LGC fields
    to LION and expanding the length of the BOE Pointer field to two
    bytes.)

- If the given segment belongs to a non-Centerline feature, the tool
  will populate the output Board of Elections LGC Pointer field with the
  value '1'. If it belongs to a Centerline feature, the tool will
  populate the output Board of Elections LGC Pointer with an integer
  corresponding to the output LGC field that has been loaded from the
  Segment_LGC entry that contains a 'Y' in the BOE_PREFERRED_LGC_FLAG.
  For example, if the output LGC field that has been loaded from that
  Segment_LGC entry is LGC3, the tool will populate the output Board of
  Elections LGC Pointer with the value '3'.

- If the segment belongs to a Centerline feature:

  - The tool will populate the output Face Code field from the FACECODE
    field in the StreetName table entry (if found) for the principal
    street name corresponding to the preferred B7SC.

  - If the preferred B7SC is not found in StreetName, the tool will
    populate the output Face Code field from the FACECODE field in the
    FeatureName table entry (if any) for the principal feature name
    corresponding to the preferred B7SC.

  - If the preferred B7SC is not found in StreetName or in FeatureName,
    the tool will not write out an output record, and will issue an
    error message.

- If the segment belongs to a non-Centerline feature class, the tool
  will populate the output Face Code field from the FACECODE field in
  the FeatureName table entry for the principal feature name
  corresponding to the preferred B7SC.

### Node-Related Items

**FIELDS**: L12 (FROM-NODE), L16 (TO-NODE), L13 (FROM-X), L14 (FROM-Y),
L17 (TO-X), L18 (TO-Y), L11 (FROM-SECTIONAL-MAP), L15
(TO-SECTIONAL-MAP):

**METHODOLOGY**:

- From the segment's spatial data, the tool will determine which
  endpoint of the given segment is its "from" endpoint and which is its
  "to" endpoint, and will populate the FROM-X, FROM-Y, TO-X and TO-Y
  output fields accordingly, rounded to the nearest whole integer.

- For each endpoint of the segment, the tool will perform a spatial
  query against the Node feature class to obtain that endpoint's NODEID.
  The tool will populate the FROM-NODE and TO-NODE output fields
  accordingly. If there is no node at a segment endpoint the ETL tool
  will populate that output node field with blanks and will issue an
  error message in the output report file.

- For each endpoint of the segment, the tool will perform a spatial
  query against the SectionalMap polygon feature class to obtain that
  endpoint's Sectional Map identifier. The tool will populate the
  FROM-SECTIONAL-MAP and TO-SECTIONAL-MAP output fields accordingly.

### Atomic Polygon-Based Items

**FIELDS**: L19 (LEFT-2000-CENSUS-TRACT), L28 (RIGHT-2000-CENSUS-TRACT),
L20 (LEFT-DYNAMIC-BLOCK), L29 (RIGHT-DYNAMIC-BLOCK), L25
(LEFT-ASSEMBLY-DISTRICT), L26 (LEFT-ELECTION-DISTRICT), L34
(RIGHT-ASSEMBLY-DISTRICT), L35 (RIGHT-ELECTION-DISTRICT), L27
(LEFT-SCHOOL-DISTRICT), L36 (RIGHT-SCHOOL-DISTRICT), L72
(LEFT-2010-CENSUS-TRACT), L73 (RIGHT-2010-CENSUS-TRACT), [L80, L81, L82,
L83, L84, L85, L86, L87, L100, L101, L102, L103, L104, L105]{.mark}:

**METHODOLOGY**:

First, the ETL tool will determine the segment's left and right Atomic
Polygons (APs). Certain attributes of those APs will then be used to
populate the corresponding fields of the output LION record, as
indicated in Table 4. In addition, certain attributes of the left and
right APs will be used in determining how to populate output fields L41
(Segment Locational Status), L42 (Feature Type Code) and L46 (Borough
Boundary Indicator), as described in Sections 2.2.6, 2.2.7 and 2.2.8,
respectively. Therefore, the processing described in those sections must
be performed in conjunction with the processing described in this
section.

To determine the given segment's left and right APs, the ETL tool will
generate temporary left and right "offset points" positioned on both
sides of the segment, offset two feet perpendicularly from the segment's
midpoint. (Note: the same offset points will be used to populate the
left and right zip code output fields for non-Centerline segments -- see
Section 2.3.4.) For each offset point, the tool will perform a
point-in-polygon spatial query against the Atomic Polygon feature class
to determine the given segment's left and right APs.

- If one offset point is not contained within an AP (presumably because
  the segment lies along the city limits), the output fields for that
  side of the segment will be populated with blanks.

- If both offset points fail to match to APs, the ETL tool will report
  the segment as an error with an appropriate message.

> []{#_Ref222641742 .anchor}Table 4 -- Populating Atomic Polygon-Based
> Fields

  ------------------------------------------------------------------
  **FIC**   **Output Field**          **CSCL Source**
  --------- ------------------------- ------------------------------
  L19       Left 2000 Census Tract    CENSUSTRACT_2000 attribute of
                                      left AP

  L20       Left Dynamic Block        Last three bytes of ATOMICID
                                      attribute of left AP

  L25       Left Assembly District    ASSEMDIST attribute of left AP

  L26       Left Election District    ELECTDIST attribute of left AP

  L27       Left School District      SCHOOLDIST attribute of left
                                      AP

  L28       Right 2000 Census Tract   CENSUSTRACT_2000 attribute of
                                      right AP

  L29       Right Dynamic Block       Last three bytes of ATOMICID
                                      attribute of right AP

  L34       Right Assembly District   ASSEMDIST attribute of right
                                      AP

  L35       Right Election District   ELECTDIST attribute of right
                                      AP

  L36       Right School District     SCHOOLDIST attribute of right
                                      AP

  L72       Left 2010 Census Tract    CENSUSTRACT_2010 attribute of
                                      AP on left side of segment

  L73       Right 2010 Census Tract   CENSUSTRACT_2010 attribute of
                                      AP on right side of segment

  L80       [LEFT CENSUS BLOCK 2000   CENSUSBLOCK_2000 attribute of
            BASIC]{.mark}             AP on left side of segment

  L81       [LEFT CENSUS BLOCK 2000   CENSUSBLOCK_2000 suffix
            SUFFIX]{.mark}            attribute of AP on left side
                                      of segment

  L82       [RIGHT CENSUS BLOCK 2000  CENSUSBLOCK_2000 attribute of
            BASIC]{.mark}             AP on right side of segment

  L83       [RIGHT CENSUS BLOCK 2000  CENSUSBLOCK_2000 suffix
            SUFFIX]{.mark}            attribute of AP on right side
                                      of segment

  L84       [LEFT CENSUS BLOCK 2010   CENSUSBLOCK_2010 attribute of
            BASIC]{.mark}             AP on left side of segment

  L85       [LEFT CENSUS BLOCK 2010   CENSUSBLOCK_2010 suffix
            SUFFIX]{.mark}            attribute of AP on left side
                                      of segment

  L86       [RIGHT CENSUS BLOCK 2010  CENSUSBLOCK_2010 attribute of
            BASIC]{.mark}             AP on right side of segment

  L87       [RIGHT CENSUS BLOCK 2010  CENSUSBLOCK_2010 suffix
            SUFFIX]{.mark}            attribute of AP on right side
                                      of segment

  L100      [LEFT 2020 CENSUS         CENSUSTRACT_2020 attribute of
            TRACT]{.mark}             left AP

  L101      [RIGHT 2020 CENSUS        CENSUSTRACT_2020 attribute of
            TRACT]{.mark}             right AP

  L102      [LEFT CENSUS BLOCK 2020   CENSUSBLOCK_2020 attribute of
            BASIC]{.mark}             AP on left side of segment

  L103      [LEFT CENSUS BLOCK 2020   CENSUSBLOCK_2020 suffix
            SUFFIX]{.mark}            attribute of AP on left side
                                      of segment

  L104      [RIGHT CENSUS BLOCK 2020  CENSUSBLOCK_2020 attribute of
            BASIC]{.mark}             AP on right side of segment

  L105      [RIGHT CENSUS BLOCK 2020  CENSUSBLOCK_2020 suffix
            SUFFIX]{.mark}            attribute of AP on right side
                                      of segment
  ------------------------------------------------------------------

If output field L46 (Borough Boundary Indicator) is populated with a
non-blank value, that indicates that the given segment is a borough
boundary segment. In that case, L46 will contain one of the values 'L'
or 'R', indicating the side of the segment that is in a different
borough from the one that the segment itself belongs to. For borough
boundary segments, only those output fields listed in Table 4 that
pertain to the side of the street in the borough to which the segment
itself belongs will be populated. The fields for the side out of the
borough will be populated with blanks. For example, if L46 contains an
'L' ([Left side out of borough]{.mark}), the "right" fields will be
populated with values and the "left" fields will be populated with
blanks.

The ETL tool should determine and save the values of the fields listed
in Table 4 for the side that is out of the borough, for use in
generating an output record for the proto-segment that corresponds to
the given borough boundary segment, as discussed in Section 2.6 et seq.

### Split Election District Flag (Joe does not use this field anymore)

**FIELD**: L37 (Split Election District Flag)

**METHODOLOGY**:

The value that the ETL tool will populate into L37 will be based on the
existence (or lack) of SEDAT table entries that pertain to the given
Centerline segment, or SpecialSEDAT entries that pertain to SAF data
that in turn pertains to the Centerline segment; and if there do exist
any such entries, it will be based on which side(s) of the segment those
entries pertain to.

Determining what SEDAT and SpecialSEDAT entries pertain to a Centerline
segment, if any, must take into consideration the possibility that the
segment might have a proto-segment, that is, a coincident segment entry
in the AltSegmentData table that has the same SEGMENTID as that of the
Centerline segment. (Proto-segments are discussed in detail in Section
2.6 et seq.)

If a Centerline segment does have a proto-segment, both the Centerline
segment and the proto-segment are either borough boundary street
segments or combined on-off ramps. Ramps will never have associated
address information. Therefore, if there is a SEDAT or SpecialSEDAT
entry that contains the SEGMENTID of a Centerline segment that has a
proto-segment, they must both be borough boundary street segments. In
that case, the SEDAT or SpecialSEDAT entry pertains to the entity that
belongs to the same borough as that entry. The ETL tool will determine
this by comparing the borough code in the first byte of the LIONKEY of
the SEDAT or SpecialSEDAT entry with field L1 (Borough) in the output
record being generated for the given Centerline segment and
proto-segment.

Since it is necessary, for the purpose of populating field L37, to
compare LION keys when an output LION record is being generated from a
Centerline segment that has a proto-segment, or from a proto-segment
whose implicit feature class (defined in Section 2.6) is Centerline, the
processing to populate the components of the output record's LION Key
(fields L1, L2 and L3) must be performed before L37 can be populated.

Once all SEDAT and SpecialSEDAT entries that pertain to the Centerline
segment (if any) are ascertained, the rules for populating L37 for that
Centerline segment are as follows:

- If there are no entries in the CSCL SEDAT table or SpecialSEDAT table
  that pertain to the Centerline segment, the tool will set L37 to
  blank.

- If there are only entries pertaining to the Centerline segment in
  which the field SIDE contains the value '1', the tool will set L37 to
  'L'.

- If there are only entries pertaining to the Centerline segment in
  which SIDE contains the value '2', the tool will set L37 to 'R'.

- If there are entries pertaining to the Centerline segment in which
  SIDE contains a '1' as well as entries in which it contains a '2', the
  tool will set L37 to 'B'.

When creating the output LION record for a proto-segment whose implicit
feature class is Centerline, the above rules apply but are based on the
set of SEDAT and SpecialSEDAT entries that pertain to the proto-segment
rather than to the Centerline segment.

### Traffic Direction

**FIELD**: L40 (Traffic Direction)

**METHODOLOGY**:

L40 will be populated by translating the Centerline attribute TRAFDIR as
shown in Table 5.

[]{#_Ref222641792 .anchor}Table 5 - Translation Rules for L40 (Traffic
Direction)

  --------------------------------------
   **TRAFDIR Value**   **Output Value**
  ------------------- ------------------
         blank              blank

       FT (with)              W

      TF(against)             A

   NV(non-vehicular)          P

      TW(two-way)             T
  --------------------------------------

### Segment Locational Status

**FIELD**: L41 (Segment Locational Status)

**METHODOLOGY**:

The processing described in Section 2.2.3 must be performed prior to
performing the processing for field L41.

For segments of all linear feature types, the ETL tool will populate L41
based on certain assignment rules listed below. These rules involve the
attributes ATOMICID, BOROUGH and ~~CENSUSTRACT_2000~~
[CENSUSTRACT_2020]{.mark} of the segment's left and right Atomic
Polygons, which have been determined as described in Section 2.2.3.

The assignment rules for field L41 are as follows:

- If, during the processing described in Section 2.2.3, one of the
  segment's left and right offset points was found not to be contained
  in any AP, then the segment lies along New York City's boundary with
  one of its neighboring jurisdictions (Nassau County, Westchester
  County or New Jersey). The ETL tool will populate L41 with the value
  '9'.

- If the ATOMICIDs of the left and right AP's are identical, the ETL
  tool will populate L41 with one of the values 'H' or 'I', as follows.
  It will assign the value 'H' if there is at least one other segment of
  any kind connected to [each]{.underline} of the given segment's two
  endpoints. If the segment has at least one endpoint to which no other
  segments are connected, it will assign the value 'I'.

- If the left and right AP's belong to two different boroughs, the ETL
  tool will populate L41 with the borough code that differs from that of
  the segment itself. For example, if the segment contains a Borough
  Code of '3' (= Brooklyn), and the Borough Code of the left AP is '3',
  and the Borough Code of the right AP is '4' (= Queens), then the
  segment is a Brooklyn segment lying along the border with Queens; the
  ETL tool will populate L41 with the value '4'.

- If the left and right AP's belong to the same borough, but the
  ~~CENSUSTRACT_2000~~ [CENSUSTRACT2020]{.mark} attributes of the left
  and right AP's differ, the ETL tool will populate L41 with the value
  'X'.

- If none of the above conditions are satisfied, the ETL tool will
  populate L41 with a blank.

Centerline segments (and those of all other linear feature classes) have
an attribute field called SEGLOCSTATUS. The ETL tool will validate this
attribute for consistency with the above rules. If SEGLOCSTATUS is
inconsistent with the rules, the ETL tool will populate output field L41
with the value specified in the rules rather than the value in
SEGLOCSTATUS, but will report the discrepancy as an error. (The CSCL
Maintenance System has not been designed to perform this validation on
the fly, since it is believed that doing so would cause performance
problems for the interactive maintenance routines.)

**FIELD**: L42 (Feature Type Code)

**METHODOLOGY**:

The possible values for field L42 for Centerline segments, and the rules
for assigning each such value, are listed in Table 6. Add new Feature
Type Code ="C". if Street Status =2 (constructed) and "RWJURISDICTION" =
5 (CCO), then street type = C.

   **Value**   **Definition**              **Assignment Rule**
  ------------ --------------------------- ----------------------------------
     Blank     Public street, bridge or    Assign if segment does not satisfy
               tunnel that exists          the criteria listed in this table
               physically (or its generic  for Feature Type Codes 5, 6, 9, A
               geometry), other than       or W
               Feature Type Code W         

       5       Paper street that is not    Assign if STATUS = 3.
               also a boundary             

       6       Private street that exists  Assign if RWJURISDICTION = 3
               physically                  (private) and STATUS = 2
                                           (constructed)

       9       Paper street that coincides Assign if STATUS = 9.
               with a non-physical         
               boundary                    

       A       Alley                       Assign if RW_TYPE = 10

       W       Path, non-vehicular,        Assign if TRAFDIR = NV
               addressable                 (non-vehicular) and at least one
                                           house number field is non-zero.

   [F]{.mark}  [Ferry Route]{.mark}        [Assign if RW_type=14]{.mark}

  (Feature Type Code)

### Borough Boundary Indicator

**FIELD**: L46 (Borough Boundary Indicator)

**METHODOLOGY**:

The ETL tool will perform the processing described in this section in
conjunction with the processing described in Section 2.2.3.

The ETL tool will populate L46 by comparing the borough attributes of
the segment's left and right Atomic Polygons (if any) to the borough
attribute of the segment itself, as follows:

- If there is no AP on one side of the given segment, the segment lies
  along the City limit. The tool will populate the Borough Boundary
  Indicator with the value ('L' or 'R') that identifies the side of the
  segment on which there is no AP. (Note: If there is no AP on either
  side of the segment, that condition will be identified and reported as
  an error during the processing for AP-related output fields described
  in Section 2.2.3.)

- If there are APs on both sides of the segment, the tool will validate
  that at least one of the AP boroughs is the same as that of the given
  segment. If neither AP borough matches the segment's borough, that
  will be reported as an error.

- If the segment's borough matches both AP boroughs, the segment is not
  a borough boundary segment. The tool will populate L46 with a blank.

If the segment's borough matches only one of the AP boroughs, the tool
will populate L46 with the value ('L' or 'R') that identifies the side
of the segment whose AP is in the borough that differs from that of the
segment.

### Twisted Parity Flag

**FIELD**: L47 (Twisted Parity Flag)

**METHODOLOGY**:

The ETL tool will populate L47 by translating the Centerline attribute
TWISTED_PARITY_FLAG as specified in Table 7.

[]{#_Ref222642044 .anchor}Table 7 -- Translation Rules for L47 (Twisted
Parity Flag)

  -------------------------------------
    **Source Field     **Output Field
       Value**            Value**
  ------------------ ------------------
          Y                  T

          N                blank
  -------------------------------------

### Special Address Flag

**FIELD**: L48 (Special Address Flag)

**METHODOLOGY**:

The value that will be populated into L48 depends on the types of SAF
data that pertain to the segment. Determining what SAF data, if any,
pertain to a segment in a linear feature class must take into
consideration the possibility that the segment might have a
proto-segment, that is, a coincident segment entry in the AltSegmentData
table that has the same SEGMENTID as that of the geometry-based segment.
(Proto-segments are discussed in detail in Section 2.6 et seq.)

If the geometry-based segment does have a proto-segment, SAF data
identified to the given SEGMENTID could pertain to either the
geometry-based segment or the proto-segment. Which one it pertains to is
determined as follows:

- If the proto-segment is of the [borough boundary]{.underline} type
  (ALT_SEGDATA_TYPE = B in the AltSegmentData entry for the
  proto-segment), the SAF datum pertains to whichever entity, the
  geometry-based segment or the proto-segment, has the same borough
  value as the SAF datum.

- If the proto-segment is of the [combined on-off ramp]{.underline} type
  (ALT_SEGDATA_TYPE = R):

  - It will not have any appurtenant SAF type A, B, C, D, E, F, O, P, S
    or V data, since these are all address-related and ramps will never
    have addresses.

  - If the SAF datum is stored in CommonPlace (SAFTYPE = G, N or X), it
    will be treated as pertaining to the geometry-based segment.

- If the proto-segment is of the [boundary continuity]{.underline} type
  (ALT_SEGDATA_TYPE = C), then the SAF datum pertains to the
  geometry-based segment. Boundary continuity proto-segments are
  non-physical non-street features and will never have SAF data of any
  kind.

Once all the SAF data that pertain to the segment (if any) are
determined, the rules for populating L48 for that segment are as
follows:

- If there are no SAF data of any type that pertain to the given
  segment, populate L48 with a blank.

- If there is at least one type S datum pertaining to the given segment,
  populate L48 with the value 'S', regardless of what other SAF type
  data are associated with the segment, if any. A type S datum is a
  feature in the AddressPoint feature class for which the
  SPECIAL_CONDITION attribute contains an 'S'.

- If there are no type S data pertaining to the given segment, but there
  is at least one type N datum, populate L48 with the value 'N'. A type
  N datum is a feature in the CommonPlace feature class for which the
  SAFTYPE attribute contains an 'N'.

- If there are no type S or N data pertaining to the given segment, but
  there is at least one type G datum, populate L48 with the value 'G'. A
  type G datum is a feature in the CommonPlace feature class for which
  the SAFTYPE attribute contains a 'G'.

- If there are no type S, N or G data for the given segment, but there
  is at least one SAF datum of any other type, populate L48 with the
  first SAFTYPE value encountered. The possibilities are type V in the
  AddressPoint feature class, type X in the CommonPlace feature class,
  and types A, B, C, D, E, F, O and P in the AltSegmentData table.

### Curve-Related Fields

**FIELD**: L49 (Curve Flag), L50 (Center of Curvature X-Coordinate), L51
(Center of Curvature Y-Coordinate)

**METHODOLOGY**:

Curved segments are modeled in the CSCL database as polylines containing
one or more or "shape points" between the segment's endpoints. The
Centerline feature class has an attribute called CURVE, which contains
one of the values 'I', 'L' or 'R' if the Centerline segment represents a
curved real-world feature, and contains the value 'S' otherwise.

There are two types of such "logically curved" Centerline segments.
"Regular" curves are arcs of circles; "irregular" curves are all other
curves. For regularly curved segments, the CURVE attribute contains one
of the values 'L' or 'R'. For irregular curves, CURVE contains the value
'I'.

For output records originating from Centerline segments, L49 will be
populated with the value in CURVE if it is not equal to 'S', or with a
blank if CURVE contains 'S'.

The fields L50 and L51 will be populated with non-blank values only for
regular curved segments, that is, for output LION records in which L49
has been populated with one of the values 'L' or 'R'. In all other
output records, L50 and L51 will be populated with blanks.

Since three points determine a circle, for regular curved segments, the
spatial coordinates of the center of curvature can be computed by using
the spatial coordinates of the "from" node, the "to" node and any one of
the intermediate shape points. It appears advisable for the ETL tool to
use a shape point that is positioned as midway between the two endpoints
of the segment as possible. If there is an odd number of shape points,
the central one will be used. If there is an even number, either one of
the two central shape points could be used. For consistency in the odd
case, the central shape point closest to the "from" node will be used.

The computation of the spatial coordinates of the center of the circle
is straightforward. The general equation of a circle is:

(x -- x~0~)^2^ + (y -- y~0~) ^2^ = r^2^

where (x~0~, y~0~) is the center of the circle and r is the radius.
Since the "from" node, the "to" node and the selected shape point all
lie on the desired circle, the coordinate pairs of all three of those
points satisfy the above equation. That is enough information to solve
for the unknowns x~0~ and y~0,~ which are the required Center of
Curvature Spatial Coordinates. The results must be rounded to the
nearest foot and then populated into fields L50 and L51.

### Level Codes

**FIELDS:** L53 ("From" Level) and L54 ("To" Level)

**METHODOLOGY:**

In LION, level codes are either a single letter of the alphabet or an
asterisk. An asterisk signifies that the feature is non-physical and
therefore is "level-less".

In the CSCL database, level codes are two-digit numeric values ranging
from 01 to 26, along with the value 99, which is assigned to the level
codes of non-physical features and also to physical features in the
NonStreetFeature feature class. The values from 01 to 26 correspond in
LION to the respective letters of the alphabet. The value 99 corresponds
to the LION value of asterisk.

Except for Shoreline segments (see Section 2.3), the ETL tool will
populate L53 and L54 by converting the corresponding CSCL numeric level
codes into letters of the alphabet and asterisks as follows:

**[CSCL Level Code]{.underline}** **[Output LION Level
Code]{.underline}**

01 A

02 B

03 C

**.....** **.....**

etc. etc.

**.....** **.....**

24 X

25 Y

26 Z

99 \* (asterisk)

### [2.2.13 NYPD Service Area]{.mark} 

### [FIELDS: L97 ("Left NYPD Service Area) and L98 (Right NYPD Service Area)]{.mark}

**[METHODOLOGY:]{.mark}**

[First, the ETL tool will determine the segment's left and right NYPD
Service Area.]{.mark}

[To determine the given segment's left and right NYPD Service Area, the
ETL tool will generate temporary left and right "offset points"
positioned on both sides of the segment, offset two feet perpendicularly
from the segment's midpoint. For each offset point, the tool will
perform a point-in-polygon spatial query against the NYPD BEAT feature
class to determine the given segment's left and right NYPD Service Area.
The attribute will be the first byte of the attribute of "POST" of the
found NYPD BEAT polygon when field of GEO_TYPE="HP".]{.mark}

- [If one offset point is not contained within a NYPD BEAT polygon
  (presumably because the segment lies along the city limits), the
  output fields for that side of the segment will be populated with
  blanks.]{.mark}

- [If both offset points fail to match to NYPD BEAT polygon, the ETL
  tool will report the segment as an error with an appropriate
  message.]{.mark}

### Borough

**FIELD**: L1 (Borough)

**METHODOLOGY**:

Unlike Centerline, the Shoreline feature class does not have an
attribute for the Borough Code.

The ETL tool will access the Segment_LGC table by SEGMENTID. The tool
will populate L1 with the first byte of the B5SC field in the given
Segment_LGC table entry. (Note: Segment_LGC can contain more than one
entry for a given SEGMENTID value. However, all such entries will
contain the same B5SC value. Therefore, it is immaterial from which
table entry the ETL tool obtains the Borough Code.)

For performance efficiency, the Borough Code value should be obtained at
the same time as the ETL tool is accessing the Segment_LGC table to
populate fields L2 and L5 through L9.

### Segment Locational Status

**FIELD**: L41 (Segment Locational Status)

**METHODOLOGY**:

L41 is populated via the same methodology for Shoreline as for
Centerline, including the consistency validation described in Section
2.2.6.

### Curve Flag

**FIELD**: L49 (Curve Flag)

**METHODOLOGY**:

Unlike Centerline, the other CSCL linear feature classes do not have a
CURVE attribute.

For output records originating from segments in the Shoreline and other
non-Centerline feature classes, L49 will be populated based on whether
the segment has any shape points. If so, L49 will be populated with the
value 'I'; otherwise, it will be populated with a blank.

### Zip Codes

**FIELDS**: L24 (Left Zip Code) and L33 (Right Zip Code)

**METHODOLOGY**:

Unlike the Centerline feature class, the Shoreline and other linear
feature classes do not contain zip code attributes. However, the CSCL
database does have a ZipCode polygon feature class. For output records
generated from segments in the Shoreline and other non-Centerline linear
feature classes, the fields L24 and L33 will be populated via spatial
processing, as follows.

A point-in-polygon routine will be used to spatially match the left and
right offset points computed as part of the determination of left and
right Atomic Polygons (see Section 2.2.3) against the ZipCode polygons.
Upon a match, the ZIP_CODE attribute of the matching polygon will be
populated into the respective zip code output field, either L24 or L33.
If there is no match for one or both of the offset points, the
respective output zip code field will be populated with blanks.
Non-matches will not be treated as errors, since the zip code geography
does not necessarily cover the entire territory of the city,
particularly water areas.

### Sequence Number

**FIELD**: L3 (Sequence Number)

**METHODOLOGY**:

Unlike the Centerline, Rail, Subway and Shoreline feature classes, which
have a SEGMENT_SEQNUM attribute field that will be maintained "on the
fly" (that is, assigned at the time that the given segment is created),
the NonStreetFeature feature class does not have such an attribute.

For output LION records generated from the NonStreetFeature feature
class, or generated from AltSegmentData coincident segment entries whose
implicit feature class is NonStreetFeature, the ETL tool will assign
Sequence Number values based on the combination of Borough and Face
Code, but not based on relative spatial positions of the segments. That
is, the Sequence Number assigned to each output record will be unique
within the set of LION records containing the given Borough and Face
Code values. Unlike the Sequence Numbers assigned to the segments of the
other linear feature types, those that the ETL tool assigns to
NonStreetFeature types of segments will bear no relationship to the
spatial positioning of the given segment relative to other segments for
the given Borough and Face Code.

[Note]{.underline}: It is expected that, at some future time, sequence
numbers will be converted to be based on B5SC instead of on Borough and
Face Code. If and when that is done, the ETL tool's routine to generate
sequence numbers for NonStreetFeature segments will have to be modified
accordingly.

### Feature Type Code

**FIELD**: L42 (Feature Type Code)

**METHODOLOGY**:

The possible values for field L42 and the rules for assigning them are
listed in Table 11.

[]{#_Ref222642403 .anchor}Table 11 -- Assignment Rules for L42 (Feature
Type Code)

  ----------------------------------------------------------------
   **Value**  **Definition**   **Assignment Rule**
  ----------- ---------------- -----------------------------------
       3      Non-physical     Assign if LINETYPE = 3
              census block     
              boundary         

       4      Other non-street Assign if LINETYPE = 7
              feature          

       7      Non-physical     Assign if LINETYPE = 1, 2 or 6
              boundary other   
              than census      

       8      Physical         Assign if LINETYPE = 4 or 5
              boundary such as 
              cemetery wall    
  ----------------------------------------------------------------

Currently, all non-street features are either physical or are district
boundaries. Therefore, if a segment satisfies the assignment rule for
Feature Type Code '4', it is likely either that the segment has been
assigned an erroneous LINETYPE value, or it has been stored in an
inappropriate feature class. The ETL tool will write out an output LION
record, but will also write a warning message in the output report.

It is not anticipated that any features will be added in the future to
the NonStreetFeature feature class that are neither physical features
nor district boundaries. If that should ever occur, it would be
advisable to consider modifying the ETL tool so that it no longer issues
the warning message for Feature Type Code '4'.

### Level Codes

**FIELDS:** L53 ("From" Level Code) and L54 ("To" Level Code)

**NOTE:** The ETL tool will populate L53 and L54 with asterisks for all
NonStreetFeature (NSF) segments, including those that are physical
(specifically, those with the LINETYPE value '5'). No level code
attribute fields are defined in the NSF feature class. Therefore, it is
not currently possible to extract level codes for physical NSF features.
If that should ever be deemed to be required, a data model enhancement
would have to be made to add level code fields to the NSF feature class,
those fields would have to be appropriately populated and maintained,
and the ETL tool would have to be modified accordingly.

## Coincident Segments

Except for multi-decked physical features (such as a multi-level bridge
or highway, or an elevated highway or rail line running along the bed of
a surface street), coincident segments are modeled differently in the
CSCL database than in LION.

- In LION, all coincident segments are represented by coincident
  geometry.

- In the CSCL database, as in LION, the segments of multi-decked
  physical features are represented by coincident geometry. Each of the
  segments has a distinct SEGMENTID.

- In LION, in addition to multi-decked physical features, there are
  three other types of coincident segments: borough boundary segments,
  combined "on" and "off" highway ramp segments, and boundary continuity
  segments. Such coincident segments exist in sets in which all the
  segments have the same SEGMENTID. (Typically, such sets consist of two
  segments, but there can be more than two.) In the CSCL database, these
  coincident sets are modeled as follows:

  - Only one segment of the set is represented in a linear feature
    class. It is referred to in this document as the "geometry-modeled
    segment".

  - The other segment or segments of the set are represented in the CSCL
    database only by entries in the AltSegmentData table, so that they
    have no geometry representation of their own in the database. In
    that sense, in CSCL, they are "latent" segments. When the ETL tool
    extracts these into LION records, they will be transformed into
    actual segments (with geometry). The AltSegmentData entries are
    referred to as "proto-segments". Tacitly, proto-segments have the
    same geometry as the geometry-modeled segments with which they
    coincide, except that they may have the reverse topological
    (from--to) direction.

The ETL tool will generate an output LION record for a coincident
segment entry in AltSegmentData only if a geometry-modeled segment
exists with the same SEGMENTID. Otherwise, the ETL tool cannot generate
a LION record, since the geometry to do so is lacking. However, it is
expected that there will never be any such "orphaned" proto-segments,
since the CSCL Maintenance System has been designed to prevent them from
being created.

To aid in optimizing performance, the ETL tool is designed so that each
time it generates an output record for a geometry-modeled segment, it
immediately determines whether there is a corresponding proto-segment or
proto-segments, and if there are any, it immediately generates an output
record for each such proto-segment. This leverages the processing
performed to populate fields in the output record for the geometry-based
segment without later having either to repeat those algorithms or to
retrieve the output record for the geometry-based segment.

Table 12 lists the fields in AltSegmentData.

[]{#_Ref212361222 .anchor}Table 12 -- AltSegmentData Table Layout

  ------------------------------------------------------------------
  **Field**                         **Comments**
  --------------------------------- --------------------------------
  OBJECTID                          

  SEGMENTID                         

  LIONKEY                           

  SOS_INDICATOR                     For proto-segments, this field
                                    serves as a continuous parity
                                    indicator.

  SAFTYPE                           

  L_LOW_HN                          

  L_HIGH_HN                         

  R_LOW_HN                          

  R_HIGH_HN                         

  LOW_HN_SUFFIX                     

  HIGH_HN_SUFFIX                    

  LGC1                              

  LGC2                              

  LGC3                              

  LGC4                              

  LGC5                              

  LGC6                              

  LGC7                              

  LGC8                              

  LGC9                              

  BOROUGH                           

  ZIPCODE                           

  CREATED_BY                        

  CREATED_DATE                      

  MODIFIED_BY                       

  MODIFIED_DATE                     

  ALT_SEGMENT_SEQNUM                

  BOE_PREFERRED_LGC_FLAG            

  B5SC                              

  FEATURE_TYPE                      See Table 14 for domain

  FROM_TO_INDICATOR                 See Table 16 for domain

  ALT_SEGDATA_TYPE                  See Table 13 for domain

  TWISTED_PARITY_FLAG               Populated for proto-segments
                                    only, not SAF entries
  ------------------------------------------------------------------

AltSegmentData contains two types of entries: SAF entries and coincident
segment entries. The field ALT_SEGDATA_TYPE indicates the type, as shown
in Table 13.

Output Geosupport LION records will not be generated for SAF entries in
AltSegmentData (entries with ALT_SEGDATA_TYPE = S), but they will be
utilized to determine how to populate field L48 (Special Address Flag)
in output LION records. They will also be utilized when extracting ESRI
LION, ~~MapInfo LION and~~ SAF files.

[]{#_Ref212361587 .anchor}

Table 13 -- AltSegmentData Table: ALT_SEGDATA_TYPE Field

  -----------------------------------------
   **Value**  **Meaning**
  ----------- -----------------------------
       B      Coincident borough boundary
              segment

       C      Coincident boundary
              continuity segment

       R      Coincident on-off ramp

       S      SAF entry
  -----------------------------------------

To support the extraction of LION records for proto-segments, it has
been necessary to store a Feature Type code in AltSegmentData coincident
segment entries, since the feature type of a proto-segment might be
different from that of the geometry-modeled segment with which it
coincides. The field FEATURE_TYPE serves that purpose, as shown in Table
14.

[]{#_Ref222642586 .anchor}Table 14 -- AltSegmentData Table: FEATURE_TYPE
Field

  -----------------------------------------
   **Value**  **Meaning**
  ----------- -----------------------------
     null     None of the below (i.e.,
              public street that is not
              either paper or an
              addressable non-vehicular
              path)

       1      Rail

       2      Shoreline

       3      Non-physical census block
              boundary

       4      Other non-street feature

       5      Paper street other than
              FEATURE_TYPE_CODE 9

       6      Private street that exists
              physically

       7      Non-physical district
              boundary other than census

       8      Physical boundary, such as
              cemetery wall

       9      Paper street that also serves
              as a boundary of any kind
              including a census boundary

       A      Alley segment

       W      Addressable non-vehicular
              path
  -----------------------------------------

The term "implicit feature class" is used in this document to refer to
the CSCL feature class that a proto-segment would belong to if it were
geometry-modeled. The implicit feature class of a proto-segment affects
how the ETL tool will generate its LION output record.

Note that, except for coincident on-off ramps, the implicit feature
class of a proto-segment is not necessarily the same as the feature
class of the geometry-modeled segment with which the proto-segment is
coincident. Examples:

- Boundary continuity segments spatially coincide with, and have the
  same SEGMENTID as, their associated geometry-modeled segments.
  However, a boundary continuity segment is a non-physical non-street
  feature, so its implicit feature class is NonStreetFeature. The
  geometry-modeled segment with which it coincides is always a street
  segment, represented in the Centerline feature class.

- Along part of the Manhattan-Brooklyn border, CSCL will contain a
  Manhattan borough boundary proto-segment whose implicit feature class
  is NonStreetFeature, coincident with a Brooklyn geometry-modeled
  segment in the Shoreline feature class.

The implicit feature class of a proto-segment is determined from its
FEATURE_TYPE as specified in Table 15.

[]{#_Ref222642741 .anchor}Table 15 -- Implicit Feature Class Definitions

  -----------------------------------------------
  **Implicit Feature      **AltSegmentData
  Class**                 FEATURE_TYPE Values**
  ----------------------- -----------------------
  Centerline              Null, 5, 6, 9, A, W

  Rail or Subway          1

  Shoreline               2

  NonStreetFeature        3, 4, 7, 8
  -----------------------------------------------

Note that Rail and Subway have been grouped into a single implicit
feature class, since no distinction between these types of features is
made in LION.

The field FROM_TO_INDICATOR indicates whether the proto-segment has the
same or reverse topological direction as that of the geometry-based
segment with which it is coincident. That affects the manner in which
the ETL tool will populate numerous fields in the output LION records
generated from proto-segments.

[]{#_Ref222642623 .anchor}Table 16 -- AltSegmentData Table:
FROM_TO_INDICATOR Field

  -----------------------------------------
   **Value**  **Meaning**
  ----------- -----------------------------
     null     Proto-segment has the same
              topological direction as that
              of the coincident
              geometry-based segment

       R      Proto-segment has the reverse
              topological direction from
              that of the coincident
              geometry-based segment
  -----------------------------------------

### Determining the Coincident Segment Count

The output field L57 (Coincident Segment Count) must be populated with
the appropriate value in every LION output record. If there are no
segments coincident with the one being written out, the ETL tool will
populate its L57 field with the value '1'.

The Centerline feature class has an attribute field called
COINCIDENT_SEG_COUNT. It contains an integer greater than '1' for
Centerline segments that have coincident segments, whether they are
physical multi-decked segments, proto-segments or both. The value in
COINCIDENT_SEG_COUNT indicates the total number of coincident segments
and proto-segments, including the given Centerline segment.

When processing Centerline segments, to optimize efficiency, the ETL
tool will only attempt to determine if AltSegmentData has any
proto-segments coincident with the given Centerline segment when the
COINCIDENT_SEG_COUNT of the Centerline segment is greater than 1. That
determination will be facilitated utilizing the relationship class
CenterlinesHaveAltSegmentData, with SEGMENTID serving as the access key.

If a Centerline segment does have proto-segments, the ETL tool will
generate their output LION records immediately after generating the one
for the Centerline segment. This will enable the tool to capture certain
values from the output record generated from the Centerline segment
without having to repeat all the processing to determine those values
for the proto-segments. Among those values is L57, the Coincident
Segment Count. In other words, if the geometry-based segment to which a
proto-segment pertains is a Centerline segment, the latter's Coincident
Segment Count value will be used to populate the proto-segment's L57
field.

The CSCL linear feature classes other than Centerline do not contain a
COINCIDENT_SEG_COUNT attribute, nor do they have a relationship class
linking the feature class to AltSegmentData. Therefore, to populate L57
for an output LION record generated from a segment in one of those
feature classes (as well as for that segment's proto-segments, if any),
it will be necessary to determine if the segment has any coincident
segments, and if so, how many. The ETL tool will do so as follows:

1.  First, if the given non-Centerline segment belongs to the Rail,
    Subway or Shoreline feature class (but not to NonStreetFeature), the
    ETL tool must determine if it is part of a set of coincident
    multi-decked physical segments, and if so, it must determine how
    many segments there are in the set. It will do so spatially
    utilizing ESRI's feature intersection tools. (It cannot do so by
    utilizing the SEGMENTID, since coincident multi-decked physical
    segments have unique SEGMENTIDs).

2.  Whether the given segment is or is not part of a set of multi-decked
    physical segments, the ETL tool will search AltSegmentData by
    SEGMENTID to determine if there are any proto-segments coincident
    with it (there can be any number of such proto-segments).).

3.  The ETL tool will populate L57 with the total number of coincident
    segments as determined above, counting the segment being written
    out, all multi-decked physical segments coincident with it (if any),
    and all proto-segments if there are any.

4.  To avoid having to repeat the above processing to determine the
    coincident segment count for the other coincident segments, the ETL
    tool will be designed to generate the output records for all
    segments in a coincident set consecutively, both the multi-decked
    ones if any, and the proto-segments, if any.

**RECOMMENDATION:** An improvement in execution performance of the ETL
tool, and a simplification of its logic flow, might be achieved by
adding a COINCIDENT_SEGMENT_COUNT attribute to the linear feature
classes other than Centerline and maintaining it "on the fly" during
database updating, just as it will be maintained for Centerline
segments. That would obviate the need for the ETL tool, when processing
every non-Centerline segment, to find and count the number of coincident
segments. (The Maintenance System could potentially also make use of
this attribute to facilitate ensuring that coincident segments are kept
spatially synchronized with each other. For example, if an elevated Rail
segment is split, it would only be necessary to determine whether there
is a coincident street segment that also has to be split if the Rail
segment's COINCIDENT_SEGMENT_COUNT is greater than one.)
