### Face Code

A proto-segment always belongs to a different feature from that of its
associated geometry-modeled segment, and its implicit feature class may
even be different from the feature class of the geometry-modeled
segment. Therefore, the values of feature-specific fields for the
proto-segment cannot be obtained from the geometry-modeled segment. Most
of these output fields will be obtained from fields in the
AltSegmentData entry for the given proto-segment, as indicated in Table
17. Field L2 (Face Code) will be obtained as follows:

- The preferred B7SC for the proto-segment will be constructed by
  concatenating the AltSegmentData fields B5SC and LGC1.

- If the implicit feature class of the proto-segment is Centerline, the
  StreetName table will be accessed by the preferred B7SC with the
  PRINCIPAL_FLAG = 'Y'. If an entry matching those criteria is found and
  it contains a Face Code value, it will be populated into L2.

- If the implicit feature class of the proto-segment is not Centerline,
  the FeatureName table will be accessed as described above instead of
  the StreetName table.

- If the ETL tool is unable to obtain a Face Code value via the above
  procedure, it will not write an output LION record for the given
  proto-segment, and it will issue an appropriate error message. (LION
  records must not be written out without a valid Face Code value, since
  it is part of the LION Key, which serves as the primary key.)

### Fields Affected by Topological Direction

When generating a LION output record from a proto-segment, the ETL tool
examines the FROM_TO_INDICATOR field in the AltSegmentData entry to
enable the output record to be generated with the proper topological
direction.

The following discussion applies to combined on-off ramp proto-segments
and boundary continuity proto-segments. The case of borough boundary
proto-segments must be handled differently, and is discussed at the
bottom of this section.

[Proto-Segments Other Than Borough Boundaries]{.underline}

If the FROM_TO_INDICATOR does not contain the value 'R', then the ETL
tool will populate all of the output fields for the proto-segment that
are discussed in this section by copying the values that are in the
corresponding fields in the output record generated from the
geometry-based segment.

If the FROM_TO_INDICATOR does contain 'R', that signifies that the
topological direction of the proto-segment is opposite to that of the
geometry-based segment. In that case, the manner in which output fields
affected by topological direction should be populated is as follows:

- The values that the ETL tool will populate into all corresponding
  pairs of "from" and "to" fields in the LION segment generated from the
  proto-segment will be interchanged from the values in the LION segment
  generated from the geometry-based segment. Specifically, the ETL tool
  will interchange the following pairs:

  - L11 and L15 (Sectional Map numbers)

  - L12 and L16 (NODEIDs)

  - L13 and L17 (X Coordinates)

  - L14 and L18 Y Coordinates)

  - L53 and L54 (Level Codes) -- see discussion in Section 2.6.6

- The values that the ETL tool will populate into all corresponding
  pairs of "left" and "right" fields in the LION segment generated from
  the proto-segment will be interchanged from those in the LION segment
  generated from the geometry-based segment. Specifically, the ETL tool
  will interchange the following pairs:

  - L19 and L28 (2000 Census Tracts)

  - L20 and L29 (Dynamic Blocks)

  - L21 and L30 (Low House Numbers)

  - L22 and L31 (High House Numbers)

  - L23 and L32 (Department of Sanitation Subsections)(NO??? could not
    find the corresponding data layer in CSCL)

  - L24 and L33 (Zip Codes)

  - L25 and L34 (Assembly Districts)

  - L26 and L35 (Election Districts)

  - L27 and L36 (School Districts)

  - L64 and L65 (BLOCKFACEIDs)

  - L72 and L73 (2010 Census Tracts)

> Etcs...

- The values that the ETL tool will populate into certain other fields
  must be modified from the values that are in those fields for the
  geometry-based segment, as follows:

  - L39 (Sanitation District Boundary Indicator): If the value of this
    field for the geometry-based segment is either 'L' or 'R', the ETL
    tool will populate this field for the proto-segment with the
    opposite value. If the geometry-based value is other than 'L' or
    'R', it will be populated into the proto-segment unchanged.

  - L40 (Traffic Direction) - see discussion in Section 2.6.5.

  - L46 (Borough Boundary Indicator): If the value of this field for the
    geometry-based segment is either 'L' or 'R', the ETL tool will
    populate this field for the proto-segment with the opposite value.
    If the geometry-based value is other than 'L' or 'R', it will be
    populated into the proto-segment unchanged.

  - L49 (Curve Flag): If the value of this field for the geometry-based
    segment is either 'L' or 'R', the ETL tool will populate this field
    for the proto-segment with the opposite value. If the geometry-based
    value is other than 'L' or 'R', it will be populated into the
    proto-segment unchanged.

[Borough Boundary Proto-Segments]{.underline}

The ETL tool populates the "from" and "to" output fields in the output
record generated from a borough boundary proto-segment in the same
manner as described above for non-borough boundary proto-segments.
However, borough boundary proto-segments require special handling with
respect to populating their "left" and "right" output fields.

In the output record generated from the geometry-modeled segment, these
fields contain non-blank values only for the side of the segment that is
in that segment's borough. Therefore, that record does not contain
values for the side that is in the proto-segment's borough. However,
when that record was generated, the ETL tool determined the values for
the side in the proto-segment's borough (with the exception of the
zipcode -- see below), and saved them for use in generating the output
record for the proto-segment (see the discussion at the bottom of
Section 2.2.3).

In the output record generated from the (borough boundary)
proto-segment, the ETL tool populates the side-related output fields
only for the side that is in the borough to which the proto-segment
belongs. If the FROM_TO_INDICATOR does not contain an 'R', that is the
side opposite that for which the geometry-modeled segment's side-related
fields are populated. If the FROM_TO_INDICATOR does contain an 'R', it
is the same side as that for which the geometry-modeled segment's
side-related fields are populated.

In either case, the ETL tool will populate the side-related fields for
the appropriate side using the values determined and saved for this
purpose when the geometry-modeled segment was processed, as described in
Section 2.2.3, except for the zipcode field, which will be populated
from the ZIPCODE field in the proto-segment's AltSegmentData entry. The
tool will populate the side-related fields for the opposite side with
blanks.

### Traffic Direction

The manner in which the ETL tool populates field L40 (Traffic Direction)
in the output record generated from a proto-segment depends on the
proto-segment's topological direction relative to that of the
geometry-based segment, on its feature type and on its coincident
segment type.

The proto-segment represents a physical street, bridge or tunnel if the
AltSegmentData field FEATURE_TYPE = null (non-paper street, bridge or
tunnel), 6 (physical private street), A (alley) or W (pedestrian street
or path).

Field L40 (Traffic Direction) will be populated in the output record for
the proto-segment as follows:

- If the proto-segment does not represent a physical street, bridge or
  tunnel (as defined above), L40 will be populated with a blank.

- If the proto-segment represents a physical street, bridge or tunnel
  and is a borough boundary segment (ALT_SEGDATA_TYPE = 'B' or
  ['R'):]{.mark}

  - If the value in L40 for the geometry-based segment is either of the
    one-way values, 'A' and 'W', then the value to be populated into L40
    for the proto-segment depends on the value of its FROM_TO_INDICATOR,
    as follows:

    - If the FROM_TO_INDICATOR does not contain the value 'R', the value
      populated into L40 for the proto-segment will be the same value as
      that of the geometry-based segment.

    - If the FROM_TO_INDICATOR does contain an 'R', the value populated
      into L40 for the proto-segment will be opposite to that of the
      geometry-based segment. That is, if the geometry-based value is
      'A', the proto-segment will be populated with a 'W', and vice
      versa.

  - If the geometry-based value is other than 'A' or 'W', that value
    will be populated into L40 for the proto-segment unchanged.

- ~~If the proto-segment represents a physical street, bridge or tunnel
  and is a combined on-off ramp (ALT_SEGDATA_TYPE = 'R') :~~

  - ~~If the value in L40 for the geometry-based segment is either of
    the one-way values, 'A' and 'W', then the value to be populated into
    L40 for the proto-segment depends on the value of its
    FROM_TO_INDICATOR, as follows:~~

    - ~~If the FROM_TO_INDICATOR does not contain the value 'R', the
      value populated into L40 for the proto-segment will be the
      opposite value to that of the geometry-based segment (since the
      on-ramp and off-ramp have opposite one-way traffic directions).
      That is, if the geometry-based value is 'A', the proto-segment
      will be populated with a 'W', and vice versa.~~

    - ~~If the FROM_TO_INDICATOR does contain an 'R', the value
      populated into L40 for the proto-segment will be the same value as
      that of the geometry-based segment (since the on-ramp's and
      off-ramp's opposite traffic directions are "cancelled out" by
      their reverse topological directions).~~

  - ~~If the geometry-based value is other than 'A' or 'W', that value
    will be populated into L40 for the proto-segment unchanged.~~

### Level Codes

The manner in which the ETL tool populates fields L53 and L54 (Level
Codes) in the output record generated from the proto-segment depends on
the proto-segment's topological direction as well as on its feature
type, as follows:

- If the proto-segment is not a physical feature (i.e., if FEATURE_TYPE
  = 3, 4, 5, 7 or 9), L53 and L54 will be populated with asterisks.

- If the proto-segment is a physical feature but FEATURE_TYPE is not 2
  (Shoreline) or 8 (a physical feature in the implicit feature class
  NonStreetFeature):

  - If the FROM_TO_INDICATOR in the AltSegmentData entry for the
    proto-segment contains the value 'R', the ETL tool will populate L53
    and L54 in the output record for the proto-segment by interchanging
    the values in those fields for the geometry-based segment.

  - If the FROM_TO_INDICATOR in the AltSegmentData entry for the
    proto-segment contains a value other than 'R', the ETL tool will
    populate L53 and L54 in the output record for the proto-segment by
    copying the geometry-based values without interchanging them.

<!-- -->

- Proto-segments are expected never to belong to the implicit feature
  class of Shoreline (FEATURE_TYPE = 2).

<!-- -->

- If the proto-segment is a physical feature in the implicit feature
  class NonStreetFeature (FEATURE_TYPE = 8), the ETL tool will populate
  L53 and L54 with asterisks.

### Segment Locational Status

If the value of field L41 (Segment Locational Status) for the
geometry-modeled segment is one of the integers from '1' to '5', that
signifies that the geometry-modeled segment is a borough boundary
segment. In that case, the following should be true:

- The borough boundary geometry-modeled segment should have a coincident
  proto-segment.

<!-- -->

- The AltSegmentData entry for the proto-segment should be classified as
  a borough boundary coincident segment entry. That is, the
  ALT_SEGDATA_TYPE field in that entry should contain the value 'B'.

- The AltSegmentData entry for the proto-segment should belong to the
  other borough than the one to which the geometry-modeled segment
  belongs. Specifically, the BOROUGH field in the AltSegmentData entry
  should equal the value of field L41 in the output record generated
  from the geometry-modeled segment.

The ETL tool validates for the above conditions. If there are no
proto-segments coincident with a borough boundary geometry-based
segment, the ETL tool will report that as a data discrepancy. If there
is a coincident proto-segment, but either of the last two conditions
listed above is not satisfied, that will be reported as a data
discrepancy, but the ETL tool will continue processing that
AltSegmentData entry for output.

Although it is hypothetically possible for a geometry-modeled borough
boundary segment to have more than one coincident proto-segment, it is
expected that, in practice, there will never be more than one. (There
would appear to be no need to have a coincident boundary continuity
segment along a borough boundary, and it appears highly unlikely that a
combined on-off ramp would ever be constructed in the future lying
directly along a borough boundary.)

The ETL tool will populate field L41 in the output record for a
proto-segment as follows:

- If the proto-segment is coincident with a borough boundary
  geometry-modeled segment, the ETL tool will populate the value of
  field L41 with the value that is in field L1 (Borough Code) in the
  output record generated for the geometry-based segment.

- If the proto-segment is coincident with a non-borough boundary
  geometry-modeled segment (one whose output record contains a value
  other than '1' to '5' in field L41), the ETL tool will populate the
  value of field L41 in the output record generated from the
  proto-segment with the value that is in field L41 in the output record
  generated from the geometry-based segment.

## ESRI LION

In addition to the Geosupport LION extract, the ETL tool can also
extract LION in the format for DCP's BYTES of the BIG APPLE™ data
products: ESRI file geodatabase format ~~and MapInfo (MIF) format~~.
This section and its sub-sections discuss the ESRI LION. Section 2.8 and
its sub-sections discuss the MapInfo LION.

Many of the fields in the BYTES LION files are identical to those in the
Geosupport LION. The ETL tool developer may deem it advisable, if it is
technically feasible, to write out records into the ESRI LION ~~and the
MapInfo LION~~ in tandem with writing records into the Geosupport LION
file. That would avoid unnecessarily repeating the processing required
to populate many of the fields. (However, that would not be possible if
the user requested the production of a BYTES LION but not the Geosupport
LION, unless in those instances the ETL tool were designed to generate a
Geosupport LION "under the covers" solely for the purpose of leveraging
its algorithms. This document assumes that approach.) References of the
form L\<integer\> below are FICs of Geosupport LION fields.

Records will not be written into the Geosupport LION for subterranean
rail and subway segments that do not serve as district boundaries, as
noted in the "bulleted" items at the beginning of Section 2. However,
such records will be written into the BYTES versions. To facilitate
that, it may be advantageous for the developer to design the ETL tool to
create "virtual" (not written into the output file) Geosupport LION
records for such segments, from which the BYTES records can then be
derived.

The ESRI LION will be extracted as a single file geodatabase for the
entire city. Appendix A contains a geodatabase schema for the ESRI LION
that has been provided by DCP. The ESRI LION consists of two object
classes: a linear feature class called LION and a table of alternative
street names (aliases) called Altnames. The field JOIN_ID relates the
two components.

Certain segments that are represented in the Geosupport LION by a single
record are represented in the ESRI LION ~~(as well as the MapInfo
LION)~~ by multiple records that have identical geometry but differ in
some of their attribute data. The ETL tool will generate these records
as required. There are two cases of this: continuous parity segments and
segments that have Special Address File (SAF) data (Plus boro boundary
segments).

[The Geodatabase Lion data model can be found at folder of
"Templates\\lion.gdb".]{.mark}

### Segment Replication for Continuous Parity Condition

A continuous parity segment is a street segment in which odd and even
addresses exist in reality on the same side of the street. In the
Geosupport LION, a continuous parity segment is modeled as a single
record, with the fields nominally labeled as the left low and high house
number fields used to store the address range of one of the parities and
the nominally labeled right house number fields used to store the
address range of the other parity. Continuous parity segments are
identified by the value 'L' or 'R' in the Continuous Parity Indicator
field, which indicates on which side of the segment both address ranges
actually exist in reality. (This is also how a continuous parity segment
is modeled in the CSCL database, both in the Centerline feature class
and with respect to proto-segment entries in the AltSegmentData table,
except that instead of the LION values 'L' and 'R', in the CSCL database
the values '1' and '2' are used, respectively. For continuous parity
proto-segments, the SOSINDICATOR field serves as the Continuous Parity
Indicator.)

In the ESRI LION, a continuous parity segment is modeled as two
distinct, spatially coincident features, one containing the odd range
and the other containing the even range, with both ranges stored (in
their respective records) in the house number fields for the side of the
street on which the addresses actually exist in reality, that is, the
side identified by the Continuous Parity Indicator. The two features are
identical in all other attribute data aside from the house numbers.

For example, segment 34262 is the segment of Central Park West between
West 61 Street and West 62 Street in Manhattan. The odd address range 13
to 21 and the even range 14 to 22 are allocated to this segment. In
reality, both odd and even addresses exist on the left (west) side of
the segment, and there are no addresses on the right (east) side, since
that side adjoins Central Park.

- In the single Geosupport LION record for segment 34262, the odd range,
  13 to 21 is stored in the left house number fields; the even range, 14
  to 22 is stored in the right house number fields; and the Continuous
  Parity Indicator contains an 'L'.

- In the ESRI LION, two features must be generated in the LION linear
  feature class representing segment 34262. One feature contains 13 and
  21 in the left house number fields and zeros in the right house number
  fields. The other feature contains 14 and 22 in the left house number
  fields and zeros in the right house number fields. Aside from the
  house number fields, both records are identical in every respect, that
  is, in both geometry and attribute data (including LION keys,
  SEGMENTID etc.).

During ESRI LION extraction, when the ETL tool is processing a CSCL
Centerline segment whose CONTINUOUS_PARITY_FLAG contains '1' or '2', or
a proto-segment that contains house number values and whose SOSINDICATOR
contains '1' or '2', the ETL tool will generate two output features. In
one feature, the tool will store the odd range in the house number
fields for the side of the segment indicated by the
CONTINUOUS_PARITY_FLAG or SOSINDICATOR, and will populate zeros into the
house number fields for the other side. In the other feature, the tool
will store the even range in the house number fields for the side
indicated by the flag, and zeros in the house number fields for the
other side. The geometry and all other attribute values will be
identical for the two features. The ETL tool will set the output
SegCount field value accordingly (reflecting the existence of both
features), as discussed in detail in Section 2.7.3.

### Segment Replication for SAF Data

The ETL tool creates coincident output records for segments that have
SAF data. The methodology for determining what SAF data, if any, are
associated with a segment or proto-segment is described in detail at the
end of Section 2.2.10.

In addition to the "regular" output ESRI LION record generated from a
CSCL segment or proto-segment, one additional output record (or two, if
the SAF datum has a continuous parity condition) is generated for
[each]{.underline} SAF datum associated with that segment or
proto-segment. Such "SAF replicants" will have identical geometry to
that of the "regular" output record, and most of their attribute items
will also be identical to those of the "regular" output record. However,
certain of their attributes are obtained from the SAF data instead of
from the CSCL segment or proto-segment, as described below.

SAF replicants will be generated for the following CSCL SAF data:

- All SAF entries in the AltSegmentData table (entries in which the
  SAFTYPE field contains a value)

- All points in the CommonPlace feature class for which the SAFTYPE
  attribute contains a value

- All points in the AddressPoint feature class for which the
  SPECIAL_CONDITION attribute = 'S' or 'V'

In generating SAF replicants, care must be taken to interpret the
SOSINDICATOR field correctly, as follows:

- In SAF type A, B, C, E and P AltSegmentData entries, the SOSINDICATOR
  serves as a continuous parity indicator, and the output record will be
  generated in accordance with the methodology described in Section
  2.7.1. For example, if a type A SAF entry in AltSegmentData contains
  '1' in the SOSINDICATOR, and the entry contains address ranges in the
  left and right house number fields, two output records will be
  generated for that entry, with both address ranges stored in the left
  house number fields in the respective output records. Those records
  are in addition to the "regular" output record or records generated
  for the underlying street segment.

- In SAF type D, F and O AltSegmentData entries, the SOSINDICATOR serves
  as a side of street indicator, not a continuous parity indicator. Type
  D and O entries contain only a single address range, which pertains to
  one side of the underlying street segment (the side indicated by the
  SOSINDICATOR). One output record will be generated (in addition to the
  "regular" output record or records.) In that output record,
  side-related output fields, such as house numbers and zip codes, will
  be populated only for the side identified by the SOSINDICATOR value.
  For example, in a record generated for a type D SAF entry in which
  SOSINDICATOR = '1', the zip code value from the AltSegmentData ZIPCODE
  field will be stored in the RZip field in the output ESRI LION
  feature, and the LZip output field will be populated with null values.

- SAF type G, N and X features are stored in the CommonPlace feature
  class. They represent Non-Addressable Placenames (NAPs). Since these
  names do not have associated house numbers, the continuous parity
  concept is not applicable to them. NAPs pertain to a specific side of
  the underlying street segment. The SOSINDICATOR attribute serves as
  the side of street indicator. One output record will be generated (in
  addition to the "regular" record or records).

- SAF type S and V features are stored in the AddressPoint feature
  class. They are identified by SPECIAL_CONDITION = 'S' or 'V'. These
  are individual addresses or address ranges for individual buildings,
  and pertain to a specific side of the street. The SOSINDICATOR serves
  as a side of street indicator. One output record will be generated (in
  addition to the "regular" record or records).

> Output ESRI LION features generated for SAF data are populated as
> follows. All data items not obtained from the CSCL SAF data as
> specified below are obtained from attribute fields and corresponding
> street names of the underlying segment, including in particular the
> output fields Street, StreetCode (a B5SC field), LGC1 through LGC4 and
> the BOE_LGC field (= BOE LGC Pointer).

- The output field SpecAddr will contain the SAF type, populated as
  follows:

  - If the SAF replicant is being generated from a common place SAF
    feature, or from an AltSegmentData SAF entry other than SAFTYPE =
    'F', SpecAddr will be populated from the SAFTYPE field of that
    common place or entry.

  - If the SAF replicant is being generated from an AltSegmentData SAF
    entry with SAFTYPE = F, SpecAddr will be populated with the value
    'D'.

  - If the SAF replicant is being generated from an address point SAF
    feature, SpecAddr will be populated from its SPECIAL_CONDITION
    attribute (that is, with the value 'S' or 'V').

  - Note that the SpecAddr output field may not contain the same value
    in SAF replicants as it does in the output record generated directly
    from the geometry-modeled CSCL segment. The latter is populated with
    the same value that is (or would be) populated into field L48 of the
    Geosupport LION record, as described in Section 2.2.10.

- For SAF replicants generated from type A SAF data:

  - The house number items (LLo_Hyphen, LHi_Hyphen, RLo_Hyphen,
    RHi_Hyphen, FromLeft, ToLeft, FromRight and ToRight) will be
    populated from the corresponding fields in the AltSegmentData entry
    (rather than from the Centerline segment).

  - The output field SAF Streetname will be copied from the output field
    Street.

  - The output field SAF Streetcode (a B5SC field) will be copied from
    the output field StreetCode.

- For SAF replicants generated from type B, C, D, E, F, O and P SAF
  data:

  - The output fields for house numbers and the SAF Streetcode (a B5SC
    field) will be populated from the corresponding fields in the
    AltSegmentData SAF entry, rather than from the Centerline segment's
    attribute data.

  - The output field SAF Streetname will be populated with the principal
    name of the preferred SAF B7SC, obtained from the LOOKUP_KEY field
    in the CSCL StreetName table entry that is flagged as principal for
    the SAF preferred B7SC value. The SAF preferred B7SC value for this
    lookup will be formed by concatenating the values in the fields B5SC
    and LGC1 in the AltSegmentData SAF entry.

  - For type D and F records, the zip code output field for the side of
    the segment indicated by the SOSINDICATOR will be populated from the
    AltSegmentData ZIPCODE field.

- For SAF replicants generated from SAF type G, N and X data:

  - The SAF Streetcode output field will be populated from the first six
    bytes (the B5SC) of the B7SC attribute field of the given
    CommonPlace feature.

  - The SAF Streetname will be populated with the name obtained from the
    LOOKUP_KEY field in the FeatureName table entry that is flagged as
    principal for the aforementioned B7SC value.

  - All house number fields will be populated with blanks.

- For SAF replicants generated from SAF type S or V data:

  - The house number and zip code output fields for the side of the
    segment indicated by the SOSINDICATOR will be populated from the
    corresponding AddressPoint attributes. See the discussion of house
    number fields in Section 2.7.3 for further details on how to
    populate the output house number fields for type S and V replicants.

  - For type S replicants, the SAF StreetCode output field will be
    populated from the first six bytes of the B7SC_ACTUAL AddressPoint
    attribute. For type V replicants, the SAF StreetCode output field
    will be populated from the first six bytes of the B7SC_VANITY
    AddressPoint attribute.

  - The SAF Streetcode output field will be populated with the name
    obtained from the LOOKUP_KEY field in the StreetName table entry
    that is flagged as principal for the given B7SC value (that is, for
    the B7SC_ACTUAL for type S replicants, and the B7SC_VANITY for type
    V replicants).

### Methodologies for Populating Output Fields

Fields in the output ESRI LION that are "empty" (devoid of meaningful
contents) are populated with blanks, zeros or null values, depending on
the field. Appendix C contains a DCP-provided table that indicates, for
both the ESRI LION and the MapInfo LION, how "empty" fields should be
populated.

Aside from the special treatment of continuous parity and SAF data and
the treatment of "empty" fields discussed above, almost all of the
attribute fields in the ESRI LION feature class will be populated with
the same values that are in the corresponding fields in the Geosupport
LION file. Methodologies for populating fields that are not entirely
straightforward are as follows:

- The output field SpecAddr will be populated with a blank in all output
  records other than SAF replicants. In SAF replicants, it will be
  populated with the SAF type as described in Section 2.7.2.

- The output fields [SAF Streetname]{.underline} and [SAF
  Streetcode]{.underline} are two fields that exist only in the Bytes
  LION files, not in the Geosupport LION. In output records generated
  directly from geometry-modeled segments and in continuous parity
  replicants, the ETL program will populate these fields with blanks. In
  SAF replicants, they will be populated as specified in Section 2.7.2.

- The output field [SegCount]{.underline} will reflect all coincident
  records, regardless of the source of their generation. Records
  generated from proto-segments (coincident segment entries in
  AltSegmentData), continuous parity replicants, SAF replicants, and
  records generated from physically coincident features that are
  geometry-modeled in the CSCL database, will all be accounted for in
  the SegCount value. Note that Bytes LION files can have many more
  coincident segments than Geosupport LION, because of the segment
  replication for continuous parity conditions and for SAF data. In
  particular, the number of actual coincident segments in Bytes LION can
  exceed 9. That is expected never to occur in Geosupport LION. However,
  the SegCount field in Bytes LION, having been defined based on the
  Coincident Segment Counter field (field L57) in the Geosupport LION,
  is a one-byte string, and therefore cannot accommodate a value greater
  than 9. When there are more than 9 coincident segments in Bytes LION,
  the ETL program will populate SegCount with the value '9' in those
  output records, and will issue a warning message that will state the
  true segment count. **It is recommended** that DCP consider enhancing
  the length of the SegCount field in the Bytes LION layout to two
  bytes. If and when that is done, the ETL program should be modified to
  remove the warning and to populate SegCount with the true value when
  the number of coincident segments exceeds 9.

- The output field [Street]{.underline} will be populated from the
  LOOKUP_KEY field in the StreetName or FeatureName table entry for the
  principal name of the Preferred B7SC associated with the segment (or
  the underlying segment, in the case of an SAF record). The Preferred
  B7SC is the concatenation of the fields L1 (Borough), L5 (5-Digit
  Street Code) and L6 (LGC1) in the corresponding Geosupport LION
  record.

- The output field [TrafSrc]{.underline} is defined as a three-byte
  string. The CSCL source item for this field is the Centerline
  attribute TRAFDIR_VER_FLAG, which is defined as a one-byte string, the
  domain of which consists of the three values 'F', 'P' and 'T'. The ETL
  tool will populate TrafSrc with the values 'FLD', 'DCP' and 'DOT',
  respectively.

- The ESRI LION contains two sets of [house number fields]{.underline}:

<!-- -->

- One set consists of the fields [LLo_Hyphen, LHi_Hyphen, RLo_Hyphen and
  RHi_Hyphen]{.underline}. With the exception of certain types of
  segments as discussed below, these fields will be populated directly
  from the CSCL house numbers with no reformatting. In this format,
  Queens-style hyphenated house numbers are stored with an explicit
  hyphen character and with three digits following the hyphen.

- The other set consists of the fields [FromLeft, ToLeft, FromRight and
  ToRight]{.underline}. With the exception of certain types of segments
  as discussed below, these fields will be populated as follows.
  Queens-style hyphenated house numbers are stored in the following
  "normalized" format: The explicit hyphen is deleted. The digits to the
  left of the (deleted) hyphen are retained unmodified. The digits to
  the right of the (deleted) hyphen are formatted into three bytes,
  right-justified and zero-filled. For example, 45-03 would be stored in
  these fields as 45003; 45-12 would be stored as 45012; and 45-102
  would be stored as 45102. If the house numbers are not Queens-style
  hyphenated house numbers, these fields will be populated with the same
  values that are in the fields LLo_Hyphen, LHi_Hyphen, RLo_Hyphen and
  RHi_Hyphen.

- In output records for SAF type S and V replicants, the output house
  number fields will be populated as follows.

  - If the HYPHEN_TYPE attribute in the address point contains one of
    the values 'N' or 'Q', the address point contains a single house
    number, which is stored in the address point's HOUSE_NUMBER field.
    Form this single house number value into the output address range by
    populating it into all four output house number fields, "low" and
    "high" and "from" and "to", for the appropriate side of the segment.
    If HYPHEN_TYPE = 'N', the house number is unhyphenated and must be
    populated into all four fields unmodified. If HYPHEN_TYPE = 'Q', it
    is hyphenated. In that case, when populating the "from" and "to"
    fields, delete the hyphen character and concatenate the digits to
    the left and right of the hyphen as usual.

  - If HYPHEN_TYPE = 'R', the address point contains a range of
    unhyphenated house numbers, which is stored in the HOUSE_NUMBER
    field in the form of a pair of numbers separated by a dash. The dash
    is NOT a hyphen in this case; it is a range separation character.
    (Note: the dash may or may not be bracketed by blanks. For example,
    the range 345 to 349 might be expressed as '345--349' or as '345 --
    349'.) In this case, populate the "low" and "from" output house
    number fields for the appropriate side of the segment with the value
    to the left of the dash, and populate the corresponding "high" and
    "to" output house number fields with the value to the right of the
    dash.

  - If HYPHEN_TYPE = 'X', the address point contains a range of
    hyphenated house numbers. In this case, the (hyphenated) low house
    number of the range is stored in the HOUSE_NUMBER field and the
    (hyphenated) high house number of the range is stored in the
    HOUSE_NUMBER_RANGE field. Populate the "low" and "from" output house
    number fields for the appropriate side of the segment with the
    HOUSE_NUMBER value. Populate the corresponding "high" and "to"
    output house number fields with the HOUSE_NUMBER_RANGE value. When
    populating the "from" and "to" fields, delete the hyphen character
    and concatenate the digits to the left and right of the hyphen as
    usual.

- In output records for certain types of segments, including their
  continuous parity and SAF replicants, all house number fields
  ([LLo_Hyphen, LHi_Hyphen, RLo_Hyphen,]{.underline} [RHi_Hyphen,
  FromLeft, ToLeft, FromRight and ToRight)]{.underline}
  [will]{.underline} [be populated with zeros, regardless of the values
  in the]{.underline} [CSCL]{.underline} [source]{.underline}
  [data.]{.underline} [The]{.underline} [applicable]{.underline} [types
  of segments are]{.underline} [as follows:]{.underline}

  - Generic segments (Centerline segments with SEGMENT_TYPE = 'G').
    (Note: the house number fields in combined generic/roadbed segments
    (Centerline segments with SEGMENT_TYPE = 'B') and replicants based
    on them will NOT be zeroed out.)

  - Proto-segments coincident with generic segments (but NOT with
    combined generic/roadbed segments)

  - Non-physical Centerline segments (RW_TYPE = 12) (these include paper
    streets and faux segments)

  - Proto-segments that are not physical streets (FEATURE_TYPE = any
    value other than null, '6' or 'W')

<!-- -->

- The field [RB_Layer]{.underline} will be populated based on the value
  of the segment's Include/Exclude Flag and its Segment Type Code
  (fields L58 and L56 in the Geosupport LION record, respectively). The
  rules are as follows:

<!-- -->

- If L58 = 'E', set RB_Layer = 'N' (regardless of the value in L56).
  Otherwise:

- If L56 = blank, 'B', 'E' or 'U', set RB_Layer = 'B'

- If L56 = 'G' or 'F', set RB_Layer = 'G'

- If L56 = 'C', 'R', 'S' or 'T', set RB_Layer = 'R

> Note: If the ETL tool is programmed to use the source CSCL data to
> determine the populating of RB_Layer instead of the Geosupport LION
> output record, care must be taken to treat segments for which
> SEGMENT_TYPE = 'S' as roadbed segments, that is, to set RB_Layer = 'R'
> for those segments.

- The fields [LBoro and RBoro]{.underline} will be populated as follows.
  Every output record "belongs" to a specific borough, even if it lies
  on a borough boundary. The borough that the output record "belongs" to
  is determined by the borough of the CSCL source data from which the
  record was generated, as follows:

<!-- -->

- For records generated from Centerline segments and from SAF data in
  the CommonPlace and AddressPoint feature classes, the borough that the
  output record "belongs" to is indicated by the BOROUGHCODE attribute
  of the given CSCL source feature.

- For records generated from Rail, Subway, Shoreline and
  NonStreetFeature segments, the borough that the output record
  "belongs" to is the first byte of the B5SC, obtained from the
  Segment_LGC table by SEGMENTID, as described for the Geosupport LION
  in Section 2.3.1.

- For records generated from proto-segments or from SAF data in the
  AltSegmentData table, the borough that the output record "belongs" to
  is indicated in the AltSegmentData field BOROUGH.

> The output fields LBoro and RBoro will be populated based on the
> borough that the segment "belongs" to as defined above, and the value
> of the BoroBndry output field. Note that the contents of the BoroBndry
> field indicates the side of the segment that is out of the borough
> that the segment belongs to. If the BoroBdry field contains 'L' or
> 'R', the output field for the opposite side, RBoro or LBoro,
> respectively, will be populated with the borough code of the borough
> that the record "belongs" to, and the borough field for the other side
> of the segment will be populated with a null value. Note that if
> BoroBndry contains 'L', it is RBoro (not LBoro) that is populated with
> a value, and vice versa. If the BoroBdry field does not contain one of
> the values 'L' or 'R', both LBoro and RBoro will be populated with the
> borough code of the borough that the record "belongs" to.

- The field [MH_RI_Flag]{.underline} will be populated based on the
  borough to which the output segment "belongs" (in the sense defined in
  the discussion of LBoro and RBoro above), and on the segment's left
  and right Borough and 2000 Census Tract values, as follows:

<!-- -->

- If the output segment belongs to Manhattan, and the borough/tract
  combination for at least one side of the segment = Manhattan tract 309
  (i.e., that side is in Manhattan AND is in 2000 census tract is 309),
  set MH_RI_Flag = 'M'.

- If the output segment belongs to the Bronx, and the borough/tract
  combination for at least one side of the segment = Bronx tract 1
  (i.e., that side is in the Bronx AND is in 2000 census tract 1), set
  MH_RI_Flag = 'R'

- If neither of the above conditions is satisfied, set MH_RI_Flag to
  null.

<!-- -->

- The field [Join_ID]{.underline} serves to link segments in the LION
  feature class with entries in the Altnames table. This field is a
  15-character string and will be populated in the LION feature class as
  follows:

<!-- -->

- For output records other than those generated from SAF data, Join_ID
  is formed by concatenating the Borough (copied from LBoro or RBoro,
  whichever field is not null), the output fields Face Code, LGC1, LGC2,
  LGC3, LGC4, and two spaces. The LGCs are formatted numerically, that
  is, right-justified and zero-filled within two bytes, and are set to
  '00' if there is no value for the given LGC field.

- For SAF replicants (output records generated from SAF data), Join_ID
  is formed by concatenating Borough (populated as described above)**,**
  the SAF 5-digit street code and SAF LGC1, LGC2, LGC3, LGC4 fields
  (populated as described below), and SpecAddr (= the SAF type).

  - For the SAF replicants generated from AltSegmentData SAF entries
    (types A, B, C, D, E, O and P): the output SAF 5-digit street code
    subfield will be populated from the last five bytes of the B5SC
    field in the AltSegmentData entry. The output LGC subfields will be
    populated from the LGC fields in the AltSegmentData entry. The LGC
    fields will be formatted numerically, that is, right-justified and
    zero-filled within two bytes, and set to '00' if there is no value
    for the given LGC field.

  - For SAF replicants generated from CommonPlace features (types G, N
    and X): the output SAF 5-digit street code subfield will be
    populated from the second through sixth bytes of the CommonPlace
    B7SC attribute. The LGC1 output field will be populated from the
    last two bytes of the CommonPlace B7SC attribute, right-justified
    and zero-filled within the two-byte subfield. The LGC2, LGC3 and
    LGC4 output subfields will be populated with all zeros.

  - For type S SAF replicants, which are generated from AddressPoint
    features: the output SAF 5-digit street code subfield will be
    populated from the second through sixth bytes of the AddressPoint
    B7SC_ACTUAL attribute. The LGC1 output field will be populated from
    the last two bytes of the AddressPoint B7SC_ACTUAL attribute. The
    LGC2, LGC3 and LGC4 output subfields will be populated from
    AddressPointLGCs entries, if any (see Note 5 below Table 35 in
    Section 7.8), or with zeros if there is no corresponding
    AddressPointLGCs entry.

  - For type V SAF replicants, which are generated from AddressPoint
    features: the output SAF 5-digit street code subfield will be
    populated from the second through sixth bytes of the AddressPoint
    B7SC_VANITY attribute. The LGC1 output field will be populated from
    the last two bytes of the AddressPoint B7SC_VANITY attribute. The
    LGC2, LGC3 and LGC4 output subfields will be populated from
    AddressPointLGCs entries, if any (see Note 5 below Table 35 in
    Section 7.8), or with zeros if there is no corresponding
    AddressPointLGCs entry.

<!-- -->

- The fields [MapFrom]{.underline} and [MapTo]{.underline} are defined
  as three bytes each, unlike the related Geosupport LION fields L11
  (From Sectional Map) and L15 (To Sectional Map), which are defined as
  two bytes each. Three bytes are provided in the Bytes LION fields to
  accommodate the inclusion of a quarter-sectional suffix, if any. As
  specified in Section 2.2.2, to populate L11 and L15 in Geosupport LION
  records, the ETL program performs a spatial query against the
  SectionalMap polygon feature class. For the Bytes LION files, the
  QuarterSectionalMap feature class will be spatially queried instead.
  The MapFrom and MapTo fields in the Bytes LION records will be
  populated as follows:

  - A spatial query will be performed for the corresponding ("from" or
    "to") segment endpoint against the QuarterSectionalMap polygon
    feature class.

  - If the spatial query for a segment endpoint fails to find a
    quarter-sectional polygon, the corresponding output field (MapFrom
    or MapTo) will be populated with blanks, and a warning message will
    be issued.

  - 

  - If a polygon is found, the value in the polygon's SECTIONAL_MAP
    attribute field and the value in the SECTIONAL_QTR_SUFFIX field (if
    any) will be concatenated, and the resulting string will be inserted
    left-justified blank-filled into the corresponding three-byte output
    field (MapFrom or MapTo). For example (using '#' to represent a
    blank):

    - Sectional map 4 with no quarter-sectional suffix would be stored
      in the output field as '4##'.

    - Map 6 with quarter-suffix C would be stored as '6C#'.

    - Map 3W with no suffix would be stored as '3W#'.

    - Map 2E with suffx B would be stored as '2EB'.

    - 

    - Map 12 with no suffix would be stored as '12#'.

    - 

    - Map 15 with suffx C would be stored as '15C'.

### Generating the AltNames Table

The Altnames table is extracted to contain entries for all street names
and feature names pertaining to all features represented in the ESRI
LION. The ETL tool extracts the names from the CSCL StreetName and
FeatureName tables. However, the ETL tool does not extract any names
into the AltNames table for which the value of the DCP_FLAG is 'N'.

[The Geodatabase AltNames Table data model can be found at folder of
"Templates\\lion.gdb".]{.mark}

A set of output AltNames records will be generated for each Join_ID
value that occurs in an output record in the LION feature class. Each
record in the set will contain a street name or feature name belonging
to a B7SC value that is explicitly or implicitly stored in the given
Join_ID. In SAF output records, the B7SCs are stored explicitly in the
Join_ID, in the sense that it contains a B5SC and a list of LGCs from
which B7SCs can be directly formed by concatenation. In non-SAF output
records, the B7SC values in the Join_ID are stored implicitly in the
sense that the Join_ID contains a Face Code value instead of a B5SC. To
retrieve all the names in the StreetName or FeatureName table (for which
DCP_FLAG = 'Y') for all the implicit B7SC values in such a Join_ID, it
is necessary to concatenate the B5SC value that corresponds to the given
Face Code value with each of the LGC values listed in that Join_ID. That
B5SC value is stored in the output field StreetCode in any of the LION
output segment records that contain the given Join_ID value.

Street and feature names will be stored in AltNames in two forms:

- As a single, unparsed character string in the field Street, obtained
  from the LOOKUP_KEY field in the given StreetName or FeatureName table
  entry.

- In ESRI's standard parsed format in the component fields PDir
  (pre-directional), PType (pre-type), SName (basic street name), SType
  (suffix type, also commonly known as post-type) and SDir (suffix
  directional, also commonly known as post-directional). These fields
  correspond to the parsing component fields in CSCL's StreetName table,
  except that there are no pre- and post-modifier fields in the ESRI
  LION.

The rules for populating the parsed component fields are as follows:

- For names in the CSCL FeatureName table, the entire name will be
  populated into the SName field from the FeatureName field LOOKUP_KEY.

- For names in StreetName, the ETL tool will populate the output ESRI
  LION record as follows:

1.  If the StreetName entry contains values in both the PRE_MODIFIER and
    POST_MODIFIER fields, the ETL tool will concatenate the values in
    all of that entry's street name component fields, separating each
    consecutive pair of non-null values with a single blank, and will
    populate the resulting string into the 30-byte SName field,
    truncating on the right if necessary. If truncation was necessary,
    the ETL tool will issue a warning message into the output report.

2.  If the StreetName entry contains a value in the PRE_MODIFIER field
    but not the POST_MODIFIER field, the ETL tool will concatenate the
    values in PRE_MODIFIER, PRE_DIRECTIONAL, PRE_TYPE and STREET_NAME,
    separating each consecutive pair of non-null values with a single
    blank, and will populate the resulting string into the 30-byte SName
    field, truncating on the right if necessary. If truncation was
    necessary, the ETL tool will issue a warning message into the output
    report. If there are values in the entry's POST_TYPE and/or
    POST_DIRECTIONAL fields, they will be copied into the SType and/or
    SDir field, respectively.

3.  If the StreetName entry contains a value in the POST_MODIFIER field
    but not the PRE_MODIFIER field, the ETL tool will concatenate the
    values in STREET_NAME, POST_TYPE, POST_DIRECTIONAL and
    POST_MODIFIER, separating each consecutive pair of non-null values
    with a single blank, and will populate the resulting string into the
    30-byte SName field, truncating on the right if necessary. If
    truncation was necessary, the ETL tool will issue a warning message
    into the output report. If there are values in the entry's
    PRE_DIRECTIONAL and/or PRE_TYPE fields, they will be copied into the
    PDir and/or PType field, respectively.

# Street Name Dictionary

The Street Name Dictionary (SND) is extracted as a single file for the
entire city. After all output records have been written, the file is
sorted on the fields Borough and Street/Feature Name (that is, positions
2 through 34 of the output record).

The CSCL StreetName and FeatureName tables contain the following fields
that affect SND extraction:

- LOOKUP_KEY: For names that are to be extracted to the SND, this field
  will contain the given street or feature name in a
  Geosupport-normalized format. (In particular, the character string
  stored in this field will always be no longer than 32 bytes for such
  entries.) The ETL tool will use this field to populate the
  street/feature name field in output SND records. (The CSCL Maintenance
  System will also use this field, to check for duplicates when new
  names are being added to StreetName and FeatureName.)

- ENDERS_FLAG: Identifies special StreetName and FeatureName entries
  intended only for extraction to the Enders Table output file, as
  described in Section 4.3. These entries will not be extracted to the
  SND.

- EXCEPTION_FLAG: Identifies entries to be used to generate records in
  the Exception Table output file, as described in Section 4.1. These
  entries will also be extracted to the SND, if they satisfy the
  filtering criteria.

Not all names in the CSCL StreetName and FeatureName tables are
extracted into the SND. The filtering criteria are as follows:

- Names for which LOOKUP_KEY = null will not be extracted.

- Names for which ENDERS_FLAG = 'Y' will not be extracted.

<!-- -->

- Any names that do not have a street code assigned to them will not be
  extracted, in spite of the fact that the LOOKUP_KEY field is not null.
  The ETL tool will identify these as all StreetName and FeatureName
  entries in which the B10SC field is unpopulated. (Note: the absence of
  a B10SC value is not necessarily a data error. These are likely to be
  names that have been supplied by City agencies such as NYPD and FDNY
  but have been deemed inappropriate for inclusion in the SND and thus
  have intentionally not had street codes assigned to them.)

Although the Geosupport SND contains two types of records, non-type S
records and type S records, the ETL tool only writes out non-type S
records. It will write out one non-S output record for each qualified
entry in StreetName and FeatureName (each entry that satisfies the above
filtering criteria).

Table 19 contains a layout of the (non-type S) output records.

[]{#_Ref214090239 .anchor}Table 19 -- SND Output File -- Record Layout

  -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **FIC**   **Field**            **Len**   **Frm**   **To** **Comments**
  --------- ------------------ --------- --------- -------- ---------------------------
  SNDN1     Record Type                1         1        1 

  SNDN2     Borough                    1         2        2 

  SNDN3     Street Name or            32         3       34 
            Feature Name                                    

  SNDN4     Primary Name Flag          1        35       35 

  SNDN5     Principal Name             1        36       36 
            Flag                                            

  SNDN6     B10SC                     11        37       47 

  N/A       Filler                     2        48       49 

  SNDN7     Numeric Name               1        50       50 
            Indicator                                       

  SNDN8     Geographic Feature         1        51       51 
            Type                                            

  SNDN9     Length of Name             2        52       53 

  SNDN10    Full Name                 32        54       85 Vestige of partial names
                                                            feature

  N/A       Filler                     2        86       87 Reserved for possible
                                                            future use for a "Minimum
                                                            SNL" field

  N/A       Filler                    20        88      107 Formerly used for 20-Byte
                                                            Name, no longer required

  SNDN11    Horizontal                 1       108      108 
            Topology Name Type                              
            Code                                            

  N/A       Filler                    92       109      200 
  -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

A (non-type S) record will be written for each "qualified" entry in the
StreetName and FeatureName tables. The fields in the output record will
be populated as indicated in Table 20 and the notes following it.

[]{#_Ref222642996 .anchor}Table 20 -- Populating SND Output Records

+---------+-------------------+-----------------------------------------+
| **FIC** | **Field**         | **Methodology to Populate**             |
+=========+===================+=========================================+
| SNDN1   | Record Type       | Populate with the value '1'             |
+---------+-------------------+-----------------------------------------+
| SNDN2   | Borough           | Copy first byte of StreetName or        |
|         |                   | FeatureName field B10SC                 |
+---------+-------------------+-----------------------------------------+
| SNDN3   | Street Name or    | Populate from StreetName or FeatureName |
|         | Feature Name      | field LOOKUP_KEY, store LJSF. See Note  |
|         |                   | 1.                                      |
+---------+-------------------+-----------------------------------------+
| SNDN4   | Primary Name Flag | If PRIMARY_FLAG = 'Y', populate with    |
|         |                   | value 'P'.                              |
|         |                   |                                         |
|         |                   | If PRIMARY_FLAG = 'N', populate with    |
|         |                   | 'V'                                     |
+---------+-------------------+-----------------------------------------+
| SNDN5   | Principal Name    | If PRINCIPAL_FLAG = 'Y', populate with  |
|         | Flag              | 'F'.                                    |
|         |                   |                                         |
|         |                   | If PRINCIPAL_FLAG = 'N', populate with  |
|         |                   | 'S'.                                    |
+---------+-------------------+-----------------------------------------+
| SNDN6   | B10SC             | Copy StreetName or FeatureName field    |
|         |                   | B10SC                                   |
+---------+-------------------+-----------------------------------------+
| SNDN7   | Numeric Name      | Populate with 'N' if name contains at   |
|         | Indicator         | least one numeric digit immediately     |
|         |                   | preceded by a blank; else, populate     |
|         |                   | with a blank.                           |
+---------+-------------------+-----------------------------------------+
| SNDN8   | Geographic        | Copy StreetName or FeatureName field    |
|         | Feature Type      | SND_FEATURE_TYPE                        |
+---------+-------------------+-----------------------------------------+
| SNDN9   | Length of Name    | Populate with length of name, measured  |
|         |                   | from first byte (whether or not it      |
|         |                   | contains a blank) up to and including   |
|         |                   | last non-blank character. Store RJZF.   |
+---------+-------------------+-----------------------------------------+
| SNDN10  | Full Name         | Copy value populated in field SNDN3 --  |
|         |                   | see Note 2                              |
+---------+-------------------+-----------------------------------------+
| SNDN11  | Horizontal        | If name is from StreetName, copy        |
|         | Topology Name     | StreetName field HORIZONTAL_TOPO_TYPE.  |
|         | Type Code         |                                         |
|         |                   | If name is from FeatureName, populate   |
|         |                   | with a blank.                           |
+---------+-------------------+-----------------------------------------+

**[NOTES TO TABLE 20:]{.underline}**

1.  SNDN3 (Street Name or Feature Name): This field will be populated
    from the StreetName or FeatureName field LOOKUP_KEY, as follows.
    LOOKUP_KEY contains names in a format that has been converted from
    the Geosupport System normalized format in which names are stored in
    the SND, called the "Sort Format", by compacting the name (i.e.,
    replacing any sequences of multiple consecutive blanks with a single
    blank). The ETL tool will convert the name back to the Sort Format
    for populating into output field SNDN3 by restoring the removed
    blanks (if any). This will be done as follows:

    i.  The name will be scanned from left to right.

    ii. If the end (last non-blank character) of the name is reached and
        no numeric digits ('0' through '9') have been encountered, the
        name will be populated into SNDN3 unmodified.

    iii. If a numeric digit is encountered, we'll use the term "current
         numeric string" (CNS) to refer to the string of (one or more)
         consecutive numeric digits that begin with the given one and
         are immediately followed by a non-numeric character (possibly a
         blank). Let L be the length of the CNS. L could be 1 or greater
         than 1. The CNS is processed as follows:

         A.  If the CNS is at the beginning of a "word" (i.e., if it
             occupies the first byte position in LOOKUP_KEY or is
             immediately preceded by a blank), and the CNS has a length
             of 1, 2 or 3, a sequence of blanks called "alignment
             blanks" will be inserted into the name, positioned
             immediately preceding the CNS. The number of alignment
             blanks that must be inserted is equal to (4 -- L). For
             example, if L = 2 (i.e., the CNS consists of two
             consecutive numeric digits), then (4 -- L) = 2, and so two
             alignment blanks must be inserted immediately preceding the
             CNS.

         B.  If the CNS is at the beginning of a word and L \> 3, no
             alignment blanks will be inserted preceding the CNS.

         C.  If the CNS is not at the beginning of a word or at the
             beginning of LOOKUP_KEY (i.e., if it is immediately
             preceded by a non-blank character), then in addition to the
             alignment blanks (if any) inserted as described in step A
             above, a single word-separating blank will also be
             inserted, positioned following that preceding non-blank
             character, regardless of the length of the CNS.

         D.  If the last digit of the CNS is the last non-blank
             character in the name, the processing is complete. The
             (possibly) reformatted name will be populated into field
             SNDN3. Otherwise, the processing will continue below.

         E.  If the character immediately following the CNS is not a
             blank (it is necessarily non-numeric, since if it were a
             numeric digit it would have been included in the CNS), a
             single word-separating blank will be inserted, positioned
             immediately following the last digit of the CNS.

    iv. The scan of the name in LOOKUP_KEY will continue from left to
        right. If another numeric digit is encountered, it will be
        treated as the beginning of a new CNS, and the above processing
        will be repeated for that CNS.

    v.  When the scan reaches the end (the last non-blank character) of
        the name, the processing is complete. The reformatted name will
        be populated into field SNDN3.

    vi. Examples ('**\***' represents an inserted alignment blank, '\$'
        represents an inserted word-separating blank; note that all
        existing word-separating blanks are left in place):

> [Name in LOOKUP_KEY]{.underline} Output [Name (in Sort
> Format)]{.underline}
>
> 3 AVENUE **\*\*\***3 AVENUE
>
> 11 AVENUE **\*\***11 AVENUE
>
> 108 STREET **\***108 STREET
>
> EAST 7 STREET EAST **\*\*\***7 STREET
>
> EAST 23 STREET EAST **\*\***23 STREET
>
> EAST 104 STREET EAST **\***104 STREET
>
> EAST 9 STREET BLDG16 EAST **\*\*\***9 STREET BLDG\$**\*\*1**6
>
> 9/11 MEMORIAL PLAZA **\*\*\***9\$/\$**\*\***11 MEMORIAL PLAZA

vii. [SND3 will be in original format when 'SND_FEATURE_TYPE=="
     U"]{.mark}

> [(Misc. Structure -- Rail/subway station)]{.mark}

1.  SNDN10 (Full Name): This field is a vestige of "partial street
    names", a type of name that is no longer stored in the SND. (Partial
    street names are not to be confused with front-truncated street
    names.) The ETL tool will populate this field with an exact copy of
    the name stored in field SNDN3. **RECOMMENDATION**: If and when DCP
    determines definitively that SNDN10 is no longer required, the ETL
    tool should be modified to treat it as a filler field and populate
    it with blanks.

# Geosupport System Normalizing Tables

The ETL tool can produce output files for the following Geosupport
System normalizing tables:

- Exception Table, discussed in Section 4.1

- Universal Word Table and Last Word Table, discussed in Section 4.2.

- Enders Table, discussed in Section 4.3.

## Exception Table

The output Exception Table is created in the form of a text file
containing variable-length records. Each output record is constructed by
concatenating the following three items in sequence:

- A name in the LOOKUP_KEY field obtained from an entry in the CSCL
  StreetName or FeatureName table, possibly modified by deleting the
  last word, as explained below

- A single blank

- An end-of-line (CRLF) character.

A single output file is produced for the entire city. The output file is
sorted on the entire record.

Output records will be generated only for entries in the StreetName and
FeatureName tables for which EXCEPTION_FLAG = 'Y' and ENDERS_FLAG = 'N'.
In general, one output record will be created for each such table entry.
However, in some cases, a single output record might be created
corresponding to multiple table entries (see "eliminating duplicates"
below).

To create the output records, the following processing must be
performed:

1.  [Examine last word for possible deletion:]{.underline} If the last
    word of the exception name is listed in the CSCL UniversalWord
    and/or LastWord tables, that word must be deleted when formatting
    the exception name for output, along with the word-separating blank
    between the preceding word and that word. Whether such deletion is
    necessary will be determined by matching the last word of the
    exception name to the contents of each of the fields (other than
    OBJECTID) in the CSCL UniversalWord and/or LastWord tables. If there
    is an exact match to any of those fields, the last word will be
    deleted.

2.  [Generate output record:]{.underline} After deleting the last word
    and the blank preceding it when necessary, the output record will be
    formatted as described at the beginning of this section and then
    written into the output Exception Table file.

3.  [Eliminate duplicates]{.underline}: The dropping of last words could
    result in duplicate names (and therefore duplicate output records),
    if two or more names flagged as exceptions are identical except for
    their last words. The ETL tool will eliminate duplicate output
    records.

4.  [[See Document of "ETL for the Exception Street Name
    Table.doc".]{.underline}]{.mark}

## Universal Word Table and Last Word Table

The ETL tool extracts a Universal Word Table output file and a Last Word
Table output file from the entries in the CSCL UniversalWord and
LastWord tables, respectively. The output files are extracted in ASCII
comma-delimited or "Comma-Separated Value" (CSV) format. Both output
files have the same format. The fields in the output record are listed
in Table 21.

[]{#_Ref222653407 .anchor}Table 21 -- Universal and Last Word Table
Fields

  ------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **FIC**        **Field**                      **Source**
  -------------- ------------------------------ --------------------------
  WT1            Unique "C" Program Variable    See Note 1
                 Name                           

  WT2            Directional Indicator          See Note 2

  WT3            Full Spelling                  Corresp. field in CSCL
                                                table

  WT4            Standard Abbreviation          Corresp. field in CSCL
                                                table

  WT5            Shortest Abbreviation          Corresp. field in CSCL
                                                table

  WT6, WT7 etc.  Other acceptable               See Note 3
  up to WT15 (as abbreviation(s), if any        
  many of these                                 
  fields as                                     
  necessary)                                    
  ------------------------------------------------------------------------

**[NOTES TO TABLE 21:]{.underline}**

1.  WT1 (Unique "C" Program Variable Name): The ETL tool will populate
    this field with a four-byte character string constructed as follows.
    The string will be unique to the given output record within the
    given output file. (It will serve as part of a variable name within
    the source code of a Geosupport "C" program into which the Universal
    and Last Word table files extracted by the ETL tool will ultimately
    be imbedded.) The value must be unique only within each Word Table,
    not across both tables. The value of WT1 within each table will be
    derived as follows:

    - The first character will consist of the first character of the
      value in the field WT3 (Full Spelling). It is referred to below as
      the "initial letter". It will always be alphabetic.

    - The remaining three characters will consist of an integer of up to
      three digits, right-justified and zero-filled. The value assigned
      will be the next available integer, that is, the smallest integer
      not yet used for the given initial letter in the given table.

    - For example, the value populated into WT1 in the first Universal
      Table output record that is generated for an entry whose full
      spelling begins with the letter D would be D001. The value
      populated into WT1 for the next Universal Word Table output record
      that is generated for an entry whose full spelling also begins
      with D would be D002, etc. (The same values can also be used for
      output Last Word Table records. If the same value happens to be
      used in the WT1 field in a Universal Word Table output record and
      a Last Word Table output record, that would not imply any
      relationship between those records.)

    - A suggested design approach is to utilize two 26 X 2 (26-row
      two-column) arrays in the ETL program, one for each Word Table.
      The first column would contain the letters of the alphabet from A
      to Z. The second column would contain the next available integer
      for the given letter. The second column would be initialized to
      '1' for all letters, and would be incremented when used in an
      output record.

2.  WT2 (Directional Indicator): The ETL tool will populate field WT2
    with the value 'Y' if the record is for a "directional" word, and
    with the value 'N' otherwise. Since the CSCL Universal and Last Word
    tables do not contain a field to identify directional words, the ETL
    tool will be "hard-coded" to identify those words. If (and only if)
    the field WT3 contains one of the words listed below, the record
    will be treated as a directional for the purpose of populating field
    WT2:

  --------------------
  EAST
  --------------------
  EASTBOUND

  NORTH

  NORTHBOUND

  NORTHEAST

  NORTHWEST

  SOUTH

  SOUTHBOUND

  SOUTHEAST

  SOUTHWEST

  WEST

  WESTBOUND
  --------------------

3.  WT6 through WT15 (Other Acceptable Abbreviations): As many of these
    fields will be populated as necessary to accommodate the value(s)
    from the corresponding fields in the CSCL table.

4.  [See "ETL Last and Universal Word Tables.doc" for more
    information]{.mark}.

Both output files must be sorted on field WT3 (Full Spelling). Since
this field is of variable length in the comma-delimited format, the ETL
tool must sort the CSCL tables prior to generating the output files.

## Enders Table

The Enders Table output file is extracted as a sequential, fixed-length
file with a record length of 32 bytes. The ETL tool writes one output
record for each entry in StreetName or FeatureName in which the
ENDERS_FLAG = 'Y'. The record consists entirely of a single 32-byte
field, which will be populated with the contents of the leftmost 32
bytes of the LOOKUP_KEY field from the given StreetName or FeatureName
entry.

A single file is produced for the entire city. No sorting is required.

Note that the only fields that will be populated with values in
StreetName and FeatureName enders entries (entries in which the
ENDERS_FLAG = 'Y') are DCP_FLAG, ENDERS_FLAG, LOOKUP_KEY and
EXCEPTION_FLAG. All other fields will be empty, including the B10SC,
PRIMARY_FLAG etc. The LOOKUP_KEY field in enders entries always contains
an (intentionally) invalid name, stored in the form that the Geosupport
System normalizer would produce if it did not recognize the name as
being "enders-impacted" (i.e., if the name was not listed in
Geosupport's Enders Table).

As a hypothetical example, if Geosupport did not recognize the name B Q
E as being enders-impacted, it would normalize it to B Q EAST. (The 'E'
in B Q E actually stands for "expressway", not "east".) B Q EAST is the
form in which the name will appear in the LOOKUP_KEY field in the
StreetName enders entry. The ETL tool will extract B Q EAST from this
enders entry into the Enders output file, where its presence will
prevent Geosupport from normalizing B Q E incorrectly. (The CSCL
StreetName table will also contain a "regular" (non-enders) entry for B
Q E. That entry will contain a full complement of field values,
including the fields B10SC, PRIMARY_FLAG etc.

[See "ETL for the Enders Table V2.doc" for more information.]{.mark}

# Face Code File

The ETL tool produces a separate Face Code output file for each borough.
The files are sorted on bytes 2 through 5, the Face Code field (field
FC2 in the layout below). Note that there is no need to include field
FC1 (Borough) as a sort key, since the Face Code file will be extracted
as a separate file for each borough.

Each Face Code file will contain one record for each face code value
valid in the given borough. The ETL tool will create those records by
writing out one output record into the appropriate borough file for each
entry in the StreetName or FeatureName table that contains a non-null
Face Code value.

**ASSUMPTION**: Each valid combination of Borough and Face Code occurs
in exactly one entry in exactly one of CSCL's name tables. The
Maintenance System will be designed to ensure this. The ETL tool does
not validate for the existence of entries with duplicate face codes, and
is not designed to eliminate such duplicates.

[]{.mark}Table 22 contains a layout of the Face Code output file. The
last column indicates the source of data for populating each field.

[]{#_Ref222653515 .anchor}Table 22 -- Face Code Output File

  ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **FIC**   **Field**                 **Len**   **Frm**   **To** **CSCL Source of Data**
  --------- ----------------------- --------- --------- -------- ---------------------------
  FC1       Borough                         1         1        1 Copy first byte of
                                                                 StreetName or FeatureName
                                                                 field B10SC

  FC2       Face Code                       4         2        5 Copy StreetName or
                                                                 FeatureName field FACECODE.
                                                                 Store right-justified
                                                                 zero-filled

            Filler                          1         6        6 Populate with blank

  FC3       B10SC                          11         7       17 Copy StreetName or
                                                                 FeatureName field B10SC

  N/A       Filler                          1        18       18 Populate with blank

  FC4       Name of street or              32        19       50 Copy StreetName or
            non-street feature                                   FeatureName field
                                                                 LOOKUP_KEY, store
                                                                 left-justified space-filled
  ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

# District Equivalency Files

The ETL tool produces two types of district equivalency files: ThinLION
and ThinFire. For each of these, the ETL tool produces a separate file
for each borough. Each of these files also has a sort requirement, as
noted in the respective sections below.

## ThinLION

[]{.mark}Table 23 contains a layout of the ThinLION output file. The
last column in the table and the notes following the table indicate the
CSCL source of data for populating each field.

ThinLION is extracted as a separate file for each borough. One output
record will be written into ThinLION for each feature in the Atomic
Polygon (AP) feature class belonging to the given borough. Most of the
fields in the output record will be populated from attribute fields of
the given Atomic Polygon.

ThinLION is sorted on the fields TL2 and TL3 (in that order of
priority). Note that there is no need to include TL1 (Borough) as a sort
key, since a separate file is extracted for each borough.

[See "ThinLIONExtractorConfiguration.xml" and "ETL THINLION CSCL_V16
(Feb09, 2023).doc" for the output sequence of the fields]{.mark}.

[]{#_Ref212968444 .anchor}~~Table 23 -- ThinLION Output File~~

  -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **~~FIC~~**   **~~Field~~**      **~~Len~~**   **~~Frm~~**   **~~To~~**  **~~Format~~**   **~~CSCL Source~~**
  ------------- ----------------- ------------- ------------- ------------ ---------------- -------------------------------
  ~~TL1~~       ~~Borough~~           ~~1~~         ~~1~~        ~~1~~                      ~~Copy AP attribute BOROUGH~~

  ~~TL2~~       ~~2000 Census         ~~6~~         ~~2~~        ~~7~~     ~~See Sec. 1.4~~ ~~Populate from AP attribute
                Tract~~                                                                     CENSUSTRACT_2000~~

  ~~TL3~~       ~~Dynamic Block~~     ~~3~~         ~~8~~        ~~10~~                     ~~Populate with last 3 bytes of
                                                                                            AP attribute ATOMICID~~

  ~~TL4~~       ~~2000 Census         ~~4~~        ~~11~~        ~~14~~                     ~~Copy AP attribute
                Block Basic~~                                                               CENSUSBLOCK_2000~~

  ~~TL5~~       ~~2000 Census         ~~1~~        ~~15~~        ~~15~~    ~~Blank if       ~~Populate from AP attribute
                Block Suffix~~                                             none~~           **CENSUSBLOCK_2000_SUFFIX**~~

  ~~TL6~~       ~~1990 Census         ~~6~~        ~~16~~        ~~21~~    ~~See Sec. 1.4~~ ~~Populate from AP attribute
