**[NOTES TO Table 23:]{.underline}**

1.  TL7 (Community Development Eligibility), TL9 (Minor Census Economic
    Area) and TL10 (Health Area): These fields will be populated from
    attributes of the feature class CensusTract2010. The access key for
    this feature class consists of the concatenation of the attribute
    fields BOROUGH and CENSUSTRACT_2010 of the AP feature class. The ETL
    tool will match that value to the CensusTract2010 attribute BOROCT.

    a.  Populate TL7 from CensusTract2010 attribute CD_ELIGIBILITY

    b.  Populate TL9 from CensusTract2010 attribute MCEA

    c.  Populate TL10 from CensusTract2010 attribute HEALTH_AREA

2.  TL11 (Health Center District): This field will be populated from an
    attribute of the feature class HealthArea. The access key for this
    feature class consists of the attribute field HEALTH_AREA of
    CensusTract2010. The ETL tool will match this value to the
    HEALTHAREA attribute of HealthArea. The ETL tool will populate TL11
    from the HealthArea attribute HEALTH_CT_DISTRICT.

3.  TL12 (Police Patrol Borough Command) and TL13 (Police Precinct): The
    CSCL NYPDPrecinct and NYPDBoroughCommand polygon feature classes are
    not based on Atomic Polygons. Consequently, the AP feature class
    does not contain attributes for these district types that could be
    captured for populating TL12 and TL13. The ETL tool will capture
    these values spatially, as follows. The ETL tool will generate a
    centroid point for the AP being processed. The ETL tool will then
    perform a spatial point-in-polygon search for that centroid against
    the NYPDPrecinct polygons. If there is an NYPDPrecinct polygon that
    contains the AP centroid, its BOROUGH_COMMAND and PRECINCT attribute
    values will be populated into TL12 and TL13 respectively. If there
    is no such precinct polygon, TL12 and TL13 will be populated with
    blanks. (The latter case will not be treated as a data error, as
    there may validly be areas of the city not covered by any precinct,
    such as some water APs.)

4.  [TL32 (Patrol Borough): The field will be Extracted from
    \"PATROL_BOROUGH\" in CSCL.NYPDPatrolBorough\" feature]{.mark}
    [class.]{.mark}

## ThinFire

Table 25 contains a layout of the ThinFire output file. The last column
in the table indicates the CSCL source of data for populating each
field.

ThinFire is extracted as a separate file for each borough. One output
record will be written into ThinFire for each feature in the FireCompany
feature class. ThinFire will be sorted on the fields TF1 (Admin Fire
Company Type) and TF2 (Admin Fire Company Number). Note that there is no
need to include TF5 (Borough) as a sort key, since a separate file is
extracted for each borough.

[]{#_Ref222653667 .anchor}Table 25 -- ThinFire Output File

  -----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **FIC**   **Field**                **Len**   **Frm**   **To** **CSCL Source of data**
  --------- ---------------------- --------- --------- -------- ---------------------------
  TF1       Admin Fire Company             1         1        1 First byte of FireCompany
            Type                                                attribute UNIT_SHORT.

  TF2       Admin Fire Company             3         2        4 Last three bytes of
            Number                                              FireCompany attribute
                                                                UNIT_SHORT.

  TF3       Admin Fire Division            2         5        6 Attribute BOROUGHCOMMAND of
                                                                FireCompany f.c.

  TF4       Admin Fire Battalion           2         7        8 Attribute BATTALION of
                                                                FireCompany f.c.

  TF5       Borough                        1         9        9 See Note 1
  -----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**[NOTE TO Table 25]{.underline}:**

Note 1: TF5 (Borough): The FireCompany feature class does not have an
attribute for Borough. Although it would be possible to determine the
borough spatially by forming a fire company centroid and performing a
point-in-polygon match to borough polygons or AP polygons, the following
alternative method involving attribute matching appears likely to
provide better performance efficiency and is recommended for
consideration by the developer:

- Except for the three special cases listed below, find any AP whose
  ADMIN_FIRE_COMPANY attribute exactly matches the FireCompany attribute
  UNIT_SHORT (these two attributes, which serve as the unique identifier
  for a fire company, are identical data items that have been given two
  different names in these two feature classes). There will always be a
  match to at least one AP (multiple APs are likely to match in almost
  all cases), since FireCompany polygons are generated by dissolving APs
  based on ADMIN_FIRE_COMPANY. Populate TF5 with the BOROUGH attribute
  of any of the matching AP's.

- The following three special cases will be handled by "hard-coding":

  - Fire Company E-81 belongs to the Bronx, even though the territory
    (and Atomic Polygons) it covers, the Marble Hill neighborhood, is
    part of Manhattan. Populate field TF5 with the value '2'.

  - Fire Company E-260 belongs to Queens, even though the territory it
    covers, Roosevelt Island, is part of Manhattan. Populate field TF5
    with the value '4'.

  - Fire Company E-263 belongs to Queens, even though the territory it
    covers, Rikers Island, is part of the Bronx. Populate field TF5 with
    the value '4'.

# Special Address File

There are 13 Special Address File (SAF) output record types, classified
as types A, B, C, D, E, G, I, N, O, P, S, V and X. (The CSCL database
also contains SAF data identified as type F, but the ETL tool
re-classifies these as type D records in the output files.) Each SAF
record pertains to a particular geographic feature, as follows:

- Type I records represent named street intersections and pertain to
  nodes, which are identified by NODEID.

- SAF records of types other than I pertain to segments of linear
  features. In the output SAF files, appurtenant segments are identified
  by LION Keys.

  - Type A, B, C, D, E, O, P, S and V records contain address
    information and pertain to street segments, which are represented in
    the CSCL database either as Centerline segments or as street feature
    proto-segments (coincident segment entries in the AltSegmentData
    table with an implicit feature class of Centerline).

  - Type G, N and X records contain Non-Addressable Place names (NAPs)
    and pertain either to street segments or proto-segments, or to
    Shoreline segments.

In the CSCL database, the SEGMENTID of a linear feature-related SAF
record may identify a Centerline or Shoreline segment that has a
proto-segment (i.e., an AltSegmentData coincident segment entry with the
same SEGMENTID). In that case:

- The proto-segment is necessarily either a coincident borough boundary
  segment (ALT_SEGDATA_TYPE = 'B') or a boundary continuity segment
  (ALT_SEGDATA_TYPE = 'C'). It is never a combined on-off ramp
  (ALT_SEGDATA_TYPE = 'R'), since SAF records never pertain to ramps.

- If the geometry-represented segment is a Shoreline segment, the SAF
  record necessarily pertains to it, not to the proto-segment. That is
  because proto-segments that are coincident with Shoreline segments are
  always non-physical borough boundary features and thus never have
  appurtenant SAF data. (Note: G, N and X are the only SAFTYPEs that can
  pertain to a Shoreline segment.)

- If the geometry-represented segment is a Centerline segment and the
  proto-segment is a boundary continuity segment, the SAF record
  necessarily pertains to the geometry-represented segment. Boundary
  continuity proto-segments are non-physical features and never have
  appurtenant SAF data.

- If the geometry-represented segment is a Centerline segment and the
  proto-segment is a borough boundary segment, the SAF record pertains
  to the entity (the geometry-represented segment or the proto-segment)
  that belongs to the same borough as the SAF record.

Whether an SAF record pertains to a geometry-represented segment or a
proto-segment affects how certain fields in certain SAFTYPEs will be
populated, as noted in the sections on those SAFTYPEs. That is because
feature-specific data items (such as street codes, Face Codes and
Sequence Numbers) differ between the geometry-represented segment and
the proto-segment.

In some cases different SAF record types have the same record layout,
although they may utilize different subsets of the fields in that layout
or may utilize the same field differently. Specifically, the 13 SAF
record types have five distinct layouts, grouped as follows:

- Record types A, B, C, E, G, N, P and X have the layout shown in Table
  28.

- Record types O and V have the layout shown in Table 33 and Table 35
  (the same layout is in both tables, but the populating rules differ).

- Record type D has the layout shown in Table 30.

- Record type I has the layout shown in Table 32.

- Record type S has the layout shown in Table 34.

SAF record types that have the same layout will be written into the same
output file. The ETL tool will produce a single output file for the type
I records. The tool will produce two output files for each of the four
segment-related record layouts: a generic version and a roadbed version.
Therefore, the tool will produce a total of nine SAF output files.

Except for the type I records, the file version(s) into which the ETL
tool will write a particular SAF output record depend(s) on the
combination of the SAFTYPE of the SAF record and the SEGMENT_TYPE and
INCEX_FLAG of the Centerline segment to which the SAF record is
appurtenant, as shown in Table 26. For type G, N and X records only, it
is possible for the record to pertain to a segment belonging either to
the Centerline feature class (or a proto-segment whose implicit feature
class is Centerline) or to the Shoreline feature class; if it pertains
to a Shoreline segment, the output record will be included in both the
generic and roadbed versions.

In Table 26, the column labeled "FIC String" lists the alphabetic
(file-identifying) portion of the FIC for the given SAF output file.
Since the generic and roadbed versions of a given SAF output file have
identical layouts, the same FIC String will be used for both versions.

[]{#_Ref222718765 .anchor}Table 26 -- SAF Output File Rules

  --------------------------------------------------------------------
  **FIC      **SAFTYPEs**        **SEGMENT_TYPEs to **SEGMENT_TYPEs to
  String**                       Include in the     Include in the
                                 Generic Version**  Roadbed Version**
  ---------- ------------------- ------------------ ------------------
  SAFI       I                   N/A                N/A

  SAFA       A, B, C, E, G, N,   B, E, G (except    E, R, S (proposed
             P, X                when INCEX_FLAG =  value), U or
                                 'E'), U or         Shoreline segment
                                 Shoreline segment  

  SAFD       D                   B, E, G (except    E, R, S, U
                                 when INCEX_FLAG =  
                                 'E'), U            

  SAFV       O, V                B, E, G (except    E, R, S, U
                                 when INCEX_FLAG =  
                                 'E'), U            

  SAFS       S                   B, E, G (except    E, R, S, U
                                 when INCEX_FLAG =  
                                 'E'), U            
  --------------------------------------------------------------------

## CSCL Source Components for SAF Data

The ETL tool will generate SAF output records from certain features or
table entries in four CSCL database components, depending on the
SAFTYPE, as shown in Table 27. Certain output fields will be obtained
from related CSCL components, such as the StreetName and FeatureName
tables and the RoadbedPointerList table.

[]{#_Ref222718829 .anchor}Table 27 -- CSCL Source Components for SAF
Data

+------------------+--------------------------+
| **SAFTYPEs**     | **CSCL Source            |
|                  | Component**              |
+==================+==========================+
| I                | NamedIntersection table  |
+------------------+--------------------------+
| A, B, C, D, E,   | AltSegmentData table SAF |
| O, P             | entries (see             |
|                  |                          |
|                  | Table 13                 |
|                  |                          |
|                  | )                        |
+------------------+--------------------------+
| G, N, X          | CommonPlace feature      |
|                  | class                    |
+------------------+--------------------------+
| S, V             | AddressPoint feature     |
|                  | class                    |
+------------------+--------------------------+

### Use of the Roadbed Pointer List

With respect to the extraction of SAF record types A, B, C, D, E, O and
P, the AltSegmentData table includes the generic and roadbed entries
that are needed to produce the required records for both the generic and
roadbed versions of the respective SAF output files.

In the CommonPlace and AddressPoint feature classes, the SAF type G, N,
S, V and X data associated with divided street segments point only to
roadbed segments or proto-segments coincident with roadbed segments. To
produce the required generic output records for record types G, N, S, V
and X, the ETL tool will access the CSCL RoadbedPointerList table to
obtain the SEGMENTID of the corresponding generic segment or
proto-segment, and will then access that generic segment in the
Centerline feature class or proto-segment in the AltSegmentData table to
obtain certain data items required to construct the output generic SAF
record, such as the generic segment's or proto-segment's Sequence
Number.

RPL access is not required for Type G, N and X records that pertain to
non-Centerline features.

### Normalized Names in SAF Records

All of the SAF record types have a field for a name as the first 32
bytes of the record. Depending on the record type, the name is a street
name, a place name or an intersection name. The name is required to be
in a Geosupport System normalized format called the "Sort Format".

All output SAF name fields will be populated by obtaining the name from
the field LOOKUP_KEY in the appropriate entry in the StreetName table or
FeatureName table, and converting the contents of that field into the
Sort Format as described in detail in Note 1 to Table 20.

the layout shown in Table 28.

                    N                                                                      none

  [SAFA21]{.mark}   [Side borough code X, G or    [1]{.mark}   [120]{.mark}   [120]{.mark} [blanks if
                    N]{.mark}                                                              none]{.mark}

  [SAFA22]{.mark}   [Side CT2010 X,G or N         [6]{.mark}   [121]{.mark}   [126]{.mark} [Same format as
                    (XXXXYY)]{.mark}                                                       Geo-support
                                                                                           Lion]{.mark}

  [SAFA23]{.mark}   [Side AP for X,G or           [3]{.mark}   [127]{.mark}   [129]{.mark} [RJZF, blanks if
                    N]{.mark}                                                              none]{.mark}
  ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This section discusses the generation of SAF Type A, B, C, E and P
records. Section 7.4 discusses Types G, N and X.

SAF Type A, B, C, E and P records are extracted from the entries in the
AltSegmentData table having those SAFTYPE values. The output records
will be written into the generic SAFA file, the roadbed SAFA file or
both, depending on the SEGMENT_TYPE of the appurtenant Centerline
segment, in accordance with the rules in Table 26.

Table 29 contains a list of the fields in the SAFA Type A, B, C, E and P
output records, along with the CSCL source of data for populating each
field. The source for most of the fields is the AltSegmentData entry
from which the given output record is being generated, as indicated in
the last column in Table 29. The sources for other output fields are
described in the notes below Table 29.

[]{#_Ref222719506 .anchor}Table 29 -- Populating SAF Record Types A, B,
C, E and P

  --------------------------------------------------------------------
  **FIC**   **Field**             **CSCL Source of Data**
  --------- --------------------- ------------------------------------
  SAFA1     Special Address       Except for type C records, obtained
            Street Name or        from StreetName table -- see Note 1.
            Neighborhood Name or  For type C records, populate with
            Addressable Place     the value '75 STREET'.
            Name                  

  SAFA2     Borough               AltSegmentData field BOROUGH

  SAFA3     Face Code             Obtained from bytes 2 through 5 of
                                  AltSegmentData LIONKEY field

  SAFA4     Sequence Number       Obtained from bytes 6 through 10 of
                                  AltSegmentData LIONKEY field

  SAFA5     SOS Indicator         AltSegmentData field SOS_INDICATOR
                                  -- see Note 2

  SAFA6     B5SC                  AltSegmentData field B5SC

  SAFA7     Left Low HN           AltSegmentData field L_LOW_HN

            Filler                N/A

  SAFA8     Left High HN          AltSegmentData field L_HIGH_HN

            Filler                N/A

  SAFA9     Right Low HN          AltSegmentData field R_LOW_HN

            Filler                N/A

  SAFA10    Right High HN         AltSegmentData field R_HIGH_HN

            Filler                N/A

  SAFA11    SAF Record Type Code  AltSegmentData field SAFTYPE

            Filler                N/A

  SAFA12    LGC1                  AltSegmentData field LGC1

  SAFA13    LGC2                  AltSegmentData field LGC2

  SAFA14    LGC3                  AltSegmentData field LGC3

  SAFA15    LGC4                  AltSegmentData field LGC4

**[NOTES TO Table 29:]{.underline}**

1.  SAFA1 (Street Name): For type C records, the ETL Tool will be
    "hard-coded" to populate this field with '75 STREET'. For types A,
    B, E and P records, this field will be populated with the preferred
    street name in the Geosupport Sort Format. It will be obtained from
    the LOOKUP_KEY field in the pertinent StreetName or FeatureName
    table entry as follows.

    a.  The AltSegmentData fields B5SC and LGC1 will be concatenated to
        form the Preferred B7SC. (**ASSUMPTION**: the AltSegmentData
        field LGC1 always contains the Preferred LGC.)

    b.  StreetName will be accessed with a composite key consisting of
        the Preferred B7SC and PRINCIPAL_FLAG = 'Y'.

    c.  If the StreetName access fails, FeatureName will be accessed
        with the same key. If that is successful, a warning message will
        be issued.

    d.  If one of the name table accesses is successful, the contents of
        LOOKUP_KEY from that table entry will be converted to Sort
        Format as described in Note 1 to Table 20 and then populated
        into SAFA1.

    e.  If neither name table access is successful, SAFA1 will be
        populated with blanks and an error message will be issued.

    f.  [Street name in the first 32 characters should be in sort
        format, but spaces before & after dash or slash should be
        removed. To treat anything with a dash or slash as an alphabetic
        word, not numeric even beginning with number. The same changes
        also apply to SND & exception table.]{.mark}

2.  SAFA5 (SOS Indicator): If AltSegmentData field SOS_INDICATOR = '1',
    SAFA5 will be populated with 'L'. If SOS_INDICATOR = '2', SAFA5 will
    be populated with 'R'. Otherwise, SAFA5 will be populated with a
    blank.

3.  SAFA17 (Segment Type Code): This field will be populated with the
    value of the appurtenant Centerline segment's SEGMENT_TYPE
    attribute.

4.  Filler: This 14-byte filler corresponds to fields SAFA19 and SAFA20,
    which are populated with spatial coordinates only for type G, N and
    X records. For type A, B, C, E and P records, this filler field will
    be populated with blanks. The purpose of the filler is to preserve
    the shared layout that has existed between type A, B, C, E and P
    records and type G, N and X records.

## Type D Records

Table 30 contains a layout of the SAF Type D output records. The last
column in the table and the notes immediately following the table
indicate the CSCL source of data for populating each output field.

SAF Type D data are extracted from the Type D and F entries in the
AltSegmentData table. Those entries are identified by the values 'D' and
'F' in the field SAFTYPE. Note that, although AltSegmentData contains
SAF entries identified as Type F, their SAF Type will be changed to 'D'
in the extracted SAF output file.

Type D output records will be written into the generic SAFD file, the
roadbed SAFD file or both, depending on the SEGMENT_TYPE of the
appurtenant Centerline segment, in accordance with the rules in Table
26.

**[NOTES TO Table 30:]{.underline}**

1.  SAFD1 (Street Name): This field will be populated with the primary
    name of the given Duplicate Address Pseudo-Street name (DAPS) in
    Geosupport Sort Format. It will be obtained by accessing the
    LOOKUP_KEY field in the pertinent StreetName table entry with a
    composite key consisting of the B5SC from the AltSegmentData entry
    and PRIMARY_FLAG = 'Y'. The contents of LOOKUP_KEY in that entry
    will be converted to Sort Format as described in Note 1 to Table 20.

2.  SAFD5 (SOS Indicator): If AltSegmentData field SOS_INDICATOR = '1',
    SAFD5 will be populated with 'L'. If SOS_INDICATOR = '2', SAFD5 will
    be populated with 'R'. Otherwise, SAFD5 will be populated with a
    blank.

3.  SAFD7 (Low HN) and SAFD8 (High HN): SAF Type D records contain only
    a single address range, which corresponds to either the left side or
    the right side of the appurtenant segment, as indicated by the SOS
    Indicator in the AltSegmentData SAF entry. In the AltSegmentData
    entry for a Type D SAF record, the house number fields for the side
    indicated by the SOS Indicator contain the given address range, and
    the house number fields for the other side of the segment are null.
    SAFD7 and SAFD8 will be populated from the non-null AltSegmentData
    low and high house number fields, respectively.

4.  SAFD9 (Regular B5SC)[^2]: The ETL program will be hard-coded to
    populate SAFD9 based on the value that is populated into SAFD6 as
    specified in the list below. For the SAFD6 value listed in the first
    column, the ETL program will populate SAFD9 with the value in the
    third column. (Street names are shown for reference purposes only.)
    If the SAFD6 value does not appear in the below list, the ETL tool
    will issue an error message and will not write an output record.

> Hard-coding for SAFD9 is necessary because the appropriate value is
> not necessarily the B5SC stored in Segment_LGC. A Centerline segment
> that has an associated SAF type D record might also have one or more
> type B records, which by definition contain alternative B5SC values
> applicable to the segment. The appropriate value for populating SAFD9
> might be one of those values or it might be the B5SC in Segment_LGC.
> The ETL program has no means to make that determination.
>
> **In the future, if the street codes assigned to any of the street
> names in the above list are changed, or if SAF type D or F
> AltSegmentData entries are created for any additional streets, the ETL
> program hard-coding will have to be modified accordingly.**

5.  SAFD12 (DAPS Type): If the AltSegmentData field SAFTYPE contains an
    'F', SAFD12 will be populated with the value '1' (signifying a
    "pseudo-DAPS"). If it contains a 'D', SAFD12 will be populated with
    a blank.

6.  SAFD13 (Segment Type Code): This field will be populated with the
    value of the appurtenant Centerline segment's SEGMENT_TYPE
    attribute. (Note that if the SAF record pertains to a proto-segment,
    the SEGMENT_TYPE attribute of the Centerline segment applies to that
    proto-segment also.)

## Type G, N and X Records

Output SAF type G, N and X records are written for each feature in the
CSCL CommonPlace feature class for which the SAFTYPE attribute field
contains a 'G', 'N' or 'X' and the B7SC field is populated with a value
other than NULL or blanks, [and "Security_level" isn't "Publis Safety
Agency]{.mark}". No SAF records are written out for other CommonPlace
features. In addition, if the SAFTYPE = 'G', 'N' or 'X' but the B7SC is
NULL or blanks, an error message is issued.

The output records are written into the generic SAFA file, the roadbed
SAFA file or both, depending on whether the CommonPlace feature pertains
to a Centerline or Shoreline segment, and if the former, depending on
the SEGMENT_TYPE, in accordance with the rules in Table 26.

When writing type G, N and X records into the generic SAFA file, if the
SEGMENTID attribute of the CommonPlace feature identifies a roadbed
segment or proto-segment, the ETL program will access the RPL as
described in Section 7.1.1 to obtain the SEGMENTID of the corresponding
generic (or combined generic and roadbed) segment or proto-segment. As
detailed in the notes to Table 31, the ETL program will then populate
the output fields SAFA3, SAFA4, SAFA17 and SAFA18 with the values of
these items that pertain to the generic segment or proto-segment instead
of to the roadbed segment or proto-segment.

Table 31 contains a layout of the Type G, N and X output records. (It is
the same layout as for Type A, B, C and E records, but the CSCL data
sources and the contents of some of the output fields are different.)
The sources for populating the fields in a Type G, N or X output record
are indicated in the last column in Table 31 and in the notes below the
table. For most of the fields, the attribute data of the CommonPlace
feature from which the given output record is being generated will serve
as the source data for both the roadbed output file and the generic
output file.

  --------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **FIC**           **Field**              **CSCL Source of Data**
  ----------------- ---------------------- ---------------------------------------
  SAFA1             Place Name             Obtained from FeatureName table - see
                                           Note 1

  SAFA2             Borough                CommonPlace attribute BOROUGHCODE

  SAFA3             Face Code              See Note 2

  SAFA4             Sequence Number        See Note 2

  SAFA5             SOS Indicator          CommonPlace attribute SOSINDICATOR --
                                           see Note 3

  SAFA6             B5SC of NAP            First 6 bytes of CommonPlace attribute
                                           B7SC

  SAFA7             Left Low HN            Populate with blanks -- see Note 4

                    Filler                 Populate with blanks

  SAFA8             Left High HN           See Note 5

                    Filler                 Populate with blanks

  SAFA9             Right Low HN           Populate with blanks -- see Note 4

                    Filler                 Populate with blanks

  SAFA10            Right High HN          See Note 5

                    Filler                 Populate with blanks

  SAFA11            SAF Record Type Code   CommonPlace attribute SAFTYPE

                    Filler                 Populate with blanks

  SAFA12            LGC1 of NAP            Populate with the 7th and 8th bytes of
                                           CommonPlace attribute B7SC

  SAFA13            LGC2 of NAP            Populate with blanks -- see Note 6

  SAFA14            LGC3 of NAP            Populate with blanks -- see Note 6

  SAFA15            LGC4 of NAP            Populate with blanks -- see Note 6

  SAFA16            Pointer to BOE         Populate with the value '1'
                    Preferred LGC          

  SAFA17            Segment Type Code      See Note 7

  SAFA18            Segment ID             See Note 8

  SAFA19            X Coordinate of Place  Populate with X coordinate of
                                           CommonPlace point rounded to nearest
                                           whole integer

  SAFA20            Y Coordinate of Place  Populate with Y coordinate of
                                           CommonPlace point rounded to nearest
                                           integer

  [SAFA21]{.mark}   [Side borough          [Blank if none]{.mark}
                    code]{.mark}           

  [SAFA22]{.mark}   [Side CT2010           [Same format as Geo-support
                    (XXXXYY)]{.mark}       Lion]{.mark}

  [SAFA23]{.mark}   [Side AP]{.mark}       [RJZF, blanks if none]{.mark}
  --------------------------------------------------------------------------------

  : []{#_Ref222719783 .anchor}Table 31 -- Populating SAF Type G, N and X
  Records

**[NOTES TO Table 31:]{.underline}**

1.  SAFA1 (Place Name): This field will be populated with the preferred
    name of the given Non-Addressable Place name (NAP) in Geosupport
    Sort Format. It will be obtained from the LOOKUP_KEY field in the
    pertinent FeatureName or StreetName table entry. The ETL program
    will query FeatureName first (since the great majority of SAF type
    G, N and X names are in FeatureName). If not found in FeatureName,
    the program will try StreetName. If not found in either table, the
    program will not write out an output record, and will issue an error
    message. The given name table will be accessed using a composite key
    consisting of the CommonPlace field B7SC combined with setting the
    FeatureName or StreetName field PRINCIPAL_FLAG to 'Y'. The contents
    of LOOKUP_KEY in that entry will be converted to Sort Format as
    described in Note 1 to Table 20 and then populated into SAFA1.

2.  SAFA3 (Face Code) and SAFA4 (Sequence Number): These fields will be
    populated with the Face Code and Sequence Number of the appropriate
    segment or proto-segment. In general, that is the segment or
    proto-segment identified by the SEGMENTID attribute of the
    CommonPlace feature. However, when the generic output file is being
    generated, if that segment or proto-segment is a roadbed feature,
    the appropriate segment from which to obtain the Face Code and
    Sequence Number is the corresponding generic segment or
    proto-segment, as explained below.

    a.  [When generating the roadbed output file]{.underline}, and when
        generating the generic output file in cases in which the
        SEGMENTID of the CommonPlace feature identifies a segment or
        proto-segment that is not a roadbed, then that segment or
        proto-segment is the one to which the SAF record pertains and
        whose Face Code and Sequence Number are to be used. In these
        cases, determining values for fields SAFA3 and SAFA4 is more
        complicated for Type G, N and X records than for the SAF record
        types that are generated from the AltSegmentData table, since
        unlike that table, the CommonPlace feature class does not
        contain a LIONKEY field from which to extract the Face Code and
        Sequence Number. The segment appurtenant to an SAF Type G, N or
        X record might be a street segment or a shoreline segment. In
        addition, if the appurtenant segment happens to be a coincident
        segment, it might be stored in the CSCL database as a
        geometry-represented segment or as a proto-segment. In view of
        these facts, the ETL tool will obtain the appropriate Face Code
        and Sequence Number via the following steps:

        1.  Determine whether the SEGMENTID attribute of the CommonPlace
            feature identifies a Centerline segment. (The overwhelming
            majority of Type G, N and X SAF records pertain to street
            segments rather than to shorelines. Therefore, it is more
            efficient for the ETL program to search the Centerline
            feature class first.)

        2.  If there is such a Centerline segment, examine the attribute
            field COINCIDENT_SEG_COUNT. If that field contains an
            integer greater than 1, the segment might have a
            corresponding proto-segment (an entry in the AltSegmentData
            table with the same SEGMENTID and with ALT_SEGDATA_TYPE not
            null (signifying a coincident segment entry rather than an
            SAF entry)).

> If there is a corresponding proto-segment, it is either a borough
> boundary proto-segment or a boundary continuity proto-segment. (SAF
> data never pertain to ramps.) The ETL tool must determine the
> appropriate entity (either the geometry-represented segment or the
> proto-segment) from which to obtain the Face Code and Sequence Number
> as follows:
>
> [If the proto-segment is a borough boundary segment]{.underline}
> (ALT_SEGDATA_TYPE = 'B'): use the entity that has the same Borough
> Code as the SAF record as the source of the data.
>
> [If the proto-segment is a boundary continuity segment]{.underline}
> (ALT_SEGDATA_TYPE = 'C'): the appropriate source is necessarily the
> geometry-represented segment. Boundary continuity proto-segments are
> non-physical features and never have SAF data.
>
> [If there is no proto-segment, or if there is one but the appropriate
> source for the Face Code and Sequence Number is the
> geometry-represented segment]{.underline}, the Sequence Number will be
> obtained from the geometry-represented segment's SEGMENT_SEQNUM
> attribute, and the Face Code will be obtained by accessing the
> Segment_LGC table by SEGMENTID, then accessing the StreetName table by
> the Preferred B7SC and PRINCIPAL_FLAG = 'Y' in the usual manner. If
> StreetName contains no entry satisfying these search criteria, or the
> entry does exist but it does not contain a Face Code value, the ETL
> tool will not write out an output record and will issue an error
> message.
>
> If the appropriate source is the proto-segment, the Face Code and
> Sequence Number will be obtained from byte positions 2 through 5 and
> positions 6 through 10, respectively, of the LIONKEY field in the
> proto-segment's AltSegmentData entry. If either of those items is not
> an integer value \> 0, the ETL tool will not write out an output
> record and will issue an error message.

3.  If there is no Centerline segment whose SEGMENTID attribute equals
    that of the given CommonPlace feature, there should be such a
    segment in the Shoreline feature class. If so, that segment's
    SEGMENT_SEQNUM attribute will be used to populate SAFA4, and SAFA3
    will be populated with the Face Code obtained by accessing the
    Segment_LGC table by SEGMENTID, then accessing the FeatureName table
    by the Preferred B7SC and PRINCIPAL_FLAG = 'Y' in the usual manner.

4.  If there is neither a Centerline segment nor a Shoreline segment
    having the SEGMENTID of the CommonPlace feature, the tool will treat
    that as an error condition in the usual manner (it will not write
    out an output record, and will issue an error message). All SAF
    records (other than type I records) [must]{.underline} be
    appurtenant to a valid street segment or shoreline segment and
    therefore must contain a valid LION Key.

<!-- -->

b.  [When generating the generic output file in cases in which the
    SEGMENTID of the CommonPlace feature identifies a roadbed segment,
    the appurtenant segment is]{.underline} the generic segment or
    proto-segment that corresponds to that roadbed segment. Its
    SEGMENTID is obtained from the RPL as discussed in Section 7.1.1. In
    this case, SAFA3 and SAFA4 will be populated as follows:

    1.  [SAFA3 will be populated with the Face Code of the generic
        segment or proto-segment, which will be obtained as
        follows.]{.underline}

- [If the generic feature is represented by a (geometry-modeled)
  Centerline segment, the Segment_LGC table will be accessed by the
  combination of the generic SEGMENTID and PREFERRED_FLAG = 'Y'. The
  B5SC and LGC from that Segment_LGC entry will be concatenated to form
  the preferred B7SC. Since the related segment belongs to a divided
  street, this B7SC should appear in the StreetName table rather than
  FeatureName. StreetName will be accessed by the combination of the
  preferred B7SC and PRINCIPAL_FLAG = 'Y' to retrieve the Face Code of
  the generic segment.]{.underline} If StreetName contains no entry
  satisfying these search criteria, or the entry does exist but it does
  not contain a Face Code value, the ETL tool will not write out an
  output record and will issue an error message.

- [If the generic feature is represented by a proto-segment, the Face
  Code will be obtained from the second through fifth bytes of the
  LIONKEY field in that proto-segment's AltSegmentData
  entry.]{.underline} If either of those items is not an integer value
  \> 0, the ETL tool will not write out an output record and will issue
  an error message.

  1.  [SAFA4 will be populated]{.underline} with the Sequence Number
      obtained from the generic segment or proto-segment, accessed by
      the generic SEGMENTID, as follows.

<!-- -->

- [If the generic feature is represented by a Centerline segment, the
  Sequence Number will be obtained from that segment's SEGMENT_SEQNUM
  attribute.]{.underline}

- [If the generic feature is represented by a proto-segment, the
  Sequence Number will be obtained from the six through tenth bytes of
  the LIONKEY field in that proto-segment's AltSegmentData
  entry.]{.underline} If that item is not an integer value \> 0, the ETL
  tool will not write out an output record and will issue an error
  message.

3.  SAFA5 (SOS Indicator): If CommonPlace field SOS_INDICATOR = '1',
    SAFA5 will be populated with 'L'. If SOS_INDICATOR = '2', SAFA5 will
    be populated with 'R'. Otherwise, SAFA5 will be populated with a
    blank.

4.  SAFA7 (Left Low HN) and SAFA9 (Right Low HN): The ETL tool will
    populate these fields with blanks. Note that the GRID Generation
    System populates the Low HN field for the side identified by the SOS
    Indicator with a value.

5.  SAFA8 (Left High HN) and SAFA10 (Right High HN): The High HN field
    for the side identified by the SOS Indicator is intended to be
    populated with the house number of an "underlying address" for the
    given place name, if one is known. The CommonPlace feature class has
    an attribute called PRIMARYADDRESSPOINTID, which contains an
    ADDRESSPOINTID value if an underlying address for the place name is
    known. If PRIMARYADDRESSPOINTID does not contain a value, the ETL
    tool will populate the High HN field with blanks. If
    PRIMARYADDRESSPOINTID does contain a value, the ETL tool will use it
    to retrieve the feature in the AddressPoint feature class whose
    ADDRESSPOINTID attribute equals the given PRIMARYADDRESSPOINTID
    value, and will populate the High HN field for the side identified
    by the SOS Indicator as follows:

- If the HYPHEN_TYPE attribute of the address point contains the value
  'R', the address point's HOUSE_NUMBER attribute contains a range of
  unhyphenated house numbers expressed in the form of the low house
  number of the range followed by a dash followed by the high house
  number of the range. (Note: there might or might not be spaces between
  the dash and the digits to the left and/or right of the dash. For
  example, the data in HOUSE_NUMBER might appear as '22-28' or as '22 --
  28'.) The ETL tool will populate SAFA8 or SAFA10 (whichever of these
  output fields corresponds to the side identified by the SOS Indicator)
  with the low-address portion of the range (the string of digits to the
  left of the dash) only (after reformatting that house number into the
  special Edgewater Park format if required, as explained below); the
  dash and the digits to the right of the dash will not be used.

- If the HYPHEN_TYPE attribute of the address point contains any value
  other than 'R', the ETL tool will populate SAFA8 or SAFA10 with the
  value in the address point's HOUSE_NUMBER field without modification
  (except possibly for reformatting the house number into the special
  Edgewater Park format if required, as explained below).

- Note that the SAF output record layout for SAF types including G, N
  and X does not include fields for house number suffixes. Therefore, if
  the underlying house number has a suffix stored in the address point
  feature, the ETL tool will not utilize it (except to determine whether
  the address is in Edgewater Park), but will output only the basic
  house number component (reformatted into the special Edgewater Park
  format if necessary).

- Edgewater Park is a neighborhood in the Bronx that has unique house
  number formatting requirements. If the underlying address is an
  Edgewater Park address, the ETL tool will reformat it from the
  "real-world format" in which it is stored in the CSCL AddressPoint
  feature class into the "special Edgewater Park format" in which such
  house numbers are stored in other CSCL components and in LION. In the
  real-world format, the house number includes an Edgewater Park section
  suffix, which is a letter of the alphabet from 'A' to 'E'. In the
  special Edgewater Park format, the section letter is dropped (which is
  not relevant to the creation of SAF type G, N and X output records,
  since they contain no suffixes) and a corresponding multiple of 10,000
  is added to the house number. For example, if the section letter is
  'A', 10,000 (= 1 X 10,000) is added; if it is 'B', 20,000 (= 2 X
  10,000) is added, etc. The ETL tool will process the address point as
  follows:

  a.  If the SND_FEATURE_TYPE = 'E' in the principal StreetName entry
      for the B7SC_ACTUAL attribute of the address point, the address is
      in Edgewater Park. In that case, the HOUSE_NUMBER_SUFFIX attribute
      of the address point should contain an Edgewater Park section
      letter, either by itself or following some other suffix value and
      a dash (for example, '½ - B').

<!-- -->

- If it does not contain a section letter, the ETL tool will issue a
  warning including an appropriate message (e.g., "Underlying address is
  in Edgewater Park but has no letter suffix; field has been left
  blank"), and will populate both output fields SAFA8 and SAFA10 with
  blanks.

- If it does contain a section letter, the ETL tool will add the
  appropriate multiple of 10,000 to the house number.

  a.  If the SND_FEATURE_TYPE = 'F', the street is partially inside
      Edgewater Park and partially outside it. If HOUSE_NUMBER_SUFFIX
      does not contain a section letter, the address will be assumed to
      lie outside of Edgewater Park; in that case, the tool will not
      issue a warning and it will not perform the special Edgewater Park
      reformatting. If it does contain a section letter, either by
      itself or following some other suffix value and a dash, the ETL
      tool will assume the address is within Edgewater Park; in that
      case, it will add the corresponding multiple of 10,000 to the
      house number.

6.  SAFA13 (LGC2), SAFA14 (LGC3) and SAFA15 (LGC4): All NAPs have only a
    single LGC value. DCP has stated its intention to continue adhering
    to that rule. The ETL tool will populate these fields with blanks.
    In the future, if any NAP should ever be assigned more than one LGC
    value, the ETL tool will have to be modified accordingly.

7.  SAFA17 (Segment Type Code):

    a.  If the CommonPlace feature pertains to a Centerline segment:

        1.  

        2.  For the roadbed output file, and for the generic output file
            when the SEGMENTID of the CommonPlace feature identifies a
            non-roadbed segment or proto-segment, SAFA17 [will be
            populated from the SEGMENT_TYPE attribute of the Centerline
            segment.]{.underline}

        3.  For the generic output file when the SEGMENTID of the
            CommonPlace feature identifies a roadbed segment, SAFA17
            will be populated from the SEGMENT_TYPE attribute of the
            corresponding generic Centerline segment.

    b.  If the CommonPlace feature pertains to a Shoreline segment,
        SAFA17 will be populated with the value 'U'.

8.  SAFA18 (Segment ID):

    a.  For the roadbed output file, and for the generic output file
        when the SEGMENTID attribute of the CommonPlace feature
        identifies a non-roadbed segment (including a Shoreline
        segment), SAFA18 will be populated with the SEGMENTID attribute
        of the CommonPlace feature.

    b.  For the generic output file when the SEGMENTID of the
        CommonPlace feature identifies a roadbed segment, SAFA18 will be
        populated with the corresponding generic SEGMENTID, obtained
        from the RPL.

## Type I Records

One output SAF Type I record is written into the SAFI output file for
each entry in the CSCL NamedIntersection table. Table 32 contains a
layout of the SAF Type I output records. The last column in the table
indicates the CSCL source of data for populating each output field.

[]{#_Ref222718650 .anchor}Table 32 -- Layout and Populating Rules for
SAF Record Type I

  --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **FIC**   **Field**            **Len**   **Frm**   **To** **Format**   **CSCL Source of
                                                                         Data**
  --------- ------------------ --------- --------- -------- ------------ ---------------------
  SAFI1     Primary                   32         1       32 LJSF         See Note 1
            Intersection Name                                            

  SAFI2     Node ID                    7        33       39 RJZF         NamedIntersection
                                                                         field NODEID

            Filler                    13        40       52              N/A

  SAFI3     Multiple Field             1        53       53 M or blank   NamedIntersection
                                                                         field MULTIPLEFIELD
                                                                         -- see Note 2

  SAFI4     B7SC of                    8        54       61              NamedIntersection
            Intersection Name                                            field B7SC

  SAFI5     B5SC of One Cross          6        62       67              NamedIntersection
            Street                                                       field B5SC_CROSS1

  SAFI6     B5SC of Other              6        68       73              NamedIntersection
            Cross Street                                                 field B5SC_CROSS2

            Filler                    12        74       85              N/A

  SAFI7     SAF Record Type            1        86       86              'I'
            Code                                                         

            Filler                    12        87       98              N/A
  --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**[NOTES TO Table 32:]{.underline}**

1.  SAFI1 (Primary Intersection Name): This field will be populated with
    the intersection name in Geosupport Sort Format, It will be obtained
    from the LOOKUP_KEY field of the pertinent StreetName table entry
    via a composite key consisting of the B7SC of the Intersection Name
    and the PRINCIPAL_FLAG = 'Y'. The contents of LOOKUP_KEY in that
    entry will be converted to Sort Format as described in Note 1 to
    Table 20.

2.  SAFI3 (Multiple Field): If the NamedIntersection field MULTIPLEFIELD
    contains a 'Y', the ETL tool will populate SAFI3 with the value 'M'.
    Otherwise, it will populate it with a blank.

## Type O Records

SAF Type O records are extracted from the entries in the AltSegmentData
table for which SAFTYPE contains an 'O'. The output records are written
into the generic SAFV file, the roadbed SAFV file or both, depending on
the SEGMENT_TYPE of the appurtenant Centerline segment, in accordance
with the rules in Table 26.

Table 33 contains a list of the fields in the SAF Type O output records.
The CSCL source for populating each field is indicated in the last
column in Table 33 and in the note below the table.

[]{#_Ref222718465 .anchor}Table 33 -- Layout and Populating Rules for
SAF Record Type O

  -----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **FIC**   **Field**        **Len**   **Frm**   **To** **Format**   **CSCL Source of
                                                                     Data**
  --------- -------------- --------- --------- -------- ------------ ----------------------
  SAFV1     Street Name           32         1       32 LJSF         Obtained from
                                                                     StreetName table --
                                                                     see Note 1

  SAFV2     Borough Code           1        33       33 1, 2, 3, 4   AltSegmentData field
                                                        or 5         BOROUGH

  SAFV3     Face Code of           4        34       37 RJZF         Obtained from bytes 2
            Actual Segment                                           through 5 of
                                                                     AltSegmentData LIONKEY
                                                                     field

  SAFV4     Sequence               5        38       42 RJZF         Obtained from bytes 6
            Number of                                                through 10 of
            Actual Segment                                           AltSegmentData LIONKEY
                                                                     field

  SAFV5     SOS Indicator          1        43       43 L, R or      AltSegmentData field
            for Actual                                  blank        SOS_INDICATOR -- see
            Segment                                                  Note 2

  SAFV6     B5SC                   6        44       49              AltSegmentData field
                                                                     B5SC

  SAFV7     Low HN Basic           7        50       56 RJSF         Obtained from
                                                                     AltSegmentData field

                                                                     depending on value of
                                                                     SOS_INDICATOR

  SAFV8     Low HN Suffix          9        57       65 RJSF         AltSegmentData field
                                                                     LOW_HN_SUFFIX

            Filler                 2        66       67              N/A

  SAFV9     High HN Basic          7        68       74 RJSF         Obtained from
                                                                     AltSegmentData field
                                                                     L_HIGH_HN or R_HIGH_HN
                                                                     depending on value of
                                                                     SOS_INDICATOR

  SAFV10    High HN Suffix         9        75       83 RJSF         AltSegmentData field
                                                                     HIGH_HN_SUFFIX

            Filler                 2        84       85              N/A

  SAFV11    SAF Record             1        86       86              AltSegmentData field
            Type Code                                                SAFTYPE

            Filler                 2        87       88              N/A

  SAFV12    LGC1                   2        89       90 RJZF         AltSegmentData field
                                                                     LGC1

  SAFV13    LGC2                   2        91       92 RJZF, blanks AltSegmentData field
                                                        if none      LGC2

  SAFV14    LGC3                   2        93       94 RJZF, blanks AltSegmentData field
                                                        if none      LGC3

  SAFV15    LGC4                   2        95       96 RJZF, blanks AltSegmentData field
                                                        if none      LGC4

  SAFV16    Pointer to BOE         1        97       97              AltSegmentData field
            Preferred LGC                                            BOE_PREFERRED_LGC\_
                                                                     FLAG

  SAFV17    Segment Type           1        98       98              SEGMENT_TYPE attribute
            Code                                                     of appurtenant
                                                                     (actual) Centerline
                                                                     segment

  SAFV18    Segment ID of          7        99      105 RJZF         AltSegmentData field
            Actual Segment                                           SEGMENTID

  SAFV19    X Coordinate           7       106      112              Populate with blanks.
                                                                     (Field is used only
                                                                     for type V records.)

  SAFV20    Y Coordinate           7       113      119              Populate with blanks.
                                                                     (Field is used only
                                                                     for type V records.)
  -----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**[NOTES To Table 33:]{.underline}**

1.  SAFV1 (Street Name): this field will be populated with the preferred
    street name in Geosupport Sort Format. It will be obtained from the
    LOOKUP_KEY field in the pertinent StreetName table entry as follows.
    The AltSegmentData fields B5SC and LGC1 will be concatenated to form
    the Preferred B7SC. (**ASSUMPTION**: the AltSegmentData field LGC1
    always contains the Preferred LGC.) StreetName will then be accessed
    with a composite key to retrieve the entry that contains the
    Preferred B7SC and in which the StreetName field PRINCIPAL_FLAG =
    'Y'. The contents of LOOKUP_KEY in that entry will be converted to
    Sort Format as described in Note 1 to Table 20.

2.  SAFV5 (SOS Indicator): If AltSegmentData field SOS_INDICATOR = '1',
    SAFV5 will be populated with 'L'. If SOS_INDICATOR = '2', SAFV5 will
    be populated with 'R'. Otherwise, SAFV5 will be populated with a
    blank.

## Type S Records

SAF Type S records are extracted from the AddressPoint feature class.
Output records are written for each address point for which the
SPECIAL_CONDITION attribute contains the value 'S'. An output record is
written into the generic SAFS file, the roadbed SAFS file or both,
depending on the SEGMENT_TYPE of the appurtenant Centerline segment, in
accordance with the rules in Table 26. (Note: AltSegmentData does not
have a field for SEGMENT_TYPE. Instead, proto-segments implicitly have
the same SEGMENT_TYPE as their corresponding geometry-represented
segments. Therefore, if a type S record pertains to a proto-segment, the
SEGMENT_TYPE value of the corresponding Centerline segment will be used
for purposes of applying the Table 26 rules, as well as to populate
output field SAFS15.)

Table 34 contains a list of the fields in the SAF Type S output records.
The CSCL source of data for populating each field is indicated in the
last column in Table 34 and in the notes below the table.

**[NOTES TO Table 34:]{.underline}**

1.  SAFS1 (Street Name) and SAFS3 (Face Code): These fields will be
    populated, respectively, with the preferred street name in
    Geosupport Sort Format and the Face Code corresponding to the
    preferred street name. Both items will be obtained from the
    pertinent StreetName table entry, from the fields LOOKUP_KEY and
    FACECODE, respectively. The table will be accessed using a composite
    key consisting of the AddressPoint attribute B7SC_ACTUAL combined
    with setting the StreetName field PRINCIPAL_FLAG to 'Y'. SAFS1 will
    be populated by converting the contents of LOOKUP_KEY in that
    StreetName entry to Sort Format as described in Note 1 to Table 20.

> [When the B7SC_actuak doesn't have a face code, the lion key should be
> generated from the face code and sequence number of the segment that
> the address point is associated to.]{.mark}
>
> If StreetName contains no entry satisfying these search criteria,
> ~~[or the entry does exist but it does not contain a Face Code
> value,]{.mark}~~ the ETL tool will not write out an output record and
> will issue an error message.
>
> (Note: the B7SC_ACTUAL field in a type S address point contains the
> preferred B7SC value of the segment. Since the preferred B7SC of every
> roadbed segment is the one assigned to the generic name of the street
> (and DCP has stated its intention to continue adhering to that rule),
> the use of the B7SC_ACTUAL value to obtain the street name and Face
> Code as described above is valid even when the appurtenant segment is
> a roadbed segment and the record is being written into the generic
> output file.)

2.  SAFS4 (Sequence Number), SAFS15 (Segment Type Code) and SAFS16
    (Segment ID): These fields will be populated as follows:

    a.  If the Centerline segment identified by the type S address
        point's SEGMENTID is a non-roadbed segment (SEGMENT_TYPE not =
        'R') regardless of the output file, or if it is a roadbed
        segment and the output record is being written into the roadbed
        output file:

- SAFS15 and SAFS16 will be populated with the SEGMENT_TYPE and
  SEGMENTID of the Centerline segment, respectively.

- If the BOROUGHCODE fields of the type S address point and the
  Centerline segment are equal, the address point pertains to the
  Centerline segment. SAFS4 will be populated from the SEGMENT_SEQNUM
  attribute of the Centerline segment.

- If the BOROUGHCODE fields of the type S address point and the
  Centerline segment are not equal, the address point pertains to a
  borough boundary proto-segment having the given SEGMENTID. SAFS4 will
  be populated from the ALT_SEGMENT_SEQNUM field of the proto-segment's
  AltSegmentData entry.

  a.  For the generic output file only, if the Centerline segment
      identified by the type S address point's SEGMENTID is a roadbed
      segment:

<!-- -->

- The SEGMENT_TYPE and SEGMENTID of the corresponding generic segment
  will be obtained from the RPL and will be populated into SAFS15 and
  SAFS16, respectively.

- If the BOROUGHCODE field of the type S address point and that of the
  Centerline segment identified by the generic SEGMENTID are equal,
  SAFS4 will be populated from the SEGMENT_SEQNUM attribute of the
  generic Centerline segment.

- If the BOROUGHCODE field of the type S address point and that of the
  generic Centerline segment are not equal, there is a borough boundary
  proto-segment having the given generic SEGMENTID. SAFS4 will be
  populated from the ALT_SEGMENT_SEQNUM field of that proto-segment's
  AltSegmentData entry.

3.  SAFS10 (LGC1), SAFS11 (LGC2), SAFS12 (LGC3), SAFS13 (LGC4) and
    SAFS14 (Pointer to BOE Preferred LGC): These fields will be
    populated as follows:

    a.  If the BOROUGHCODE value in the type S address point is
        identical to the borough code in the first byte of the B5SC
        field in any Segment_LGC entry for the given SEGMENTID, the type
        S address pertains to a geometry-represented Centerline segment.
        In that case, the LGC output fields will be populated as
        follows:

- SAFS10 will be populated with the LGC value contained in that
  Segment_LGC entry for the given SEGMENTID in which the
  PREFERRED_LGC_FLAG contains a 'Y'.

- If there are any other Segment_LGC entries for the given SEGMENTID,
  then as many as necessary of the output fields SAFS11, SAFS12 and
  SAFS13 will be populated in turn from the LGC values in those entries.
  For example, if there are two other entries, then SAFS11 and SAFS12
  will be populated with the respective values, and SAFS13 will be
  populated with blanks.

- SAFS14 will be set to the integer value corresponding to the output
  LGC field that was populated from that Segment_LGC entry in which
  BOE_PREFERRED_LGC_FLAG contained a 'Y'. For example, if SAF12 (LGC3)
  was populated from that entry, then SAFS14 will be populated with the
  value '3' (corresponding to LGC3).

b.  If the BOROUGHCODE value in the type S address point differs from
    the borough code in the first byte of the B5SC field in any
    Segment_LGC entry for the given SEGMENTID, the type S address
    pertains to a borough-boundary proto-segment. In that case, the ETL
    tool will perform the following processing:

- First, the ETL tool will verify that there is a such a proto-segment
  entry in AltSegmentData. The entry should satisfy the following
  conditions:

  - It contains the same SEGMENTID as the type S address point

  - ALT_SEGDATA_TYPE = 'B' (signifying a borough boundary proto-segment)

  - The BOROUGH field in the entry equals the BOROUGHCODE value in the
    type S address point

  - The B7SC_ACTUAL of the type S address point equals the concatenation
    of the fields B5SC and LGC1 of the proto-segment. (Note: this
    validates that the proto-segment belongs to the same street as the
    type S address and that the B7SC_ACTUAL of the address point is the
    preferred B7SC of the proto-segment.)

- If there is no proto-segment satisfying the above conditions, the ETL
  tool will report the case as an error. The message will indicate which
  of the above conditions has been found to be violated. An SAF record
  will not be written out.

- If there is such a proto-segment, the output fields SAFS10 (LGC1)
  through SAFS13 (LGC4) will be populated from the fields named LGC1
  through LGC4 in the proto-segment's AltSegmentData entry. Null values
  will be replaced with blanks. The field SAFS14 (the Pointer to BOE
  Preferred LGC) will be populated by copying the proto-segment's
  BOE_PREFERRED_LGC_FLAG.

4.  SAFS5 (SOS Indicator): If the AddressPoint field SOS_INDICATOR =
    '1', SAFS5 will be populated with 'L'. If SOS_INDICATOR = '2', SAFS5
    will be populated with 'R'. Otherwise, SAFS5 will be populated with
    a blank.

5.  SAFS7 (Basic House Number): Will be populated as follows:

- If the HYPHEN_TYPE attribute of the address point contains the value
  'R', the address point's HOUSE_NUMBER attribute contains a range of
  unhyphenated house numbers expressed in the form of the low house
  number of the range followed by a dash followed by the high house
  number of the range. (Note: there might or might not be spaces between
  the dash and the digits to the left and/or right of the dash. For
  example, the data in HOUSE_NUMBER might appear as '22-28' or as '22 --
  28'.) The ETL tool will populate SAFS7 with the low-address portion of
  the range only; the dash and the digits to the right of the dash will
  not be used. That value will then be modified as discussed below if
  the address point is in Edgewater Park.

- If the HYPHEN_TYPE attribute of the address point contains any value
  other than 'R', the ETL tool will populate SAFS7 with the value in the
  address point's HOUSE_NUMBER field without modification (except for
  the special Edgewater Park reformatting if required).

- If the address point is in Edgewater Park, the house number will be
  reformatted by adding an appropriate multiple of 10,000 to the house
  number. The method for determining whether an address is in Edgewater
  Park, and if so, the quantity that must be added to the house number,
  are described in Note 5 to Table 31.

6.  SAFS8 (House Number Suffix): Will be populated as follows:

- If the address point is not in Edgewater Park, SAFS8 will be populated
  from the address point's HOUSE_NUMBER_SUFFIX attribute, or with blanks
  if that is null.

- If the address point is in Edgewater Park, the house number suffix
  will be reformatted by dropping the Edgewater Park section letter, as
  described in Note 5 to Table 31. If there is a suffix value in
  addition to the section letter, it will be retained and populated into
  SAFS8 without the dash separating it from the section letter. If there
  is no such suffix value, SAFS8 will be populated with blanks.

## Type V Records

SAF Type V records are extracted from the AddressPoint feature class.
Output records are written for each address point for which the
SPECIAL_CONDITION attribute contains the value 'V'. The output records
are written into the generic SAFV file, the roadbed SAFV file or both,
depending on the SEGMENT_TYPE of the appurtenant Centerline segment, in
accordance with the rules in Table 26.

Table 35 contains a list of the fields in the SAF Type V output records.
The CSCL source of data for populating each field is indicated in the
last column in Table 35 and in the notes below the table.

Note that Type V records have the same layout and are written into the
same SAF output files as Type O records, but their CSCL data sources and
therefore the methods for populating their fields are different. The
spatial coordinate fields, SAFV19 and SAFV20, are populated with values
only in type V records.
