**[NOTES TO Table 35:]{.underline}**

1.  SAFV1 (Vanity Street Name): This field will be populated with the
    preferred name of the vanity street in Geosupport Sort Format. It
    will be converted from the LOOKUP_KEY field of the pertinent
    StreetName table entry. The table will be accessed using a composite
    key consisting of the address point field B7SC_VANITY combined with
    setting the StreetName field PRINCIPAL_FLAG to 'Y'. The contents of
    LOOKUP_KEY in that entry will be converted to Sort Format as
    described in Note 1 to Table 20.

> Note: the B7SC_VANITY field in a type V address point contains the
> preferred B7SC value of the vanity street name. Since the preferred
> B7SC of every roadbed segment is the B7SC that is assigned to the
> generic name of the given street (and DCP has stated its intention to
> continue adhering to that rule), the use of the B7SC_VANITY value to
> obtain the vanity street name as described above is valid even when
> the vanity street is a divided street and the record is being written
> into the generic output file.

2.  SAFV3 (Face Code of Actual Segment): Populated from the FACECODE
    field in the StreetName table entry for the principal name of the
    actual street. Obtained by accessing StreetName using a composite
    key consisting of the AddressPoint attribute B7SC_ACTUAL combined
    with setting the StreetName field PRINCIPAL_FLAG = 'Y'.

> Note: the B7SC_ACTUAL field in a type V address point contains the
> preferred B7SC value of the actual segment. Since the preferred B7SC
> of every roadbed segment is the one assigned to the generic name of
> the street (and DCP has stated its intention to continue adhering to
> that rule), the use of the B7SC_ACTUAL value to obtain the Face Code
> as described above is valid even when the appurtenant segment is a
> roadbed segment and the record is being written into the generic
> output file.

3.  SAFV4 (Sequence Number of Actual Segment), SAFV17 (Segment Type Code
    of Actual Segment) and SAFV18 (Segment ID of Actual Segment): These
    fields must be populated with the values from the "actual" segment,
    that is, the segment on which the vanity address is physically
    located.

> **ASSUMPTION**: The ETL tool has been designed under the assumption
> that no vanity addresses are located on proto-segments (which is
> tantamount to assuming that there are no vanity addresses located on
> borough boundaries). That is in fact the case as of the writing of
> this document. **In the future, if there should ever be any cases in
> which the "actual" segment of a vanity address is a proto-segment, the
> ETL tool will have to be modified accordingly.**
>
> When creating the output record for the generic output file, if the
> vanity address is located on a divided street, these fields must be
> populated with the values from the generic segment that corresponds to
> the roadbed segment identified in the address point.
>
> The ETL tool will obtain the values for populating SAFV4, SAFV17 and
> SAFV18 as follows:

a.  If the Centerline segment identified by the type V address point's
    SEGMENTID is a non-roadbed segment (SEGMENT_TYPE not = 'R')
    regardless of the output file, or if it is a roadbed segment and the
    output record is being written into the roadbed output file:

> SAFV4, SAFV17 and SAFV18 will be populated with the Sequence Number,
> Segment Type Code and Segment ID values from the Centerline segment's
> SEGMENT_SEQNUM, SEGMENT_TYPE and SEGMENTID attributes, respectively.

b.  If the Centerline segment identified by the type V address point's
    SEGMENTID is a roadbed segment, and the output record is being
    written into the generic output file:

> SAFV4, SAFV17 and SAFV18 will be populated with the Sequence Number,
> Segment Type Code and Segment ID values from the SEGMENT_SEQNUM,
> SEGMENT_TYPE and SEGMENTID attributes, respectively, of the generic
> segment that corresponds to the Centerline segment. The generic
> segment will be identified by searching the RPL in the usual manner.

4.  SAFV5 (SOS Indicator): If AddressPoint field SOS_INDICATOR = '1',
    SAFV5 will be populated with 'L'. If SOS_INDICATOR = '2', SAFV5 will
    be populated with 'R'. Otherwise, SAFV5 will be populated with a
    blank.

5.  SAFV7 (Low HN Basic), SAFV8 (Low HN Suffix), SAFV9 (High HN Basic)
    and SAFV10 (High HN Suffix): An address point feature might contain
    a single house number or it might contain low and high house numbers
    that define an address range. The house number information is stored
    in the address point's attribute data as follows:

- The attribute HYPHEN_TYPE indicates whether the address point house
  number data consist of a single house number or a range defined by low
  and high house numbers, as follows:

  - HYPHEN_TYPE = 'N' indicates a single unhyphenated house number.

  - HYPHEN_TYPE = 'R' indicates a range of unhyphenated house numbers.

  - HYPHEN_TYPE = 'Q' indicates a single Queens-style hyphenated house
    number.

  - HYPHEN_TYPE = 'U' indicates a single hyphenated house number in
    which the digits following the hyphen are a building unit
    identifier. (Note: As of this writing, there are no address points
    in the CSCL database for which HYPHEN_TYPE = 'U'.)

  - HYPHEN_TYPE = 'X' indicate a range of hyphenated house numbers.
    Other HYPHEN_TYPE values indicate a single house number.

- A single house number, whether hyphenated (HYPHEN_TYPE = Q or U) or
  unhyphenated (HYPHEN_TYPE = N), is stored in the attribute
  HOUSE_NUMBER (and in the attribute HOUSE_NUMBER_SUFFIX, if it has a
  suffix).

- The manner in which a range is stored depends on whether it is a range
  of unhyphenated or hyphenated house numbers:

  - If it is a range of unhyphenated house numbers (HYPHEN_TYPE = R),
    the low house number and high house number are stored together in a
    single character string in the HOUSE_NUMBER field with a dash
    separating them. Note the following:

    i.  One or more spaces might or might not separate the dash from the
        low and/or high house numbers. For example, the range might
        appear as 342-344 or it might appear as 342 - 344.

    ii. In the HYPHEN_TYPE = 'R' case, if there is a value in the
        HOUSE_NUMBER_SUFFIX field, it might apply to the low house
        number or to the high house number. Because of that ambiguity,
        the suffix will not be included in the output record.

  - If it is a range of Queens-style hyphenated house numbers
    (HYPHEN_TYPE = X), the low house number is stored in the
    HOUSE_NUMBER field and the high house number is stored in the
    HOUSE_NUMBER_RANGE field. If the low house number of the range has a
    suffix, it is stored in the HOUSE_NUMBER_SUFFIX field. If the high
    house number has a suffix, it is stored in the
    HOUSE_NUMBER_RANGE_SUFFIX field.

> The ETL tool will populate the output fields SAFV7, SAFV8, SAFV9 and
> SAFV10 as follows:

- If HYPHEN_TYPE = N, Q or U, the tool will populate SAFV7 from
  HOUSE_NUMBER, and will populate SAFV8 from HOUSE_NUMBER_SUFFIX if the
  latter contains a value, else with blanks. The tool will populate
  SAFV9 and SAFV10 with the same values that are populated into SAFV7
  and SAFV8, respectively.

- If HYPHEN_TYPE = R, the tool will populate SAFV7 with the digits in
  HOUSE_NUMBER that are to the left of the dash, and will populate SAFV9
  with the digits to the right of the dash. It will populate SAFV8 and
  SAFV10 with blanks.

- If HYPHEN_TYPE = X, the tool will populate SAFV7 from HOUSE_NUMBER,
  SAFV8 from HOUSE_NUMBER_SUFFIX if the latter contains a value, else
  with blanks, SAFV9 from HOUSE_NUMBER_RANGE, and SAFV10 from
  HOUSE_NUMBER_RANGE_SUFFIX if the latter contains a value, else with
  blanks.

> **ASSUMPTION**: The ETL tool has been designed under the assumption
> that no vanity addresses are located in Edgewater Park. (In fact, as
> of the writing of this document, no vanity addresses exist in the CSCL
> database in the entire borough of the Bronx). **In the future, if
> there should ever be any such cases, the ETL tool will have to be
> modified to reformat the basic house number and house number suffix
> fields in those cases as described in Notes 5 and 6 to Table 34.**

6.  SAFV13 (LGC2), SAFV14 (LGC3), SAFV15 (LGC4), SAFV16 (Pointer to BOE
    Preferred LGC): Any additional LGC values for vanity addresses
    beyond the one that is a component of B7SC_VANITY are stored in the
    AddressPointLGCs table, which can be accessed from the AddressPoint
    data by ADDRESSPOINTID via the relationship class
    AddressPointsHaveLGCs. The ETL Tool will insert an integer from 1 to
    4 into SAFV16 to identify the LGC output field that contains the LGC
    value obtained from the AddressPointLGCs entry in which BOE_LGC =
    'Y'. For example, if LGC2 (stored in SAFV13) contains the LGC value
    that was obtained from the aforementioned AddressPointLGCs entry,
    then SAFV16 will be set to '2'. If instead it is LGC3 (in SAFV14)
    that contains that LGC value, then SAFV16 will be set to '3'.
    However, if none of the AddressPointLGCs entries have BOE_LGC = 'Y,
    that signifies that the LGC obtained from the AddressPoint
    B7SC_VANITY attribute and loaded into LGC1 (in SAFV12) is the BOE
    Preferred LGC; in that case, set SAFV16 to '1'.

# SEDAT and Special SEDAT

The Split Election District Address Table (SEDAT) and the Special SEDAT
are extracted as two distinct output files that have identical record
layouts. They are extracted from the CSCL SEDAT and SpecialSEDAT tables,
respectively. One output record is written for each entry in those
tables.

Entries in the CSCL SEDAT table are associated with Centerline segments.
It is possible for multiple SEDAT entries to be associated with one
Centerline segment. There is a relationship class called
CenterlinesToSEDAT that links SEDAT table entries and Centerline
segments by SEGMENTID.

Entries in the CSCL SPECIALSEDAT table are associated with SAF records,
which are stored in the CSCL database as SAF entries in the
AltSegmentData table or as point features in the AddressPoint or
CommonPlace feature classes, depending on the SAF record type.

## SEDAT

The ETL tool writes one record into the SEDAT output file for each entry
in the CSCL SEDAT table. Table 36 contains a layout of the SEDAT output
file. The last column in the table indicates the CSCL source of data for
populating each field.

[]{#_Ref222720134 .anchor}Table 36 -- SEDAT Output File

  ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **FIC**    **Field**              **Len**   **Frm**   **To** **CSCL Source of data**
  ---------- -------------------- --------- --------- -------- --------------------------
  SEDAT1     LION Key                    10         1       10 SEDAT table LIONKEY field

  SEDAT2     Parity of Address            1        11       11 SEDAT table PARITY field
             Range                                             

  SEDAT3     Street Name                 32        12       43 See Note 1

  SEDAT4     Side of Street               1        44       44 See Note 2

  SEDAT5     Low House Number             7        45       51 SEDAT table LOWADDRESS
                                                               field

  SEDAT6     Low House Number             8        52       59 SEDAT table
             Suffix                                            LOW_ADDR_SUFFIX field

  SEDAT7     High House Number            7        60       66 SEDAT table HIGHADDRESS
                                                               field

  SEDAT8     High House Number            8        67       74 SEDAT table
             Suffix                                            HIGH_ADDR_SUFFIX field

  SEDAT9     Election District            3        75       77 SEDAT table
                                                               ELECTION_DISTRICT field

  SEDAT10    Assembly District            2        78       79 SEDAT table
                                                               ASSEMBLY_DISTRICT field

  SEDAT11    B7SC                         8        80       87 See Note 3
  ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**[NOTES TO Table 36]{.underline}:**

1.  SEDAT3 (Street Name): This field will be populated after output
    field SEDAT11 has been populated (see Note 2 below). The Preferred
    B7SC value populated into SEDAT11 will be used in a composite key
    with PRINCIPAL_FLAG = 'Y' in the usual manner to access the entry in
    the StreetName table for the principal name of the Preferred LGC.
    SEDAT3 will then be populated with the principal preferred street
    name in Geosupport-normalized format from the LOOKUP_KEY field in
    that entry.

> Note that the 42-byte STREET field in the CSCL SEDAT table is not
> being used to populate the output record. **RECOMMENDATION**: The
> STREET field in the CSCL SEDAT table should be dropped from the CSCL
> data model. Beyond the fact that this field has an erroneous length of
> 42 bytes, its presence in this table is redundant and violates the
> general CSCL approach that street names will only be stored in one
> place in the CSCL database, in the StreetName table.

2.  SEDAT4 (Side of Street). Populate from the CSCL SEDAT Table field
    SIDE as follows:

- If SIDE = '1', populate SEDAT4 with the value 'L'

- If SIDE = '2', populate SEDAT4 with 'R'

3.  SEDAT11 (B7SC): This field will be populated with the Preferred B7SC
    of the given segment. It will be obtained in the usual manner by
    accessing the entry for the Preferred LGC in the Segment_LGC table
    via the composite key consisting of the SEGMENTID from the CSCL
    SEDAT entry and the PREFERRED_LGC_FLAG = 'Y'. The concatenation of
    the two fields B5SC and LGC from the given table entry is the
    desired Preferred LGC value.

> In performing the SEDAT11 processing, the ETL tool must handle the
> case of borough boundary coincident segments. In that case, street
> codes from two boroughs relate to the same SEGMENTID. The ETL tool
> will recognize this case by the fact that there will be two entries in
> Segment_LGC for the same SEGMENTID that have the PREFERRED_LGC_FLAG
> set to 'Y'. The one that the ETL tool will use is the one whose
> borough code (the first byte of the B5SC) is the same as that of the
> given SEDAT entry (the first byte of the LIONKEY field).
>
> Note that the 5-byte STREETCODE field in the CSCL SEDAT table is not
> being used to populate the output record, since the Segment_LGC table
> has to be accessed anyway to obtain the Preferred LGC with which to
> form the Preferred B7SC. **RECOMMENDATION**: The STREETCODE field in
> the CSCL SEDAT table appears superfluous and redundant, and should be
> dropped from the CSCL data model.

## Special SEDAT

Table 37 contains a layout of the Special SEDAT output file and the CSCL
source of data for each field. The last column in the table and the
notes following the table indicate the CSCL source of data for
populating each field.

[]{#_Ref222720174 .anchor}Table 37 -- Special SEDAT Output File

  ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

                                                               field

  SEDAT2     Parity of Address            1        11       11 SPECIALSEDAT table PARITY
             Range                                             field

  SEDAT3     Street Name                 32        12       43 See Note 1

  SEDAT4     Side of Street               1        44       44 See Note 2

  SEDAT5     Low House Number             7        45       51 SPECIALSEDAT table

             Suffix                                            LOW_ADDR_SUFFIX field

**[NOTES TO Table 37]{.underline}:**

1.  SEDAT3 (Street Name): This field will be populated with the
    principal street name of the B7SC value that is stored in the
    SpecialSEDAT table entry. The ETL tool will attempt to obtain the
    name from the StreetName table field LOOKUP_KEY by accessing
    StreetName via a composite key consisting of the B7SC value combined
    with the StreetName field PRINCIPAL_FLAG = 'Y'. If that does not
    succeed, the ETL tool will attempt to obtain the name from the
    LOOKUP_KEY field in the principal entry for the B7SC value in the
    FeatureName table. If that fails as well, the ETL tool will treat
    the case as an error; it will issue an error message and will not
    write an output record.

2.  SEDAT4 (Side of Street). Populate from the CSCL SpecialSEDAT Table
    field SIDE as follows:

- If SIDE = '1', populate SEDAT4 with the value 'L'

- If SIDE = '2', populate SEDAT4 with 'R'

# Roadbed Pointer List

[]{.mark}Table 38 contains a layout of the Roadbed Pointer List (RPL)
output file. The ETL tool writes one output record for every entry in
the CSCL RoadbedPointerList table. Each record represents one roadbed
segment associated with a given generic segment.

A single citywide RPL output file is produced. The output records are
ordered as follows:

- The records containing each generic SEGMENTID, that is, each distinct
  value in the output field RPL1, will occur consecutively.

- The set of records for a given generic SEGMENTID will be ordered based
  on the value of the CSCL RoadbedPointerList field
  ROADBED_POSITION_CODE and on a spatial determination of the positions
  of the inner roadbed segments, as follows:

  - The field ROADBED_POSITION_CODE in each CSCL RoadbedPointerList
    entry contains one of the values 'L', 'R' or 'I', indicating that
    the given entry represents the outermost road segment on the left
    side of the generic segment, the right outermost roadbed segment, or
    an inner roadbed segment, respectively. There will always be exactly
    one 'L' entry and one 'R' entry. There can be any number of 'I'
    entries, including none.

  - To order the output records properly, it is necessary to determine
    which side of the generic segment each inner roadbed segment is on,
    and what their relative positions are. The ETL tool will use spatial
    methods to do so. The spatial methodology will make use of the
    imaginary line perpendicular to the generic segment through its
    midpoint. The ETL tool will determine the intersections of that line
    with the imaginary infinite extensions of the inner roadbed
    segments. The order in which those intersections occur along the
    perpendicular line corresponds to the relative positions of the
    inner roadbed segments. The possibility that any of the roadbed
    segments can be a polyline with intermediate vertices must be taken
    into consideration.

  - The first record that the ETL tool will write out for the given
    generic segment will be the one generated from the entry for the
    right outermost roadbed segment, that is, the one whose
    ROADBED_POSITION_CODE field contains the value 'R'.

  - The next record(s) that the ETL tool will write out will be the
    right inner roadbed segments, ordered in sequence from the one
    closest to the right outermost roadbed segment to the one closest to
    the generic segment.

  - The next record that the ETL tool will write out will be the one
    generated from the entry for the left outermost roadbed segment.

  - Finally, the ETL tool will write out the records for the left inner
    roadbed segments, ordered in sequence from the one closest to the
    left outermost roadbed segment to the one closest to the generic
    segment.

[]{#_Ref222720217 .anchor}Table 38 -- Roadbed Pointer List Output File

  ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **FIC**   **Field**          **Len**   **Frm**   **To** **Format**   **CSCL Source Field**
  --------- ---------------- --------- --------- -------- ------------ -------------------------------
  RPL1      Generic                  7         1        7 RJZF         RoadbedPointerList
            SEGMENTID                                                  GENERIC_SEGMENTID field

  RPL2      Segment Type of          1         8        8              See Note 1
            Generic Segment                                            

  RPL3      Roadbed                  7         9       15 RJZF         RoadbedPointerList
            SEGMENTID                                                  ROADBED_SEGMENTID field

            Filler                   1        16       16              Populate with blank

  RPL4      Roadbed Position         1        17       17              RoadbedPointerList
            Code                                                       ROADBED_POSITION_CODE field

            Filler                   1        18       18              Populate with blank

  RPL5      Node                     1        19       19              RoadbedPointerList
            Correspondence                                             NODE_CORRESPONDENCE_IND field
            Indicator                                                  

            Filler                   3        20       22              Populate with blanks

  RPL6      From Node Level          1        23       23              RoadbedPointerList
            Code of                                                    FROM_NODE_LEVEL_COINCIDENT_RB
            Coincident                                                 field
            Roadbed Segment                                            
            (if any)                                                   

            Filler                   3        24       26              Populate with blanks

  RPL7      To Node Level            1        27       27              RoadbedPointerList
            Code of                                                    TO_NODE_LEVEL_COINCIDENT_RB
            Coincident                                                 field
            Roadbed Segment                                            
            (if any)                                                   

            Filler                   1        28       28              Populate with blank

  RPL8      From NODEID of           7        29       35 RJZF         See Note 2
            Roadbed Segment                                            

            Filler                   1        36       36              Populate with blank

  RPL9      From NODEID of           7        37       43 RJZF         See Note 2
            Generic Segment                                            

            Filler                   1        44       44              Populate with blank

  RPL10     To NODEID of             7        45       51 RJZF         See Note 2
            Roadbed Segment                                            

            Filler                   1        52       52              Populate with blank

  RPL11     To NODEID of             7        53       59 RJZF         See Note 2
            Generic Segment                                            
  ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**[NOTES TO []{.mark}Table 38]{.underline}:**

1.  RPL2 (Segment Type of Generic Segment): This field will be populated
    from the SEGMENT_TYPE attribute field of the appurtenant Centerline
    segment, accessed by the GENERIC_SEGMENTID value in the given
    RoadbedPointerList table entry. The ETL tool will **ASSUME**,
    without validating it, that this is the SEGMENTID of a valid generic
    segment in Centerline, and therefore that its SEGMENT_TYPE contains
    one of the values 'B' or 'G'.

2.  RPL8 (From NODEID of Roadbed Segment), RPL9 (From NODEID of Generic
    Segment), RPL10 (To NODEID of Roadbed Segment), RPL11 (To NODEID of
    Generic Segment): These fields will be populated as follows. The
    respective SEGMENTID will be used to access the given segment (the
    generic or roadbed segment). For each endpoint of the segment, the
    ETL tool will perform a spatial query against the Node feature class
    to obtain that endpoint's NODEID, if any, using standard ESRI
    functionality. The tool will populate the respective NODEID output
    field accordingly. If there is no node at a segment endpoint, the
    ETL tool will populate that output field with blanks, and will
    report the case as an error.

# District Boundary Geodatabase

The ETL tool creates an ESRI-formatted file geodatabase (as opposed to a
personal geodatabase) of district boundary polygons. It will contain
approximately two dozen polygon feature classes for the various types of
district boundaries.

Appendix D contains a schema for the district boundary geodatabase
provided by DCP, identified as Version 4 and dated January 29, 2009.

For many of the district types, the polygon geometry is extracted
directly from the CSCL geodatabase, which contains corresponding polygon
feature classes. However, for some of the district types, the ETL tool
creates two sets of the district polygons, one set with the polygon
geometry unmodified from how they are stored in the CSCL database, and
one set with the polygons clipped to the shoreline.

Minor Census Economic Areas (MCEAs) are a required type of output
district not modeled by polygon geometry in the CSCL database. Instead,
there is an MCEA attribute in the CensusTract2000 feature class. The ETL
tool generates MCEA polygons by dissolving CensusTract2000 polygons
based on the MCEA attribute and clipping the results to the shoreline.
(It is not required to produce a water-blocks-included version of MCEA.)

The attributes required for most of the polygon feature classes are
listed in Appendix D. Their field names are self-explanatory, and they
have corresponding fields in the CSCL database that will serve as the
data sources. For some of the polygon feature classes, no attribute
information is provided in DCP's documentation in Appendix D. Those are
Urban Renewal Area, Business Improvement District, Empire Zone, Historic
District, Zip Code and the 2010 Census districts. It is **assumed** that
the only attribute fields they require (in addition to the mandatory
ESRI OBJECTID and SHAPE fields) are the respective district identifiers,
as defined in the CSCL data model.

The ETL tool generates a temporary set of shoreline polygons that it
uses for clipping. It generates them by dissolving Atomic Polygons (APs)
based on the WATER_FLAG attribute. APs for which WATER_FLAG = '2'
(non-water) or '3' (pier) are dissolved to generate the shoreline
polygons for use in clipping.

Table 39 lists the polygon feature classes to be included in the output
district boundary geodatabase. The first column contains the feature
class name from DCP's document in Appendix D. Feature class names ending
in "wi" (which stands for "water blocks included" are the unclipped
versions of district types that will also be extracted clipped to the
shoreline. In those cases, the same feature class name but without the
"wi" ending is the name of the same district type clipped to the
shoreline.

District types for which no "wi" version is listed in Table 39 are
extracted exactly as stored in the CSCL database unless otherwise noted
in the "Descriptions" column in the table. (Note: Although Appendix D
does not list a "wi" file for Community District, clipped and unclipped
versions of this district type will be extracted, pursuant to DCP
instructions.)

[The template of District boundary Geo-database is at
C:\\NDPS\\MyFiles\\Geo-support-modernization\\Templates\\District
Boundary.gdb.]{.mark}

(\*) These output district types contain an 11-byte string field called
BCTCB2000. These fields will be populated from the first 11 bytes of the
12-byte CensusBlock2000 attribute field BCTCB. (The last byte of the
latter is the Census Block Suffix and will not be propagated to the
output record.)

(\*\*) School District 10 covers portions of two borough. A separate
nysd polygon will be written out for the portion of this school district
in each borough. The two borough-specific polygons can be generated by
intersecting the CSCL polygon for School District 10 with each borough
polygon. Both output polygons will have the same polygon ID.

~~(\*\*\*) These district types are not yet implemented. They are not to
be extracted until they have been implemented in CSCL.~~

[Note:]{.mark}

1.  [The source feature class "CENSUSBLOCK2010 doesn't have field of
    "boroName". The attribute of BoroName will be got from field
    "BoroCode".]{.mark}

> [If boroCode == "1", its BoroName =="Manhattan"]{.mark}
>
> [If boroCode == "2", its BoroName =="Bronx"]{.mark}
>
> [If boroCode == "3", its BoroName =="Brooklyn"]{.mark}
>
> [If boroCode == "4", its BoroName =="Queens"]{.mark}
>
> [If boroCode == "5", its BoroName =="Staten Island"]{.mark}
>
> [The attributes of "CB2010" are copied from field of "CB" of source
> feature class "CENSUSBLOCK2010. The attributes of "CT2010" are copied
> from field of "CT" of source feature class. The field "BCTCB2010" are
> copied from field of "BCTCB" of source feature class
> "CENSUSBLOCK2010.]{.mark}

2.  [The NYCB2020 and NYCB2020wi. Here are the rules to populate the
    field of GEOID:]{.mark}

> [If the BoroCode =="1" , GEOID = "36061" + BCTCB(Right 10
> digit)]{.mark}
>
> [If the BoroCode =="2" , GEOID = "36005" + BCTCB(Right 10
> digit)]{.mark}
>
> [If the BoroCode =="3" , GEOID = "36047" + BCTCB(Right 10
> digit)]{.mark}
>
> [If the BoroCode =="4" , GEOID = "36081" + BCTCB(Right 10
> digit)]{.mark}
>
> [If the BoroCode =="5" , GEOID = "36085" + BCTCB(Right 10
> digit)]{.mark}

3.  [The source feature class for NyNTA2020 is CSCL.NTA2020. It only has
    "NEIGHBORHOOD_CODE" field. The rest of attributes need special
    process to retrieve them from other FC or table in CSCL.]{.mark}

> [The field of "BoroCode", "BoroName" and "CountyFIPS" are retrieved
> from CSCL.borough" feature class by using the centroid point of
> NTA2020 polygon to find the borough polygon containing the centroid
> point and populate out the corresponding attributes from it.]{.mark}
>
> [The field "NTA2020" is copied from "Neighborhood_code" in
> CSCL.NTA2020.]{.mark}
>
> [The field "NTAName", "NTAAbbrev", "NTAType" are retrieved from CSCL
> table of "NTAEquiv2020". The three attribute will be populated from
> fields of "NTA_NAME","NTA_ABBREV" "NTA_TYPE" respectively from table
> "NTAEquiv2020" if the "Neighborhood_code" in NTA2020 is equal to
> NTA_Code" of CSCL. NTAEquiv2020 table.]{.mark}
>
> [The field "CDTA2020", "CDTAName" are retrieved from CSCL.CDTA2020 and
> CSCL.CDTAEquiv2020 respectively. Generate a centroid of the polygon
> and find the record of CSCL.CDTA2020 that contains the centroid. The
> found record od CDTA2020's CDTA_Code will be copied to field of
> "CDTA2020" of NTA2020. The found CDTA_code will be used to find the
> corresponding "CDTA_name" in CSCL.CDTAEquiv2020 table. The found
> "CDTA_name" will be copied to the field of "CDTAName" of
> NTA2020.]{.mark}

4.  [Nynta2010]{.mark}

> [The attributes of "BoroCode", "BoroName" and "CountyFIPS" are
> retrieved from CSCL.borough" feature class by using the centroid point
> of NTA2010 polygon to find the borough polygon containing the centroid
> point and populate out the corresponding attributes from it]{.mark}.
>
> [NTACode attribute will be copied from "Neighborhood_code" in
> "Neighborhood" feature class.]{.mark}
>
> [NTAName attribute will be retrieved from the attribute of
> "Neighborhood_name" in "NEIGHBORHOODPUMACODES" table when the
> "NTACode" of Nynta2010 equals to "Neighborhood_code" of
> "NEIGHBORHOODPUMACODES" table.]{.mark}

5.  [Nycdta2020]{.mark}

> [The source feature class for Nycdta2020 is CSCL.CDTA2020.The
> attributes of "BoroCode", "BoroName" and "CountyFIPS" are retrieved
> from CSCL.borough" feature class by using the centroid point of
> CDTA2020 polygon to find the borough polygon containing the centroid
> point and populate out the corresponding attributes from it]{.mark}.
>
> [Attribute of "CDTA2020" is copied from "CDTA_code" in
> CSCL.CDTA2020.]{.mark}
>
> [Attribute of "CDTAName" is retrieved from attribute of "CDTA_Name" in
> table of CDTAEquiv2020 when CDTA_code of CDTA202 equals to the
> CDTA_code of CDTAEquiv2020.]{.mark}
>
> [Attribute of "CDTAType" is retrieved from attribute of "CDTA_Type" in
> table of "CDTAEquiv2020" when "CDTA_code" of "CSCL.CDTA2020" equals to
> the "CDTA_code" of "CDTAEquiv2020".]{.mark}

6.  [Nyct2020]{.mark}

> [The source feature class for Nyct2020 is
> "CSCL.CENSUSTRACT2020".]{.mark}
>
> [Boro_name is got from CSCL.borough in the same way as
> nycdta2020.]{.mark}
>
> [CT2020 is]{.mark} [copied from attribute of "CT" in the source
> feature class.]{.mark}
>
> [BoroCT2020]{.mark} [is copied from attribute of "BoroCT" in the
> source feature class.]{.mark}
>
> [CDEligibil is copied from attribute of "CD_Eligibility" in the source
> feature class.]{.mark}
>
> [NTA2020 is copied from attribute of "Neighborhood_Code" in the source
> feature class.]{.mark}
>
> [CDTA2020 is copied from attribute of "CDTA_Code" in the source
> feature class.]{.mark}
>
> [PUMA is copied from attribute of "PUMA" in the source feature
> class.]{.mark}
>
> [??NTAName is retrieved from NTA_NAME in NTAEquiv2020 table when
> NTA_Code in NTAEquiv2020 equals NTA2020 in NYCT2020]{.mark}
>
> [??CDTAName is retrieved from CDTA_Name in CDTAEquiv2020 table when
> the CDTA2020 equals CDTA_code in CDTAEquiv2020 table.]{.mark}
>
> [GEOID is generated by replace the borough code in field of
> "BoroCT2020" with FIPS state and county code. It is total 11
> digits.]{.mark}

  --------------------------------------------------
  [Boro code]{.mark}        [State and county
                            FIPS]{.mark}
  ------------------------- ------------------------
  [1]{.mark}                [36061]{.mark}

  [2]{.mark}                [36005]{.mark}

  [3]{.mark}                [36047]{.mark}

  [4]{.mark}                [36081]{.mark}

  [5]{.mark}                [36085]{.mark}
  --------------------------------------------------

# Appendix A Bytes of the Big Apple™ LION in ESRI Format

The extraction of the ESRI LION is discussed in Section 2.7 and its
sub-sections. This appendix contains a copy of an updated document on
the ESRI LION provided by the Department of City Planning on April 20,
2009 and identified as V4. The document was produced using the ESRI
ARCGIS Diagrammer tool.

# Appendix C Bytes LION: Populating "Empty" FieldS

This appendix contains a DCP-supplied table indicating how to populate
fields in the ESRI LION and the MapInfo LION when the field is "empty"
(devoid of meaningful contents). For fields for which the last column
does not contain a notation, a meaningful value is mandatory.

+-------------+--------+--------+-----------+----------------------------+
| **Field**   | **ESRI | **ESRI | **MapInfo | **When no value...**       |
|             | GDB    | Len**  | Format**  |                            |
|             | Type** |        |           |                            |
+=============+:======:+:======:+:=========:+============================+
|             |        |        |           |                            |
+-------------+--------+--------+-----------+----------------------------+
| OBJECTID    | Object | 4      |           |                            |
|             | ID     |        |           |                            |
+-------------+--------+--------+-----------+----------------------------+
| SHAPE       | Line   |        |           |                            |
+-------------+--------+--------+-----------+----------------------------+
| Street      | Text   | 32     | Char(32)  |                            |
+-------------+--------+--------+-----------+----------------------------+
| FeatureTyp  | Text   | 1      | Char(1)   |                            |
+-------------+--------+--------+-----------+----------------------------+
| SegmentTyp  | Text   | 1      | Char(1)   |                            |
+-------------+--------+--------+-----------+----------------------------+
| IncExFlag   | Text   | 1      | Char(1)   | \" \" (a blank)            |

| RB_Layer    | Text   | 1      | Char(1)   |                            |

| MH_RI_Flag  | Text   | 1      | Char(1)   | \" \" (a blank)            |
+-------------+--------+--------+-----------+----------------------------+
| XFrom       | Long   | 4      | Integer   |                            |
+-------------+--------+--------+-----------+----------------------------+
| YFrom       | Long   | 4      | Integer   |                            |
+-------------+--------+--------+-----------+----------------------------+
| XTo         | Long   | 4      | Integer   |                            |
+-------------+--------+--------+-----------+----------------------------+
| YTo         | Long   | 4      | Integer   |                            |
+-------------+--------+--------+-----------+----------------------------+
| ArcCenterX  | Long   | 4      | Integer   | 0 (Zero)                   |
+-------------+--------+--------+-----------+----------------------------+
| ArcCenterY  | Long   | 4      | Integer   | 0 (Zero)                   |
+-------------+--------+--------+-----------+----------------------------+
| CurveFlag   | Text   | 1      | Char(1)   | \" \" (a blank)            |
+-------------+--------+--------+-----------+----------------------------+
| Radius      | Long   | 4      | Integer   | 0 (Zero)                   |
+-------------+--------+--------+-----------+----------------------------+
| NodeIDFrom  | Text   | 7      | Char(7)   |                            |
+-------------+--------+--------+-----------+----------------------------+
| NodeIDTo    | Text   | 7      | Char(7)   |                            |
+-------------+--------+--------+-----------+----------------------------+
| NodeLevelF  | Text   | 1      | Char(1)   |                            |
+-------------+--------+--------+-----------+----------------------------+
| NodeLevelT  | Text   | 1      | Char(1)   |                            |
+-------------+--------+--------+-----------+----------------------------+
| ConParity   | Text   | 1      | Char(1)   | \" \" (a blank)            |
+-------------+--------+--------+-----------+----------------------------+
| Twisted     | Text   | 1      | Char(1)   | \" \" (a blank)            |

#  Appendix D District Boundary Geodatabase

The extraction of an ESRI file geodatabase of district boundaries is
discussed in Chapter 10. This appendix contains a copy of a DCP document
that lists the feature classes, attributes, and spatial references for
that geodatabase. This is Version 4 of this DCP document, dated January
29, 2009. It was produced using the ESRI ARCGIS Diagrammer tool. (Note
that the DCP document is missing information on attribute fields
required for the district types listed under "Additional CSCL Polygons"
in the list of object classes. It is assumed that the only attribute
information required is the district identifiers.)

([Also see the template of Byte District boundary for the latest
version:]{.mark}

[C:\\NDPS\\MyFiles\\Geo-support-modernization\\Templates\\District
Boundary.gdb)]{.mark}

  -----------------------------------------------------------------------
  [ArcGIS Diagrammer]{.underline}
  -----------------------------------------------------------------------

ArcGIS Diagrammer is prototype application and is not supported by ESRI.
The commands assoicated with this application and the output generated
by those commands are not to be used in a production environment. ESRI
is not reponsible for errors, ommission or any damages resulting from
the use of application and associated output. Use of this application is
conditional on the acceptance of this statement.

# Appendix E File Naming Requirements

This appendix contains a table of ETL output file naming requirements
provided by DCP on 5/19/2009 and identified as Version 3.

+-----------------+--------------------+-------------------------------+
| **File Name**   | **Naming           | **Comment**                   |
|                 | Convention**       |                               |
+-----------------+--------------------+-------------------------------+
|                 |                    |                               |
+-----------------+--------------------+-------------------------------+
| LION            | \*lion.dat         | \*=Manhattan, Bronx,          |
|                 |                    | Brooklyn, Queens, or          |
|                 |                    | StatenIsland                  |
+-----------------+--------------------+-------------------------------+
| ThinED          | thinED.dat         | not by borough                |
+-----------------+--------------------+-------------------------------+
| Face Code       | \*Face.txt         | \*=Manhattan, Bronx,          |
|                 |                    | Brooklyn, Queens, or          |
|                 |                    | StatenIsland                  |
+-----------------+--------------------+-------------------------------+
| LDF             | LDFBASE.dat        |                               |
+-----------------+--------------------+-------------------------------+
| LDF header file | LDFHEADER.dat      |                               |
+-----------------+--------------------+-------------------------------+
| RPL             | RPL.txt            |                               |
+-----------------+--------------------+-------------------------------+
| ThinFire        | \*thinfire.txt     | \*=Manhattan, Bronx,          |
|                 |                    | Brooklyn, Queens, or          |
|                 |                    | StatenIsland                  |
+-----------------+--------------------+-------------------------------+
| SAF             | Generic\*.txt      | \*=**ABCEGPNX**,**D**,**OV**, |
|                 |                    | or **S**                      |
|                 +--------------------+-------------------------------+
|                 | Roadbed\*.txt      | \*=**ABCEGPNX**,**D**,**OV**, |
|                 |                    | or **S**                      |
|                 +--------------------+-------------------------------+
|                 | Intersection.txt   |                               |
+-----------------+--------------------+-------------------------------+
| Sedat           | Sedat.txt          | The ETL file needed for       |
|                 |                    | processing is a single Sedat  |
|                 |                    | file that includes Sedat      |
|                 |                    | records only                  |
+-----------------+--------------------+-------------------------------+
| Special Sedat   | specialSEDAT.txt   | The ETL file needed for       |
|                 |                    | processing is a single        |
|                 |                    | special sedat file that       |
|                 |                    | includes special Sedat        |
|                 |                    | records only                  |
+-----------------+--------------------+-------------------------------+
| Split School    | N/A                | There no longer is a split    |
|                 |                    | school file                   |
+-----------------+--------------------+-------------------------------+
| ThinTract       | \*thintract.dat    | \*=Manhattan, Bronx,          |
|                 |                    | Brooklyn, Queens, or          |
|                 |                    | StatenIsland                  |
+-----------------+--------------------+-------------------------------+
| ThinLION        | \*thinlion.dat     | \*=Manhattan, Bronx,          |
|                 |                    | Brooklyn, Queens, or          |
|                 |                    | StatenIsland                  |
+-----------------+--------------------+-------------------------------+
| SND             | SND.txt            |                               |
+-----------------+--------------------+-------------------------------+
| Exception Table | Exception.txt      |                               |
+-----------------+--------------------+-------------------------------+
| Universal Table | Universal.txt      |                               |
+-----------------+--------------------+-------------------------------+
| Enders Table    | Enders.txt         |                               |
+-----------------+--------------------+-------------------------------+
| Last Word Table | LastWord.txt       |                               |
+-----------------+--------------------+-------------------------------+
|                 |                    |                               |
+-----------------+--------------------+-------------------------------+
| BYTES LION      | v\*\_LION          | \*=cycle name (24A)           |
| (ESRI fgdb)     |                    | v24A_LION.gdb                 |
+-----------------+--------------------+-------------------------------+
| ~~BYTES LION    | ~~NYLION1.mif and  |                               |
| (MapInfo)~~     | NYLION2.mif~~      |                               |
+-----------------+--------------------+-------------------------------+
| BYTES Districts | v\*\_DISTRICTS     | \*= cycle name (24A)          |
| (ESRI fgdb)     | Feature Class      | v24A_DISTRICTS (assume that a |
|                 | names as per the   | user would have to enter the  |
|                 | ArcGIS diagrammer  | cycle information when        |
|                 | ETL document       | running the extract). The     |
|                 |                    | ArcGIS Team has requested one |
|                 |                    | fgdb containing all the       |
|                 |                    | districts for our internal    |
|                 |                    | SDE. They will break out into |
|                 |                    | Shapefile format for the      |
|                 |                    | website)                      |
+=================+====================+===============================+

[^1]: As part of Phase 3 of the CSCL project, various batch validation
    programs will be developed separately from the ETL tool. Many of
    them will be run at ETL time, either before or after the ETL tool is
    run, depending on whether the particular validation needs to process
    any ETL output files or only the CSCL database. These "stand-alone"
    batch validation programs are not further discussed in this
    document.

[^2]: This design assumes that there are no Type D SAF records that
    pertain to borough boundary segments, as is true as of this writing.
    It is not expected that there will ever be any new duplicate
    addresses. However, if there should be a Type D record in the future
    that does pertain to a borough boundary segment, the B5SC value for
    the output SAF record would have to be obtained from either the
    geometry-based segment or the proto-segment, whichever has the same
    Borough Code as the given AltSegmentData SAF Type D or F entry. That
    would require an ETL program modification.
